# MEMORY - tatara-operator

- 2026-07-19 (fix/unowned-mr-stub-unpark-deadlock) Interrupted-mint deadlock closed: a stub MergeRequest CR with NO controller owner made BOTH recovery paths dead-end (pending_events.go required own.ControllerOwner to route a human comment to the task; reconcileMRBindingBackstop's repair only ran on not-yet-parked tasks). Fix: reconcileParkedBindingRepair runs repairSourceBinding for tasks parked awaiting-human by the binding watchdog (predicate: parkedFromStage set + Source.Number>0 + zero mr/issue refs - other awaiting-human parks untouched) and unparks via stage.UnparkTargetForBindingRepair, the ONE documented exception where the unpark target derives from status.parkedFromStage (guarded by Legal(parked, from), applied through EnterStage so kind guards hold). Webhook fallback: unowned mirror comments resolve the task by the intake natural key (deterministic Get, validated against Spec.Source.Number; repo not comparable - TaskSource has no repo field) and only deliver to live tasks (parked included; failed/rejected/delivered/deleting excluded).
- 2026-07-19 (fix/384-events-k8s-io-rbac, issue #384) **Every Kubernetes Event 403-dropped: recorder writes to events.k8s.io/v1, RBAC granted events only in core group "".** The controllers construct the modern `events.k8s.io/v1` sink (`mgr.GetEventRecorder` -> `k8s.io/client-go/tools/events`, `repository_controller.go:20,80,782`, emits at `:669`), but both the chart Role (`rbac.yaml`) and the `+kubebuilder:rbac` markers granted `events` only in the legacy core group `""`. client-go's broadcaster got a 403 on every Event create and, per its non-retry-on-rejection policy, logged `Server rejected event (will not retry!)` and dropped it (9 in 1h, chronic). Picked fix A (grant the missing group) over B (downgrade recorder to the deprecated core-group `tools/record`): added `apiGroups: ["events.k8s.io"]` events `create;patch` to the chart Role + a mirroring marker on both controllers, and taught `hack/check-rbac-drift.sh`'s KNOWN_NAMESPACED the `events.k8s.io|events` pair. **KEPT** the core `""` events grant (leader-election and other legacy-recorder emitters may still use it; removing it is unproven scope). **Root-cause insight for the regression check:** the drift guard only proves chart<->markers PARITY, and #384 shipped with perfect parity (both core-group-only, both wrong) - a parity check can never catch a both-sides-wrong bug. So added a REQUIRED_ROLE_PAIRS guard in the same script that independently asserts `events.k8s.io|events` is present in the rendered namespaced Role (any verb), tying RBAC to the recorder the operator actually constructs. Scope: RBAC class ONLY (co-firing `ingest failed` -> tatara-memory#79/#80; MR-mint 422 + interrupted-mint park -> #379/#325, unchanged here). Gate green (`build`/`vet`/`lint`/`test` + drift check 169 tuples). semver:patch.
- 2026-07-19: objbudget Fit* (MergeRequest/Issue/Task) retry NotFound with bounded backoff (~3s) - informer cache lag right after Create broke PR 388's mint; persistent NotFound still surfaces after retries.
- 2026-07-19: advanceAfterReview now takes a fresh just-settled MR to overlay and lists owned MRs via StageDriver.APIReader (uncached): overlay alone cannot heal sibling-MR staleness, and re-attempting advance on nil pendingReview is unsafe (pre-outcome MRs also have nil pending). Reconciled with #390's level-triggered re-drive: this hardens the PRIMARY edge-triggered advance (#390 left StageDriver's list cached, so nearly every drain would have leaned on the 30s backstop); dropped our separate pre-park retryStalledHandoff and the 15s MR requeue (with DrainPendingReview's reviewOwed bool) as redundant with reconcileClocks' every-reconcile live re-drive.
- 2026-07-19: reconcileMRBindingBackstop attempts repairSourceBinding (intake's repairMRBinding/repairIssueBinding) before parking awaiting-human; snapshot rebuilt from Task.Spec.Source only (stub CR, cadence refreshes rest); a mint interrupted between ownMergeRequest and stampMintStatus still parks (repair never touches an owned CR) - recoverable via normal awaiting-human unpark.
- 2026-07-19: handoff-stalled gained a human-comment unpark edge re-entering reviewing, bounded by HumanReviewRounds for all task kinds (re-entry may spawn a review pod); on re-entry #390's level-triggered re-drive completes a lost advance.
- 2026-07-19 (fix/review-handoff-redrive, incident #379) **The reviewing->advance handoff was EDGE-triggered only, so a single dropped advance parked a review-kind Task at handoff-stalled for good.** `DrainPendingReview` (reviewpost.go) calls `advanceAfterReview` exactly ONCE, on the reconcile that clears `pendingReview` (its tail); every later MergeRequest reconcile short-circuits at the now-nil `pendingReview` and never re-attempts it. `TaskReconciler.reconcileClocks` only PARKED handoff-stalled after the 5m `HandoffDeadline` - it never re-drove the advance. So when the one-shot missed (a stale CACHED owned-MR List still showing `pendingReview`; a transient controller-owner sever #369 making `owningTask` return nil so `advanceAfterReview` was skipped at reviewpost.go's `task == nil` guard; a multi-MR ordering race), the review had already landed on the PR (SCM healthy, `review_posted` in ~1-2s) but the Task sat out the whole deadline and parked handoff-stalled instead of advancing. Live incident: two kind=review Tasks (PRs #364 @15:06:54Z, #366 @15:15:22Z) whose correct terminal is parked/awaiting-human parked handoff-stalled. **Fix = LEVEL-triggered backstop, not removing the deliberate reconciler split.** Extracted the pure F.3 reviewing-exit decision `reviewAdvanceEdge(task, mrs, maxRounds) (stage.Edge, bool)` + `maxReviewRounds(proj)` (reviewpost.go), refactored `advanceAfterReview` onto them (no behavior change), and in `reconcileClocks`'s `handoffCondition` block re-run that same decision every reviewing reconcile (30s `stageRequeue` cadence, well inside 5m): if every owned MR has drained its `pendingReview`, take the F.3 edge NOW; only park handoff-stalled if it is genuinely not ready and the deadline elapsed. **The owned-MR read there is LIVE via `r.mrReader()` (uncached APIReader, fallback Client), NOT the informer cache** - `/outcome` persists the MR `pendingReview` (outcome.go:964) BEFORE it stamps the Task's OutcomeAccepted condition that arms `handoffCondition`, and the MR vs Task watch streams are independent, so a cached MR read could lag and show a pre-`/outcome` nil -> the re-drive would advance the Task before its review was ever posted; a live read closes that false-advance race (the ONLY signal distinguishing requested-not-posted from drained is `pendingReview` itself, since `/outcome` sets `Status.Status`=verdict + `ReviewedSHA` in the SAME write it sets `pendingReview`). Idempotent: `EnterStage` refuses a redundant X->X, so a race with the MR reconciler's own advance costs at most one illegal-edge counter, never a double transition. **Deliberately NOT changed:** the metric under-count the incident flagged (transition.go:119 -> `TaskTerminalEntry`) is UNCONDITIONAL after a successful terminal transition - the "1 of 2 parks counted" is a PromQL `increase()[1h]` extrapolation artifact on a step counter, not a code drop; the ownership sever itself is #369 (parent tracker) and `RepairZeroController` + this level re-drive already make the handoff robust to it. TDD: `TestReconcile_ReviewHandoffReDrivesTheDroppedAdvance` (4 subtests: drained MR advances inside deadline; drained MR reaches awaiting-human past deadline NOT handoff-stalled; undrained pendingReview does NOT advance; approved drained MR on an implement Task -> merging) fails RED with the re-drive neutralized, green with it; the existing no-owned-MR test still parks handoff-stalled (`reviewAdvanceEdge` ready=false on an empty set). Gate: controller/stage/restapi/obs tests + golangci-lint green. semver:patch.
- 2026-07-18 (fix/restapi-wire-spill-ci-memory, issue #345) `restapi.Config.Spiller`/`.CIFor`/`.Memory` were nil in wire.go (asymmetric with the webhook server and TaskReconciler) - over-budget `/outcome` writes PANICKED (not aborted; `objbudget.go` calls a nil interface with no guard), `scm_read(kind=ci)` always 501'd, `notes=all` always 502'd. Fixed by wiring all three. Rejected the nil-guard alternative (adding a guard in objbudget.Fit* to fail gracefully instead) as tech debt per hard rule 4 - the real fix is wiring the dependency, not tolerating its absence. **Scope grew past the issue's "fill the struct literal" framing**: `Config.Spiller`/`.Memory` were flat single-instance fields, not per-project resolvers like `SpillerFor func(*Project) objbudget.Spiller` (webhook/TaskReconciler already use this shape). Each Project runs its own tatara-memory endpoint, so a flat instance would silently spill/rehydrate the WRONG project's data once a second Project exists (the cluster already runs two: tatara + infrastructure) - a new correctness bug, not a wiring nit. Renamed to `SpillerFor`/`MemoryFor` (both per-project resolvers) and threaded `proj` through every `objbudget.Fit*` call site in outcome.go/handlers_v2.go (~12 sites; all had `proj` in scope already via `outcomeCtx.proj` or one extra `s.getProjectCR` call, no architectural blocker). `CIFor` needed no such change - it was already a flat `func(provider, token)` matching `ReaderFor`'s shape, since CI reads are already per-request token-resolved. Added `scm.CIReaderByProvider` (mirrors `ReaderByProvider`) instead of a type-assertion at the call site. `newMemoryFor` in wire.go duplicates `newSpillerFor`'s body (returns `restapi.NoteFetcher` instead of `objbudget.Spiller`) rather than unifying via an interface-to-interface assertion - Go doesn't convert between sibling interfaces implicitly, and the existing codebase already accepts this duplication (`addReconcilers` has its own separate copy of the same closure). Test harness (`internal/restapi` `buildV2`) gained optional `spillerFor`/`memoryFor` per-project overrides; new `wire_resolver_test.go` proves eviction and notes=all rehydration route to the CORRECT project's spiller/memory client, never a sibling's. **8-angle code review before commit** caught a real regression: `stampDocumentedBy`'s first draft re-resolved the covered task's Project via a fresh `getProjectCR` Get per loop iteration (redundant - `docbatch.go:62` already filters `DocumentsTasks` to the batch's own project) AND, unlike the sibling `covered` Get in the same loop, did not tolerate a Get failure - one unreachable Project would abort stamping for every remaining covered task in the batch. Fixed by threading `proj` down from the caller (`o.proj`) instead, matching every other function this diff touches. Also collapsed a duplicate `spillerForOrNil` call in `foldMembers` (STEP 1/STEP 5) to one resolve, added the missing `memoryForOrNil` counterpart (`rehydrateNotes` had inlined the same nil-guard `spillerForOrNil` centralizes), and simplified `scm.CIReaderByProvider` to delegate to `ReaderByProvider` + a type-assert instead of duplicating the provider switch. **Accepted, not fixed:** `newSpillerFor`/`newMemoryFor` in wire.go stay two near-identical closures (Go doesn't convert between sibling interfaces implicitly, and `addReconcilers` already duplicates this same construction independently - matches existing repo convention over a premature shared abstraction); `SpillerFor`/`MemoryFor` build a fresh `memclient.Client` per call with no per-project caching (pre-existing pattern from the webhook path, now called from more handlers - a real but low-severity cost, `memclient.New`'s nil-httpClient path shares `http.DefaultTransport`'s connection pool so the marginal cost is one small struct allocation, not a new TCP/TLS pool); `NewServer` does not fail-fast on a nil `SpillerFor`/`MemoryFor` (`internal/restapi` tests deliberately leave `MemoryFor` nil to exercise the notes=all 502 path, so a construction-time panic would break that legitimate coverage - the guard stays at the call-site helpers `spillerForOrNil`/`memoryForOrNil` instead); `postNote` now does one unconditional `getProjectCR` Get per note write (needed because `objbudget.FitTask`'s internal byte-budget eviction can fire independent of the 50-note cap check) - accepted as comparable cost to the `getTaskCR` Get already on that path, not a new class of problem.
- 2026-07-18 (fix/sweep-heartbeat-resilience, #325) **The sweep heartbeat gauge `operator_sweep_last_success_timestamp_seconds` was coupled to a fully-clean pass and so lied about liveness.** SweepProject stamped it ONLY when `firstErr == nil` (returned before the `.Set()` on any per-item error). `fail()` sets firstErr on a single item failing (one repo's list, one issue's comments, one stale/missing MR CR get - though the CR getters already return nil,nil on NotFound), so one transient forge error silenced the heartbeat for the WHOLE pass. Gauges reset on process restart and are only re-emitted by the next clean pass; after the v1.8.0 rollout (3 fresh replicas) the fresh leader hadn't completed a clean pass, so the series was ABSENT and the NoData(Alerting) "Operator sweep heartbeat stale" alert fired while the sweep was in fact running and minting Tasks. **Fix: decouple liveness from per-item errors** - moved `.Set()` to fire on every pass whose repos loop STRUCTURALLY completes (right after the tasks_minted emission), unconditional on firstErr; still `return firstErr` afterward for the reconciler requeue. The activeTaskCount hard-failure still returns BEFORE the stamp, so a sweep that genuinely cannot run still leaves the heartbeat unset (SweepErrorsTotal{reason=list_tasks} + the alert catch it). Metric NAME unchanged (alert references it), Help/comment reworded to "last completed sweep pass (liveness, not zero-error)". Registration was never the problem (all sweep metric names present in Prom index). No observability change needed: issueScan cadence is hourly (`0 * * * *`), alert threshold 2h for 10m, so the heartbeat re-establishes within one cadence of any restart, comfortably inside the window. Boy-scout: removed dead `SweepNightlyActivity` const (defined, zero callers; no nightly sweep planned - the nightly path is the doc BATCH, not the sweep). semver:patch.
- 2026-07-18 (feat/incident-refire-dedupe) Closed the RESIDUAL incident-dedup gaps #333 (v1.3.0, live) left open, found in the audit that closed 20 GH + 5 GL issues across 7 dup chains (worst: one CNPG root cause -> 5 issues across 2 projects). #333 already dedups a SAME-RULE refire (rule+workload `incidentDedupKey`) and posts operator refire comments; three gaps remained. (1) CROSS-RULE correlation: added a coarser `incidentGroupKey` (project + configured correlation labels, default `namespace,cluster`; empty when no correlation label present, since an all-empty group is a false correlation) stamped as `tatara.dev/alert-group-key` on the tracker Issue + `Task.Spec.GroupKey`. At file_issue, when the agent named no parent, `queue.FindOldestOpenGroupSibling` auto-links the new tracker under the oldest open sibling sharing the group but a DIFFERENT rule-key, collapsing a co-firing storm into one tree. LINK-ONLY (never suppresses), so a false group costs at most a spurious sub-issue link - hence enabled-by-default per the decision, not gated. Resolution is deferred to FILE time (not webhook time) so simultaneous multi-rule storms converge with only a one-API-call race window instead of a full agent turn. (2) LIVENESS escape (the `incidentStaleAge` finding #5 that server.go:855 documented but never implemented): a suppressed refire on a tracker past `INCIDENT_ESCALATE_REFIRE_THRESHOLD` (10) refires OR `INCIDENT_ESCALATE_STALE_AGE` (48h) open RE-ADMITS a fresh incident via `EnqueueEvent(..., WithIgnoreOpenIssueDedup())` - skips the open-tracker suppression but still dedups on a live Task/QE (deterministic QE name single-flights it), `Issue.Status.EscalatedAt` gates to <=1 escalation/window. This also gives a root cause that CHANGED under one alert id (helmfile#18 pw-drift vs #20 pg-exhaustion) a second look. (3) The literal "incident has no comment tool": added `submit_outcome(action=comment_issue, comment={repo,number,body})` - a TERMINAL action (rejected/tracked-elsewhere) gated operator-side to Issue CRs carrying a rule/group label, so an incident agent (no `issue_write`) can append evidence ONLY to a platform tracker, never an arbitrary human thread; chose a submit_outcome action over granting issue_write precisely to keep that scope. Cross-repo campaign: tatara-cli PR adds the comment_issue outcome schema/validation; tatara-agent-skills PR rewrites the incident skills (survey-first, comment_issue on SAME incident, issue.parent for related-distinct, escalation re-examine) - the old skills' "you have NO comment tool, always file" was the behavioural half of the bug. Semver minor (additive; existing exact-key dedup unchanged). Correction to the phase-1 read: prod runs v1.8.0, so #333 IS live; the dup chains were pre-#333 backlog, and this feature is the residual-gap closure, not a deploy-catchup.
- 2026-07-18 (fix/queuedevent-status-conflict, issue #348) **~691 `Reconciler error` lines/48h, all controller=queuedevent, all the same 409: "Operation cannot be fulfilled on queuedevents.tatara.dev ... the object has been modified".** Root cause was NOT a second writer/component - grepped the whole repo, nothing outside queue_controller.go ever writes a QueuedEvent - it was `DispatcherReconciler` conflicting with ITSELF: `Reconcile` is triggered per-QueuedEvent (`For(&QueuedEvent{})`), but internally lists the WHOLE project's pool and `admitPool` walks it, writing `Status().Update` on however many QueuedEvents it admits that pass - not just the one named in `req.NamespacedName`. Every QueuedEvent create fires its own independent reconcile that does the SAME full-pool scan, so back-to-back reconciles read a cached `List()` that can lag the immediately-prior Status().Update by informer propagation delay - the same self-conflict shape repository_controller.go's `patchStatus` doc comment already names as "the #175 409-storm fix" and unpark.go's cache-lag comment describes. `queue_controller.go` was the ONE controller file that never got the Get-fresh + `retry.RetryOnConflict` treatment 15+ other files already use (task_controller, repository_controller, sever, unpark, review_apply, projectscan, turncallback, podwatch, reaper, semver_label, sweep, task_stage, issue_apply, intake, deploy_ledger). SSA/field-owner (used elsewhere for ConfigMaps shared across genuinely different writer KINDS - project_memory.go/project_grafana.go) was considered and rejected: this is one writer racing its own stale cache, not multiple owners of one resource: consistency with the established convention, not novelty. Fix: new `patchQueuedEventStatus` (queue_controller.go, mirrors `patchTaskStatus`) replaces admitPool's raw `r.Status().Update(ctx, q)`. Two more raw writes in the SAME file got the identical treatment for the same reason (found alongside, not evidenced in Loki yet but the same bug class) - `admitTicket`'s Task label stamp and its Task status write (stage.Enter/AgentKind self-heal) now route through `patchTaskAnnotations`/`patchTaskStatus`, which were promoted from `TaskReconciler` methods to package-level functions taking `client.Client` (thin method wrappers kept on `TaskReconciler` for its own call sites) specifically so `DispatcherReconciler` - a different receiver type - could reuse them instead of duplicating the Get-fresh+retry shape a third time. The entering-stage write applies PRECOMPUTED absolute values (Stage/StageReason/AgentKind/StageEnteredAt/PodStartedAt/StageWorkStartedAt/PodRecreations) from the already-validated `task` copy onto the fresh object rather than re-running `stage.Enter`'s fallible legality check inside the conflict-retry closure (matches transition.go's "ABSOLUTE ASSIGNMENTS only, never re-derive" rule) and only touches those bounded fields, not `fresh.Status` wholesale, so it cannot clobber Stats/PendingEvents/etc. another writer moved in the meantime. Also added the explicit `WithOptions(ctrlcontroller.Options{MaxConcurrentReconciles: 1})` to `DispatcherReconciler.SetupWithManager` for consistency with every sibling controller (task/project/repository already pin it explicitly) - git history shows no prior commit ever touched this option on queue_controller.go and MEMORY has no entry discussing a deliberate omission, so this was a documentation gap, not an intentional difference; behavior is unchanged since controller-runtime's default was already 1. TDD: `queue_conflict_test.go` proves the RED/GREEN split for real - against the pre-fix raw writes, `TestAdmit_RetriesOnConflict_AdmitsDespiteStaleCache` and `TestAdmitTicket_RetriesOnConflict_StageEntersDespiteStaleCache` fail with the byte-for-byte Loki error string (`Operation cannot be fulfilled on queuedevents.tatara.dev "conflict-target": <nil>`); against the fix, all three new tests (plus the direct `patchQueuedEventStatus` unit test) pass, retrying past an injected one-time Conflict via a wrapping envtest client (mirrors retry_conflict_test.go's existing `conflictOnceWriter` idiom). Full suite green (`make generate manifests test lint`), no CRD/API change. Semver: patch.
- 2026-07-18 (fix/auto-approve-proposals-wiring, security re-review, tamper-evidence ROOT-CAUSE fix) The security re-review of d84f921 found the M4 in-body content-sha256 fingerprint SUPERSEDED-WORTHY: it is unkeyed and lives entirely in the forge-editable issue body, so anyone with GitHub Write / GitLab Reporter+ (a superset of MaintainerLogins) could strip the marker, edit scope, and re-stamp a recomputed hash. No live exploit today (Goal frozen at mint, issues.edited ignored) but the issue-edit body-refresh workstream is approved and coming, and the old comments OVERCLAIMED ("fail closed NOW: any content edit refuses"). Per the no-tech-debt rule, replaced the in-body fingerprint with a CR anchor (root cause), not doc-softening: **new `IssueSpec.ProposalBodyHash`** (`ComputeProposalContentHash` of the filing-time body), written ONCE by the operator in `mintIssueCR` when the body carries a proposal marker, into Spec - the mirror only ever writes Status (mirror.go:337-338), so nothing SCM-side can forge it. `autoApproveApplies` now refuses unless the current mirrored `Status.Body` still hashes to the Spec anchor (`ProposalBodyMatchesAnchor`, same CRLF->LF + TrimSpace normalization). The in-body marker (`<!-- tatara-proposed-by:<kind> -->`, fingerprint DROPPED) is now provenance-only (kind detection + metric label). Real guarantee, stated correctly in code + docs: a party with forge write access can edit the body and rewrite the marker, but cannot rewrite CR Spec, so ANY post-filing body change (scope edit, marker-rewrite forgery) diverges from the anchor and refuses. Fail-closed on a missing anchor (proposal filed by an older build) too. Flag-off byte-path unchanged. New matrix rows: marker-rewrite-attack-refused, missing-anchor-refused (edited-body row kept). CRD field added (make generate manifests: tatara.dev_issues.yaml). This supersedes the M4 fingerprint paragraph below - `ProposalBodyMatchesFingerprint`/`proposalFingerprintFromBody` and the `content-sha256` marker are GONE. Gate green.

- 2026-07-18 (fix/auto-approve-proposals-wiring) **Wired the dead `AutoApproveTataraProposals` flag (SECURITY-SENSITIVE - removes the last human gate before prod).** The task-centric redesign left the flag defined (project_types.go) with NOTHING reading it: every self-proposed chain (brainstorm proposal, incident file_issue) dead-ended at parked(identity-unverified) because a bot-authored issue has no maintainer approval comment. The pre-redesign machinery (`recordAutoApproval`, `Status.ApprovedByMaintainer`, `lifecycle_triage.go`) was all removed; re-wired in the NEW comment-only architecture. **Carve-out location: `verifyOneIssue` (approval_grammar.go), the SINGLE per-Issue verdict shared by all three approval callers** (`VerifyApprovalDetailed` per-Task, `GrammarVerifier.VerifyApproval` REST clarify, `ReVerifyParked` unpark) - one chokepoint, so brainstorm/incident/clarify/unpark all inherit it. Placed ONLY in the no-maintainer-comment arm (`cmt == nil`): a maintainer who commented a NON-approval still falls through to `ApprovalRefusedNoPhrase` and blocks - fail-closed respect for veto-by-comment, stricter than the literal field doc (which lists only human-authorship + close as blockers) but within its spirit ("no SECOND human gate"; the happy path is no human comment at all). **`autoApproveApplies` fail-closed on 4 axes:** flag on (default false = today's behavior EXACTLY), Issue in scope (open, not done/rejected - the human CLOSE is the veto, re-checked here as defense-in-depth even though callers filter), bot-authored (`iss.Status.Author == botLogin`, non-empty - Status.Author is SCM truth mirror-refreshed, so robust across GitLab actor/author divergence; empty author or empty botLogin => refuse), valid provenance marker present. **Marker: `<!-- tatara-proposed-by:<kind> -->`** (kinds brainstorm/incident), pure helpers in api/v1alpha1/proposal_marker.go (`StampProposalMarker`/`ProposalKindFromBody`, regex accepts ONLY the two known kinds => unknown kind fails closed). Filers stamp it on BOTH the forge issue body AND the CR body (via `mintIssueCR`) so it survives an hourly mirror refresh (mirror.go rewrites Status.Body from SCM). Evidence recorded = `ApprovalEvidence{Auto:true, Login:"<tatara:auto>", CommentID:""}`; the existing clause-2 idempotency in verifyOneIssue keeps it alive across re-verification. A real maintainer approval still WINS (recorded as human evidence, Auto:false) - auto is a no-human fallback, never an override. No API/CRD change (flag + `Auto` field already existed); labels.go:112 stale comment (claimed 3 label-driven paths on removed `Status.ApprovedByMaintainer`) rewritten to the 2 comment-only paths. Fail-closed matrix tested explicitly (flag off / human author / empty author / no marker / unknown-kind marker / maintainer non-approval comment => refuse; closed issue => vetoed; human approval => human wins; all-green => Auto:true). Gate: `make generate manifests test lint build` green.

- 2026-07-18 (fix/auto-approve-proposals-wiring, security-review-fix pass, 4 items) Independent security review returned merge-ready (no Critical/Important); owner KEPT the stricter "maintainer non-approval comment blocks auto-approve" behavior. Closed 4 follow-ups. **M1 (doc):** project_types.go AutoApproveTataraProposals doc now states the marker is stamped UNCONDITIONALLY by the filers, so flag-off still changes the stored issue body (marker present but inert - intentional, lets a later flag-flip auto-approve proposals filed while off) while gate BEHAVIOR with the flag off is exactly today's. **M2 (test):** added the empty-botLogin matrix row (project Spec.Scm.BotLogin=="" => refuse; the axis-3 check existed but was untested). **M3 (audit metric):** wired the pre-existing-but-uncalled `operator_auto_approve_total{kind}` counter (obs.AutoApproveTotal) at BOTH Auto-evidence persist sites - outcome.go clarify() (primary: proposal reaches implement via clarify submit) and VerifyApprovalDetailed's persist block (secondary: multi-issue ReVerifyParked). Threaded `metrics *obs.OperatorMetrics` (nil-safe) into VerifyApprovalDetailed + ReVerifyParked; VerifyApproval keeps its signature (passes nil) to avoid churning its many test callers; webhook passes s.cfg.Metrics. Counter increments only on the transition (issue not already approved), so no double-count. Added obs.AutoApproveCounter test accessor. **M4 (tamper-evidence, NEW REQUIREMENT):** a bot-proposal body edited since filing must NOT auto-approve - guards the incoming issue-edit body-refresh workstream (today safe only because Task.Spec.Goal is frozen + issues.edited ignored). Chose an embedded content fingerprint over a CRD field: marker is now `<!-- tatara-proposed-by:<kind> content-sha256:<64hex> -->`, hash computed over the filing-time body (normalized: CRLF->LF + both-ends TrimSpace, so cosmetic reformat is tolerated, interior edits are not). `ProposalBodyMatchesFingerprint` strips the marker back out and recomputes; autoApproveApplies now requires marker present AND fingerprint match. Fail-closed: no marker / no fingerprint / mismatch / marker removal all refuse; flag-off untouched. Self-contained in api/v1alpha1 (no CRD field, so no non-refreshed-status-field problem; the fingerprint travels in the body through the mirror). New matrix rows: empty-botLogin-refused, edited-body-refused. Gate: `make generate manifests test lint build` green.

- 2026-07-18 (WS3 sever operation) `SeverIssueFromTask(DeleteCR|Orphan)`
  (internal/controller/sever.go) is the ONE detach op both I3 and I4 use so the
  Task side (`Status.IssueRefs`), the CR side (delete / ownerRef-drop), and the
  mirror `tatara-parked` label move together. IssueRefs is cleared FIRST: the
  worst crash-state after step 1 is "CR still owner-reffed but not listed by the
  Task", which keeps a valid controller owner (no B.2-rule-5 violation) and makes
  `ownedIssues` skip it (no spurious terminal comment / label re-stamp), and the
  leader re-reconciles step 2 idempotently. The op is CLIENT-SIDE only; the
  FORGE-side `tatara-parked` removal (F.6 operator-on-promotion) is the I4
  caller's job via scanWriter (the mirror-label strip inside sever is what the
  mint decision actually reads). Rejected doing the forge write inside sever: it
  would need a writer+token the DeleteCR (I3) path does not have.
- 2026-07-18 (WS3-I3 stop) `ApplyIssueClosedStop` (issue_apply.go) is driven
  LEADER-ONLY from IssueReconciler (owned+closed+live-non-deploying stage ->
  rejected(issue-closed) + sever DeleteCR + DeleteWrapper). The webhook only
  mirrors `State=closed` (issues.closed). `deploying`/`documenting`/terminals are
  excluded (`stage.AllowsIssueClosedStop`): a merged/deploying change is not
  rewound, and C.4's deploying-close is thus never mistaken for a human stop.
  IssueReconciler ALSO finishes a crash-interrupted DeleteCR on a
  rejected(issue-closed) owner whose closed CR is still present (re-sever
  hardening), restoring prompt reopen after the sever crash window.
- 2026-07-18 (WS3-I4 one-reply resume) A human reply to a NO-RE-ENTRY parked Task
  (stage.HasReentry==false) triggers `ProjectReconciler.resumeNoReentryParks`
  (resume.go): close the old task's bot PR FIRST (closeTaskBotMRs - a focused,
  NO-issue-side-effect PR close, NOT releaseTerminal, so no spurious "stopped
  working" comment), THEN sever(Orphan) the issue, THEN MintForItem from the
  MIRROR CR (Comments end with the reply -> humanHasLastWord -> triaging ACTIVE).
  KEY NON-OBVIOUS INTERACTION: the fresh clarify mint and the old parked task
  share the SAME deterministic IntakeTaskName (both key on the issue), so
  MintForItem's createTaskRaceSafe DELETES the old stale-terminal task and
  re-mints on the NEXT pass (same mechanism the design gives I3 reopen). This is
  why the PR must be closed BEFORE the sever: once the issue is orphaned, ANY
  mint (resume or sweep) collides-and-deletes the old task, and a still-OPEN PR
  would then cascade its mirror away un-closed. The design text's "old task
  coexists / ages out as a debugging artifact" is not literally reachable under
  deterministic naming; the intent (no leaked PR, one active fresh clarify,
  gate-safe) is preserved. Leader-only; the reaper is the backstop.
  RESUME READS THE ISSUE MIRROR LIVE (uncached APIReader, resume.go `liveIssue`):
  on the DIRECT-MINT path (old kind != clarify -> no IntakeTaskName collision ->
  fresh Task created in the SAME pass) a lagging cache would hide the webhook's
  just-appended reply, humanHasLastWord would be false, and the fresh Task would
  mint parked(backlog-sweep) - needing a SECOND reply. The live read preserves the
  one-reply guarantee (#348/#352 discipline). resumeOne severs ALL open issues
  BEFORE any MintForItem so a collision-delete of the old Task cannot hard-fault a
  later in-loop sever; SeverIssueFromTask ALSO tolerates a gone Task (refs moot)
  and still orphans the issue's own ownerRef so an unsevered issue never cascades.
- 2026-07-18 (WS3 accepted-ignored inventory) Documented in handleForgeItem's
  routing default: issues.unlabeled (no body change), pull_request.edited /
  ready_for_review, pull_request_review state=dismissed + GitLab MR unapproved
  (M2 - a dismissal is weak/administrative; use request_changes or close), and
  non-default-branch push. All converge via the sweep / mirror cadence. WS3-I2
  edit fold appends an `issue_edited` pending event and NEVER calls
  driveCommentUnpark: the leader's driveUnparks drives the unpark, keeping the
  edit path off the F6-1 webhook-goroutine-mutation surface entirely.

- 2026-07-18 (webhook-primary architecture) Reactive intake is coordinated by
  IDEMPOTENT NATURAL-KEY dedup, NOT an in-process lock. Webhook and sweep both
  funnel through `controller.Minter.MintForItem`; the Task carries a
  deterministic name (`IntakeTaskName(project,kind,repo,number)`), a live
  (uncached APIReader) pre-check, and `IgnoreAlreadyExists` on Create - so the
  apiserver, not a cached List, is the arbiter. Rejected the wait-lock: it only
  coordinates within one process, breaks under leader failover / rolling
  deploys, and adds a stuck-lock failure mode. This is the controller-runtime
  FAQ / Flux / ArgoCD precedent. (spec 2026-07-17-webhook-primary-reactivity.)
- 2026-07-18 (WS1-A guard, flagged for WS1-B) `handleReview`'s terminal guard
  is `TaskDone(task) && Stage != StageParked` (server.go): a truly-terminal
  Task is dropped, but a PARKED Task reaches the appliers, which route it by
  park reason (`ReenterOnReviewChangesRequested`): merge-timeout -> merging
  (MergeReentries accounting, FOLDS at `MaxMergeReentries` rather than
  terminating), no-outcome -> implementing behind Unpark's guards, every other
  reason folds to the pending-event path. A human review must not escape a
  cap (review-loop-exhausted, stage-deadline) one review at a time.
- 2026-07-18 (WS1-B F6-1, corrected) Human-review appliers write stage + delete
  the wrapper pod from the webhook HTTP goroutine, which runs on EVERY replica;
  reconcilers are leader-only. Production is 3-replica HA (leaderElection: 1
  active + 2 standby, tatara-helmfile values/tatara-operator/default.yaml:2), so
  a non-leader applying a transition + pod-delete against the leader's reconcile
  is PERMANENT STEADY STATE on every human review, NOT a rolling-deploy
  transient (an earlier note claiming replicaCount:1 was factually wrong - fixed
  at root, not documented away). Two fixes: (1) the webhook resolves the owning
  Task through the uncached APIReader, so `reviewAlreadyProcessed` + `TaskDone`
  are authoritative across replicas (closes double STAGE-apply). (2) The
  pod-recreate race is closed at the controller. `refreshTaskFromAPI` already
  live-adopts the stage at dispatch top, so the residual hole is the intermediate
  window in ApplyReviewApproval (WS1-A F5 deletes the pod BEFORE the merging write
  lands, so a live read there still reads reviewing): `TaskReconciler.liveStageDiffers`
  re-reads live in the pod-absent (re)spawn branches and skips create/respawn once
  the stage moved (narrows the phantom spawn, generic to any non-leader
  transition), and `DrainPendingReview` now GATES on the owning Task being in
  reviewing - if the Task advanced off reviewing (a maintainer approval enters
  merging directly and a raced review pod re-arms PendingReview afterwards), the
  stale pending review is dropped "refused" without posting or overwriting
  ReviewedSHA. That gate is the load-bearing correctness guard (advanceAfterReview
  gates the ADVANCE on the same reviewing check; this gates the POST); the pod
  guard is spawn/cost prevention + defense. Route-through-leader (annotate-to-poke)
  was rejected: it would unwire WS1-A's webhook->applier call sites for no
  correctness gain over the two gates.
- 2026-07-18 (WS1-B F5-2 follow-up) A folded review now mirrors as ExternalID
  "review-<reviewID>"; a subsequent forge thread RE-SCAN (mirror.go cadence sync)
  fetches the SAME comment under the forge's NUMERIC comment id, so the mirror can
  briefly hold two rows for one review-comment until dedup/eviction converges.
  Cosmetic (mirror is byte-budget-evicted set-union, not a source of truth for
  dedup); revisit only if it shows up as duplicated review text in a bundle.
  Also: handleIssueOpened's Mark-then-mint-then-Clear is a deliberate double write
  on the happy path - Mark MUST precede the mint so a mint failure (5xx) leaves
  the sweep its cold-start marker; do NOT "optimize" it to mint-first.
- 2026-07-18 (WS1-B F8-1/F6 dedup scheme) Human-review (review.id,state) dedup
  is now ONE bounded annotation `tatara.dev/reviewed` (was one
  `tatara.dev/reviewed-<reviewID>` key per review). Value is a drop-oldest FIFO
  of up to 32 `<hash>:<state>` entries, hash = `sha256(reviewID)[:12]`. Fixes
  both the k8s 63-char annotation-NAME overflow (GitLab synthesizes
  `gl-approve-<IID>-<40hexsha>`, which blew the limit for IID>=100 so GitLab
  dedup silently never persisted) and the unbounded key growth on long-lived
  Tasks. A failed stamp now returns 5xx so the forge REDELIVERS (both appliers
  are idempotent): a lost dedup marker is worse than a redundant re-apply.
- 2026-07-18 (WS1-B F1-1 naming) `IntakeTaskName` now embeds the LITERAL
  issue/PR number and a 64-bit (16-hex) sha suffix:
  `mt-<kindInitial>-<repoRef>-<number>-<16hex>`. The old `<8hex>`-only scheme
  hid the number inside the hash (32-bit), so distinct natural keys could
  birthday-collide, and the loser's Issue mirror was never owned - silent
  permanent starvation. No migration: `IntakeTaskName` is new in this branch
  (absent on main) and the branch has never deployed, so no old-scheme Task
  can exist. F5-1: orphan-COMMENT mint is restricted to `!ev.IsPR` - an orphan
  PR comment used the COMMENTER as PR author (ClassifyPR's bot-ignore keys on
  the real author), fabricating authorship; the PR-open webhook + sweep already
  cover PRs, so orphan-issue-comment mint is preserved and PR mint is dropped.

- 2026-07-17 (Task 5, dead-cron cleanup) Deleted the confirmed-dead `cdScan` /

  `ScmCron.CDScan`, `ScmCron.HealthCheck`, `ProjectStatus.LastCDScan`,
  `ProjectStatus.LastHealthCheck`, their unreachable `activityScheduleAndLast`/
  `stampScan` arms, and the tests that constructed them
  (`projectscan_healthcheck_harness_test.go`, `TestHealthCheckCronDropped`,
  `listHealthCheckQEs`, `TestHealthCheckActivity_SchedulePatternField`). Neither
  had a dispatch call site (`runScans` never passed "cdScan"/"healthCheck" to
  either switch). The `healthCheck` MODEL/ceiling pseudo-key in
  `internal/agent/pod.go` (`modelByKind`/`effortByKind`/`spawnCeilingByKind`,
  and its test references) is a SEPARATE, LIVE concept and was left intact.
  Regenerated deepcopy + CRD; `make generate manifests test lint build` green.

- 2026-07-17 (fix/comment-unpark-cache-lag, adversarial review-fix pass) **5 findings on the cache-lag fix below, all fixed.** (1) `ProjectReconciler.SetupWithManager` did not self-wire `APIReader` - a wire.go regression would silently fall back to the cached client with no compile error and no test failure; added the same `if r.APIReader == nil { r.APIReader = mgr.GetAPIReader() }` idiom `DispatcherReconciler.SetupWithManager` already uses (queue_controller.go). `webhook.NewServer` has no manager reference to self-wire from (Config is a plain struct, no `mgr ctrl.Manager` param) - correctly left as wire.go's explicit literal assignment, not a gap. (2) A decline had a log but no metric (rule 13 gap) - new `operator_unpark_declined_total{stageReason,kind}` counter (obs/task_metrics.go, next to `operator_task_parked_total`), incremented on every decline in both `ApplyUnpark` callers. (3) Guard-decline (live Stage/StageReason drifted from the caller's belief - rare, anomalous) and rule-decline (`stage.Unpark` says not-yet - normal steady state) both collapsed into `target=="",err==nil`; `ApplyUnpark` now returns a third value, `UnparkDecline` (`DeclineGuard`/`DeclineRule`/`DeclineNone`). **`driveCommentUnpark` logs BOTH kinds at INFO** (fires once, in direct reaction to a human action - silence of either kind is anomalous) - this SUPERSEDES nothing, it is unchanged from the entry below. **`driveUnparks` now ALSO logs GUARD declines** at INFO (`"unpark: declined (drift guard)"`) - this **corrects** the entry below's "deliberately did NOT add per-decline logging to driveUnparks": that blanket statement is now only true for RULE declines (still silent there - a merge-timeout Task inside its budget declines every sweep pass and logging that would be pure spam); a GUARD decline in a sweep is not steady state, it means another writer raced the same Task, and staying silent on that would repeat this exact bug class one guard-check away. Both decline kinds count in the metric regardless of caller. (4) Corrected a false MEMORY.md claim in the entry below (see the parenthetical inserted there): `c` was never Update-only, it always stayed the read path for Issue/MR/count too - only the retry-loop Task Get moved to the live reader. (5) Verified (no code change) `loadTaskIssues`'s cached read at the `ApplyUnpark` call site is NOT a second instance of the bug - one-line comment added at the call site recording why (the owning Issue CR is guaranteed pre-existing on this path, the preceding same-request write only touches `Status.Comments`, and `stage.Unpark`'s `openIssues`/`allApproved` read `Status.State`/`Status.Status` - fields untouched by that write - so a stale read only ever routes into clarifying, never into a silent decline). Tests: self-wire (real envtest `ctrl.Manager`, both the nil->filled and preset-not-clobbered cases), guard-vs-rule metric+logging split in both `driveUnparks` and `driveCommentUnpark` (a `recordingSink` logr.LogSink captures `log.FromContext` output in the controller package, the existing JSON-log-buffer pattern covers the webhook package), metric registration + increments in obs. `make generate manifests`, N/A (no CRD/API change this pass); `go test ./... -count=1`, `golangci-lint run` both green.

- 2026-07-17 (fix/comment-unpark-cache-lag) **Comment-driven unpark lost the cache-lag race 2/2 in prod, silently.** `AppendTaskEvent`'s `Status().Update` writes straight to the API server; `driveCommentUnpark` -> `ApplyUnpark` re-Got the Task through the CACHED client microseconds later, the informer hadn't observed the write yet, `fresh.Status.PendingEvents` came back empty, and the decline (`ok=false`) is a normal non-error outcome - no log, no metric. `ApplyUnpark` now takes an explicit `reader client.Reader` (manager's `GetAPIReader()`, same #347/#348 idiom as `TaskReconciler.APIReader`) used for the retry-loop Get; `c` (cached `client.Client`) stays the Update path AND the Issue/MR/count reads (`loadTaskIssues`, `loadTaskMRs`, `CountActiveTasks`) - only the retry-loop Task Get moved to the live reader, matching how a cached informer client and the real apiserver actually relate (reads lag, writes never do). Wired at both `ApplyUnpark` callers: `webhook.Config.APIReader` (driveCommentUnpark) and `ProjectReconciler.APIReader` (driveUnparks), both from `mgr.GetAPIReader()` in wire.go. `driveCommentUnpark` now logs INFO on decline (`pending_event_unpark_declined`, task+stage_reason) - it fires in direct reaction to a human comment, so silence there hides a real race. Deliberately did NOT add per-decline logging to `driveUnparks`: it sweeps every parked Task every reconcile pass, and a decline there is the expected steady state for most of them (e.g. merge-timeout still waiting) - logging every miss would be pure log spam, not a signal. Tests use a `staleGetClient`/`upStaleGetClient` wrapper (Get returns a captured stale snapshot, everything else - Update included - passes through to the real live client) to reproduce the cached-vs-live divergence without fighting fake-client resourceVersion conflicts.

- 2026-07-13 (task-centric-redesign, WIRING-AND-BUGS pass, UNCOMMITTED) **wire.go connected nothing: five implemented+tested mechanisms had NO production caller (the old phase machine that was the fallback was deleted, so no safety net). Wired them + fixed localized bugs.** **W1 (approval GRANT was dead):** `restapi.Config.Approval` was never set, so `verifyApprovalScope` hit `s.approval == nil` and failed closed on EVERY `clarify decision=implement` - the platform could never implement anything (2398 tests passed only because `fakeApproval` existed). NO production type implemented `ApprovalVerifier`. Fix: new `controller.GrammarVerifier{Client}` (implements the restapi seam structurally, no import cycle - controller never imports restapi) reads the Issue CR's MIRRORED comments and runs the C.6 grammar; extracted the per-Issue grammar body into `verifyOneIssue` shared by `GrammarVerifier` and `VerifyApprovalDetailed` (did NOT reimplement the grammar). Wired `restapi.Config.Approval` + webhook `SpillerFor` in wire.go. **Webhook `Spiller` is PER-PROJECT:** added `webhook.Config.SpillerFor func(*Project) objbudget.Spiller` (defaults to a closure over the single `Spiller` for back-compat with existing tests); `reverifyParked`/`deliverPendingEvent` resolve it per event, matching the reconcilers (a single fixed endpoint would spill to the wrong project's memory). **W2 (B.6 reaper + doc batch never ran):** `ReapTerminal` and `MintDocBatch` had ZERO non-test callers -> terminal Tasks/Issues/MRs never released or GC'd (unbounded etcd), `tatara-parked` never stamped (reintroduced the M25 re-mint loop), `delivered` never collected. Wired `ReapTerminal` + the new W3 `driveUnparks` into `ProjectReconciler.Reconcile` (leader-only, every reconcile, regardless of cron; a reap error requeues per M25). Wired `MintDocBatch` onto the documentation cron in `runScans` REPLACING `documentationScan` - decisive: contract lines 3496-3497 + CONFLICT 5 make documentation the F2 NIGHTLY BATCH keyed on delivered Tasks; `documentationScan` (per-changed-repo diff model) is the superseded design-section-9/12 mechanism. Left `documentationScan` defined (still test-referenced, lint-safe) but unwired - noted in ROADMAP as removable. **W3 (5 of 6 park reasons had no un-park driver):** `stage.Unpark` had full re-entry bodies for merge-timeout/deploy-timeout/no-outcome/awaiting-human/backlog-sweep but only identity-unverified had a caller; `unparkFires` only CHECKS on a DeepCopy, never applies. New `internal/controller/unpark.go`: `ApplyUnpark` (the SINGLE application of stage.Unpark, shared) + `ProjectReconciler.driveUnparks` (applies to every parked Task EXCEPT identity-unverified, which stays webhook+grammar-driven). Comment-driven awaiting-human/backlog-sweep ALSO driven promptly from the webhook `deliverPendingEvent` (new `driveCommentUnpark`), with driveUnparks as the reconcile-cadence backstop. **I5 (TTL stop was dead code):** `agent.TTLStopper.StopWithHandoff` had ZERO callers - pods never gracefully TTL-stopped, the "notes never empty after a TTL stop" guarantee never ran. Wired `ttlStop` into `reconcilePodStage` gated on `agent.TTLExpired`; after the stop it nils PodStartedAt/StageWorkStartedAt to re-arm a FRESH continuation pod (bounded by maxTurnsPerTask + stage clock, NOT the crash-recreation budget - a TTL rotation is graceful). LastFinalText/PushedRepos are NOT persisted on the Task (only recordResult stamps turn-complete), so the synthetic note degrades to "(none)" - the non-empty-notes guarantee still holds; did NOT add TaskStatus fields (guardrail). **I10:** `handleTurnSubmitFailure` now routes a 410 (`agent.IsTTLGone`) into the same `ttlStop` (counted transient), instead of hard-erroring/backoff-looping. **C4 (subagent):** `foldMembers` adopted ownership but never appended to `Status.IssueRefs/MRRefs` (every consumer reads the slices) - now calls `appendTaskRefFor`. **C5:** added immutable `TaskSpec.InitialStage`+`InitialStageReason`; the create-edge honors them (`from==""` mint never fires terminal metrics), so mintTaskForIssue/mintReviewTaskForPR/MintDocBatch drop their racy non-retrying post-create stage `Status().Update` (the reconciler used to win the race and strand a backlog-swept issue actively triaged with no issueRefs); refs now stamped via `stampMintStatus` (RetryOnConflict). **C6 (subagent):** `Task.Spec.Goal` rendered UNESCAPED into the trusted assignment zone (injection) - now an escaped `<goal>` element in `<task_context>`; assignment.go no longer echoes raw goal (bundle.go is in internal/prompt, not controller). **C7 (subagent):** `/outcome` idempotency claimed the `OutcomeAccepted` fingerprint via a conditional status write on a FRESH read BEFORE side effects (was a stale top-of-handler read stamped only in trailing commit - two concurrent identical POSTs double-forged). **I1:** four contract-K.1 metrics (`operator_task_stage`, `operator_task_stage_age_seconds`, `operator_task_parked_total`, `operator_queue_age_seconds`) + `operator_orphan_adopted_total` were NEVER emitted; gauges recompute+Reset (M22 cardinality, no per-task Delete hooks). **I2 (subagent):** wired `RecordReviewOutcome`, mapping REST `request_changes`->metric `changes_requested`. **I6 (subagent):** poll backstop typo `tr.State == "completed"` -> `"complete"` (wrapper's real literal). **REVIEWS GOT WRONG:** I1 claimed the four metrics feed live alerts that "read silently green" (tatara-cd.yaml:39,54; tatara-operator.yaml:650-772) - but the CURRENT tatara-observability alert files reference entirely different metric names (`tatara_cd_cascade_stalled`, `operator_token_budget_used_ratio`, `operator_reap_delete_error_total`); the four K.1 metrics are contract-mandated (and K.2's contract alerts use them) but NO deployed alert consumes them yet, so emitting them is correct-per-contract, not alert-unblocking. Verified SOUND (untouched): mergePRSquash single egress, approval_grammar core, ourMR reaper predicate, stage transition tables/clocks. Gate: `make generate manifests` (TaskSpec InitialStage regen committed), lint, test.

- 2026-07-12 (adversarial re-review of the Request C review-fix pass, 5 must-fix + 4 minor) A SECOND review found the F1/F4 fix incomplete and two more agent-reachable gaps. **M1 (writeback bypass):** `checkRemainingScopeHardFail` was called from `finishImplement` and from `doWriteBack`'s post-switch fallthrough, but `doWriteBack` dispatches `case "triageIssue": return r.writeBackIssue(...)` BEFORE that fallthrough, and `writeBackIssue`'s `out.Action == "implement"` branch calls `r.writeBackOpenChange` directly - a triageIssue-implement Task with declared RemainingScope sailed straight through. Fixed by hoisting the check ABOVE the kind switch in `doWriteBack` (it no-ops on kinds that never set RemainingScope). Also added a kind gate to the REST `POST /tasks/{t}/change-summary` handler (was the only outcome-writing endpoint with none) rejecting `IsProjectScopedKind` kinds. **M2 (close-directive regex):** `closeDirectiveRE` only matched `clos(e|es|ed)|fix(es|ed)?|resolv(e|es|ed)` immediately followed by `#N` - missed the `-ing` inflections, `Implements`, a colon, an `issue`/`issues` word, and every ref past the first in a comma list. Widened to cover the full GitHub/GitLab keyword set + inflections + optional colon/issue-word + comma/`and` ref lists, and `neutralizeUnapprovedCloses` now rewrites per-ref (approved refs byte-preserved when the whole directive is clean, unapproved refs stripped even inside a mixed list). **M3 (fail-open on List error):** both `unapprovedSystemicSiblings` and `withApprovedSystemicGroup` returned "nothing to worry about" (nil / task unchanged) on a client List error - now fail CLOSED (all siblings treated as unapproved / SystemicGroup emptied) rather than threading a new error return through call sites mid-writeback. **M4 (stale lock, no successor Task):** REVERTED - see the 2026-07-12 de-scope entry below; `ImplementationLocked`/`ImplementationLockedAt` and the whole approval fan-out feature this fixed a gap in were removed two entries later in this same de-scope pass, not shipped. **M5 (links sync self-defeats):** `syncSiblingLinks` swallowed every GetIssue/EditIssue error but the caller stamped `Status.LinksSyncedURLs` unconditionally - under SCM rate-limiting the exact retry the gate exists for never happened. `syncSiblingLinks` now returns a `clean bool` (a permanent 404/410 counts as done via the existing `isPermanentTargetGone`, a transient error does not) and the caller only stamps on a clean sweep. **m6/m7:** added a stable name tie-break to `newestTaskForSource` (metav1.Time is second-granularity) and made `issueHasRecordedApproval` newest-wins (was any-match, asymmetric with the lock's own resolution) - the auto-approve sentinel intentionally still counts, only the doc comment claiming "identity-verified HUMAN ... ONLY" was corrected to state the truth. (Kept post-de-scope: `newestTaskForSource` is still used by `issueHasRecordedApproval` and the clarify bundle for reasons independent of the fan-out feature this round was reviewing.) **m8:** `allIssueSiblingURLs`/`issueURLFromRepoURL` now take an optional repo-slug -> URL map so a self-hosted GitLab project's sibling links use its real host instead of the gitlab.com fallback. **m9:** `checkRemainingScopeHardFail` now posts the same kind of gated conversational comment the other terminal paths use (explains the declared remaining scope) and swaps the phase label to declined, instead of leaving an implementation-labelled issue with no PR and no explanation. **Left as-is (reported, not fixed):** the scope guard only fires when a Task actually reaches `doWriteBack`/`finishImplement`; a Task whose PR already opened (PrURL set, WritebackPending cleared) that later posts a NEW change_summary with RemainingScope during a review-fix turn has no reconcile path that re-evaluates it - doing this properly needs new terminal-state semantics for "PR already open but scope declared incomplete after the fact" (close the PR? revert auto-merge? who decides?), which is a design decision, not a mechanical fix, so it was not attempted here. Full `make generate manifests` (ImplementationLockedAt), `go test ./... -race -count=1`, `golangci-lint run` (0 issues), `pre-commit run --all-files` all green.

- 2026-07-12 - Request C: removed maybeOpenFollowupIssue entirely - a non-empty ChangeSummary.RemainingScope now hard-fails the Task (Phase=Failed, reason=IncompleteImplementation) instead of filing a follow-up issue. FollowupIssueURL/RemainingScope CRD fields kept (API compat) but RemainingScope is now vestigial-on-success (its presence is always a failure signal).

- 2026-07-11 (autonomy-dedup-crd-hygiene batch, Phases 2-4) **Incident dedup, item 4a auto-approve, sibling cross-linking.** (Phase 2) Incident dedup identity moved from labels (`tatara.dev/alert-group` Task label, `tatara/alert-group-<hash>` issue label) to `TaskSpec.DedupKey`: `matchIncidentByDedupKey` Lists incident Tasks and filters by `Spec.DedupKey` + a recorded `Status.DiscoveredIssues[0]` instead of a label-selector/issue-label match. The reaper now spares a terminal incident Task while its tracked issue is still open (`incidentTrackerIssueStillOpen`, reads only cached `Status.WorkItems` state - fails toward retaining on any uncertainty), since the Task itself is now the dedup anchor and premature GC would drop the lookup mid-incident. (Phase 3, SECURITY-SENSITIVE) `proposalKind()` derives the `tatara-proposed-by:<kind>` marker kind from `ProposedIssueSpec.Incident` only - refine never creates `ProposedIssue` Tasks today (confirmed via grep), so only brainstorm/incident are distinguished; extend `proposalKind` if refine gains a propose path later. Auto-approve (path c) is inserted inside the ALREADY-SHIPPED path (a)/(b) `if task.Status.ApprovedByMaintainer == ""` block in `lifecycle_triage.go`'s implement arm, attempted only after path (b)'s maintainer-participation scan found no approver - a live human approval always wins over the mechanical auto-approve when both are available in the same reconcile. Bot-authorship for path (c) reuses the existing `isBotAuthoredProposal(proj, task)` (reads `task.Spec.Source.AuthorLogin`, no extra SCM call) rather than a fresh live-issue-author read, since the Task already carries that value from ingestion. `triageReader` gained a memoized `getIssueContent` so `isTataraAuthored`/`tataraProposedByKind` share one `GetIssue` fetch per reconcile instead of two. (Phase 4) `syncSiblingLinks` maintains a `<!-- tatara-links:start/end -->` managed block idempotently via `SpliceLinksBlock`; `parseIssueURL` (new `internal/controller/issue_url.go`) is shared across the Phase-2 reaper spare check and the Phase-4 sibling linker to avoid a duplicate GitHub/GitLab issue-URL parser.

- 2026-07-11: A verified maintainer's thread comment again releases a parked `implement` triage outcome (operator scans thread via `approvingMaintainer`, records `ApprovedByMaintainer`, falls through to `onImplement`). Reverses the earlier "a comment alone no longer releases" gate; safe because the operator - not the agent - verifies the commenter is a `MaintainerLogins` member (closed by default; SCM read error and non-maintainer/empty-list all fail closed). Manual `tatara-approved` label path unchanged.
- 2026-07-11 (fix/reaper-phase-race-pod-blip) **Orphan reaper no longer deletes a live wrapper pod mid-continuation, and the poll+reap ticker now runs on the leader only.** Grafana triage of wrapper pod `tatara-tatara-gh-tatara-operator-issue-203` (6 distinct pod UIDs in 24h, `kube_pod_container_status_restarts_total==0` on every incarnation => delete/recreate churn, not a crash) traced the blip to `reaper.go` `orphanReason` reaping on `isTerminal(task.Status.Phase)` ALONE: `phase=Succeeded` is set on turn-batch drain (`task_terminate reason=NoPendingSubtasks`), but the task is frequently revived by `resetAgentRun` to continue in the SAME warm pod (front-half implement handoff `triageImplementAction` terminal=false; conversation reactivation). Observed for task `scan-qe-84k9j`: `phase=Succeeded` 12:03:57Z -> `reaped ... reason="task phase Succeeded"` 12:04:01Z -> `lifecycle_transition Triage->Conversation` 12:04:02Z (pod killed while lifecycle still live). FIX (1): gate the phase branch on `task.Status.DeployState == ""` - an empty DeployState marks a one-shot (non-conversational) task genuinely done (reap now, unchanged); a lifecycle task showing transient `phase=Succeeded` has a non-empty DeployState, so it is skipped by the phase branch and handled by the lifecycle-terminal branch (Done/Stopped/Parked) or the idle backstop (`IdlePodReapAfter`, default 30m, issue #237, `!taskHasInflightTurn` guarded). Every `resetAgentRun` continuation carries a non-empty DeployState (implement->`Implement`, reactivation->`Triage`), so `DeployState==""` cleanly separates "done one-shot" from "between-turns lifecycle task". Cost: an await-approval park (DeployState=Conversation, phase=Succeeded) now holds its warm pod up to IdlePodReapAfter instead of cold-respawning on quick reactivation - bounded, not a leak, strictly better than instant-reap. NON-OBVIOUS: did NOT change `isTerminal` (task_controller.go:89, ~10 callers) - only the reaper's use of it; issue-derived pod naming (`podNameSuffix` -> `issue-<N>`) left as-is (the `tatara.dev/task-uid` label already disambiguates incarnations, so the shared name is not the kill trigger). FIX (2): the poll+reap ticker lived in `CallbackServer.Start` under `callbackRunnable` (NeedLeaderElection=false, correct for the HTTP callback+push-metrics handler which must serve on every replica), so `PollOnce`+`ReapOrphans` ran in EVERY replica (confirmed: two replicas logged the same reap 0.5s apart). Split the ticker into `CallbackServer.RunMaintenance(ctx)` registered as a NEW leader-only runnable `maintenanceRunnable` (NeedLeaderElection=true) in wire.go; Start keeps only the HTTP server + bounded shutdown. Leader-election-disabled (single replica) still runs it. Gate green: make generate manifests (NO CRD drift - no API change), lint (0), test (full envtest controller+manager suites), build. Design/plan: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-11-reaper-phase-race-pod-blip-design.md, docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-11-reaper-phase-race-pod-blip.md.

- 2026-07-11 (feat/task-kind-redesign, cross-flow hardening, UNCOMMITTED) **Six cross-flow interaction fixes** (PROGRESS-hardening.md "Cross-flow interaction findings"). Load-bearing decisions: (1) The tier-revert model floor is SCOPED to the terminal `tatara-helmfile` target repo (`modelForKindOnRepo`), NOT a blunt always-on floor on the 5 reasoning kinds. An always-on floor was rejected because it contradicts the existing override-wins model tests AND finding #2 (which hardens tier-revert for kind=review, so component-repo review IS tierable down normally). Scoping to tatara-helmfile protects the entire self-heal chain (the revert MR's own review/implement live there) while leaving per-component tiering intact - the sanctioned "bypass for tier-revert-originated Tasks", identified structurally by target repo (no origin marker; any helmfile change deserves opus). (2) Systemic sibling approval is enforced AUTHORITATIVELY at implement-time (prompt filter + writeback close-strip), NOT at group construction: the group is stamped once at lead-task creation before ANY approval is recorded, so construction-time approval-filtering would empty every group; construction only excludes maintainer-DECLINED siblings (a permanent label-visible no). Residual: a sibling approved AFTER lead creation is not retroactively added to the ledger role:closes group (proceeds as its own implement) - safe (never a wrong close). (3) Cross-source proposal dedup now normalizes titles and applies to BOTH brainstorm and incident, superseding the prior deliberate "incident never title-dedups" behavior (that test was updated). Gate green: make generate manifests (no new API fields - reused DeployState/DeployedVersion/ApprovedByMaintainer, no CRD drift) lint test(-race) build. Single writer.Merge egress (mergePRSquash) untouched.

- 2026-07-11 (feat/task-kind-redesign, Phase 3+4) **clarify kind reconcile + webhook routing.** clarify decomposes the issueLifecycle FRONT-half (Triage+Conversation) into a discrete kind: `reconcileClarify` (clarify.go) reuses the shared queue-drain preamble (`drainLifecycleQueues`, extracted from reconcileLifecycle - byte-identical metric semantics, both call it), the shared front-half agent-run driver (`handleFrontHalf`, extracted from handleTriage), and `handleConversation`; it dispatches ONLY ""->Triage / Triage / Conversation / terminal, and ERRORS on any deploy-half state (clarify never enters Implement/MRCI/etc). The implement-outcome terminal action is parameterized: `finishFrontHalf(onImplement)` (extracted from finishTriage) runs the shared close/discuss/guard/default arms; issueLifecycle passes `triageImplementAction` (approved label + setLifecycleState Implement, terminal=false so the shared resetAgentRun tail runs, same Task continues), clarify passes `clarifyImplementAction` (handoff.go: setLifecycleLabel(implementation) removes brainstorming/adds implementation preserving the one-of-4 invariant + populates Status.Handover warm-resume artifact + setLifecycleState Done, terminal=true so finishFrontHalf SKIPS the resetAgentRun tail that would resurrect the terminated Task). Removed maybeEnqueueDocumentation push trigger entirely (documentation is a Phase-5 cron). The trigger-label-on-Conversation->Implement webhook jump is restricted to issueLifecycle bridge tasks only (clarify has no Implement state). DEFERRED to later chunks (flagged, not silently dropped): (a) NO producer yet creates an `implement` Task off the tatara-implementation label - clarify flips the label + terminates but the label->implement-Task-creation is a Phase-6/scan concern, so the end-to-end handoff dead-ends until that lands; (b) cross-Task warm-resume FORK (a new implement Task forking clarify's ConversationObjectKey) is Phase 8 - for now Handover is populated on the clarify Task's status as the durable artifact; (c) kindProfiles triageIssue/issueLifecycle NOT dropped (bridge still in-flight; drop with Phase-6 bridge retirement). The issueLifecycle bridge is fully intact and drain-only. - 2026-07-07 (fix/memory-ready-debounce-gate) **Memory gate debounced: task/lifecycle/ingest spawn is now gated on `memoryStablyReady` (Phase==Ready AND ReadySince>=3min) instead of bare Phase==Ready, preventing herd-release on return-to-healthy or leader rotation.** Root cause: bare Phase==Ready check at 3 gate sites (task_controller.go, lifecycle.go, repository_controller.go) released ALL gated work at once when memory first transitioned to Ready, and a new leader reported memory Ready for ~3min before retrieval was confirmed. FIX: (1) `MemoryStatus.ReadySince *metav1.Time` field - set on Provisioning->Ready edge in `reconcileMemory`, cleared on leaving Ready, persists through Status().Update so it survives leader rotation. (2) `memoryStablyReady(p, now)` returns true only when Phase==Ready AND ReadySince!=nil AND age>=3min (mirrors the existing memoryRetrievalUnhealthyThreshold window). (3) All 3 gate sites now use memoryStablyReady. (4) BOY-SCOUT: generic gate in task_controller.go is now SPAWN-ONLY (task.Status.Phase=="" && !taskHasInflightTurn) - an in-flight turn keeps being supervised during a blip.
