- 2026-07-06 (issue #253) **The tool-surface probe now debounces a failing backend (3 consecutive unhealthy cycles) before metering, so the operator's own rollout churn no longer reports a still-serving chat backend as `unreachable` and trips the `> 0 for 15m` tool-surface alert.** Root cause: `updateToolSurfaceProbe` (project_tool_surface_probe.go) dials `chat /readyz` and the operator-write surface in-process on the 60s gauge cadence with a 3s timeout, and `probeToolSurfaceRoute` classifies ANY `httpc.Do` transport error as `unreachable`. During an operator self-deploy (deploy_timeout/cascade rerolls produced 3 ReplicaSet waves over ~1h), pods that were themselves starting up or shutting down emitted transient `unreachable` for a chat that was provably healthy the whole time (0 restarts, `/readyz` served 200 to the kubelet throughout, no chat error logs). The probe folds into no Project condition and gates no agent dispatch, so the ONLY impact was false-warning noise via the metric the alert reads directly. FIX (chose candidate direction #2 from the issue over #1 "suppress during startup/shutdown" and #3 "make the alert tolerant"): mirror the existing `memoryUnhealthyCycles`/`memoryRetrievalUnhealthyThreshold` debounce - new `toolSurfaceUnhealthyCycles map[string]int` (keyed by backend, serialised reconcile path, no mutex) + `toolSurfaceUnhealthyThreshold = 3`. `probeToolSurface`: a healthy result (ok/present) deletes the backend's run and meters immediately; an unhealthy result increments the run, is ALWAYS logged (now with a `consecutive` field), but is metered only once the run reaches 3. NON-OBVIOUS: unlike the memory sibling (which always meters raw and debounces only a CONDITION fold), the tool-surface metric IS the alert signal, so the debounce gates METRIC EMISSION itself (below threshold the cycle meters nothing - no ok, no failure - which the issue's "before metering unreachable" wording sanctions). Direction #1 was rejected as imprecise (detecting the pod's own outbound-startup window is fiddly; controller-runtime only reconciles post-cache-sync) and the debounce subsumes the shutdown case (a single ctx-cancel cycle is below threshold); direction #3 was rejected as masking rather than fixing signal fidelity. The debounce is per-backend so it also covers the `operator` self-probe. Metric labels unchanged, so the obs pre-seed (operator_metrics.go ~520) is untouched. Tests: 2 new (DebouncesTransientUnreachable via a closed httptest server -> unreachable; HealthyCycleResetsDebounce) + existing 4 unaffected (healthy results still meter cycle-1). build/vet/gofmt/golangci-lint + controller(full envtest)+obs suites green; -race NOT run locally (sandbox has no gcc; CI runs it). Branch tatara/fix-253-tool-surface-probe-reports-chat-backend.

- 2026-07-06 (feat/documentation-agent, operator half) **New `documentation` Task kind wired end-to-end (CRD, webhook trigger, pod per-kind table, writeback, reaper GC); ships inert.** Repo-scoped to a project's DOCS repo (not the merged component repo) - the inversion is deliberate so `writeBackOpenChange` opens the MR in the docs repo unchanged; the triggering component repo + before/after SHA ride as NEW Task annotations (`AnnSourceRepo`/`AnnSourceBaseSHA`/`AnnSourceHeadSHA`) rather than `Task.Spec.Source` (which is issue/PR-shaped, not push-shaped). Landed on top of the just-merged Batch-3 per-kind table simplification (pod.go `kindProfiles`/`branchKind`/`resolveByKind`), so this is one table row + a few kind-keyed switches, not new plumbing. THREE independent CEL gates on the same enum string (ModelByKind, EffortByKind, SpawnCeilingByKind) all needed `documentation` added to both their key-rule AND message, plus MaxProperties 9->10 each, plus the kubebuilder Task.Kind Enum separately - miss any one and the CRD rejects what Go accepts (verified via 2 new envtest CEL-acceptance tests). Model is LOCKED to claude-sonnet-5 for this kind specifically (modelForKind special-cases the fallback, not the project default) since a doc task is genuinely a Sonnet-tier job regardless of the project's general Model; ModelByKind can still override it. Documentation Tasks carry no Source (no issue/PR number) so the generic `TaskBranch`/`podNameSuffix`/`ConversationKey` SHA-key-vs-Number-key branches needed a `documentation`-specific arm (short source-head-SHA suffix) or every doc Task's pod/branch name would collide/genericize to `task-<name>`. scm.WebhookEvent gained `BaseSHA`/`HeadSHA` for push events (previously push parsed neither before/after SHA in either GitHub or GitLab payload parsers) - needed for the dedup key and the annotations. Webhook gate: `handlePush` now takes `*Project` (was just `projectName` string) so `maybeEnqueueDocumentation` can read `proj.Spec.Documentation` without a second Get; self-trigger guard compares the DOCS repo URL against the pushed repo via `scm.SameRemote`, and the docs repo must be an enrolled `Repository` CR (bot push access) or the event is silently dropped. Dedup key `doc-<sourceRepoName>-<headSHA>` so redelivery no-ops but a distinct merge always spawns. `derivePRTitle` and `branchKind` are independently-maintained switches (landmine, both updated: `docs(...)` title, `tatara/docs-<sha>` branch). Tests: 2 new files (`pod_documentation_test.go`, `documentation_test.go` in webhook) + additions across task_types/project_tiermap_validation/pod_profile/pr_title_derive/turnloop_skills/conversation_gc/scm github+gitlab tests. Awaiting: tatara-cli tool profile, tatara-agent-skills skill (both separate repos, unblocked to merge independently), then a tatara-helmfile MR to enroll the docs repo + flip `documentation.enabled` for the tatara Project. Design: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-05-documentation-agent-design.md (parent tatara repo) - note its line numbers were stale (predated the Batch-3 file splits), symbols were re-located by grep, not by line number.

- 2026-07-05 (issue #252) **The per-Project memory PrometheusRule now carries two postgres-LAYER alerts so the DB failure modes that cause the "Memory HTTP 5xx error ratio high" page are caught one hop upstream, before they surface as API 5xx.** Recurrence of the [[#238]]/#240 signature: write-path 503s on `/memories:bulk` (reads healthy) driven by a degraded `mem-tatara-pg` CNPG cluster - this time a standby (pg-3) permanently wedged after its replication slot was invalidated (`wal_removed`, the intended effect of #240's `max_slot_wal_keep_size`) then stuck on a diverged future timeline that CNPG would not re-clone. Root observability gap: the only memory alerts were on the tatara-memory API layer (`http_requests_total`/`up`), so every DB degradation was invisible until it became API 5xx - purely reactive. FIX (KISS, one file): `memoryAlertRules()` (internal/memory/monitoring.go) now takes `(cluster, namespace)` and appends `MemoryPostgresVolumeFilling` (a cnpg PVC - PGDATA or the dedicated 2Gi WAL volume - under 15% free for 5m; catches #238 disk exhaustion before WAL writes stall) and `MemoryPostgresInstanceRestarting` (a cnpg `container="postgres"` restarting >2x in 15m; catches the primary crash/failover thrash of #238/#240). NON-OBVIOUS - metric choice: both key off `kubelet_volume_stats_{available,capacity}_bytes` (kubelet) and `kube_pod_container_status_restarts_total` (kube-state-metrics), which are cluster-standard and VERIFIED present in Prometheus during triage, NOT `cnpg_*`. Reason: despite #238's `PGPodMonitor`, `list_prometheus_metric_names cnpg_.*` returned EMPTY and `up{namespace=tatara}` showed only chat/memory/operator jobs (no postgres target) - the cnpg scrape is not landing metrics (most likely the running operator predates #238; PodMonitor code is correct and wired at project_memory.go:109, so not churned). Alerting on absent `cnpg_*` series would be silently inert (hard rule 4), so replication-slot/streaming-standby alerting (the exact wedged-standby signature of #252) is DEFERRED to a follow-up gated on confirming cnpg_* metrics flow. Scoping: rules are per-Project, and several Projects' cnpg clusters (mem-tatara-pg, mem-infrastructure-pg) share namespace `tatara`, so each rule scopes series by `namespace=<ns>, {persistentvolumeclaim|pod}=~"<cluster>-.*"` (cluster = `mem-<proj>-pg`, pods/PVCs are `<cluster>-<n>[-wal]`). NOT DONE (out of repo/too risky, flagged as triage lever areas): auto-recovering a wedged invalidated-slot standby CNPG won't re-clone; retuning `max_slot_wal_keep_size` (= half WAL volume, ~1GB - aggressive on the 2Gi default but changing it re-opens the #240 disk-full tradeoff); tatara-memory API pods shipping no logs to Loki (separate repo). Tests: monitoring_test.go asserts both alerts present+warning and cluster/namespace-scoped exprs. Branch tatara/fix-252-memory-5xx-alert-recurs-mem-tatara-pg-st.

- 2026-07-05 (issue #236) **Infra-incident Tasks are now EXEMPT from the `Memory.Phase == Ready` admission gate, breaking the self-heal deadlock where an incident investigating the down memory stack was gated on that same stack.** Incident (same outage as [[#238]]): `mem-tatara-pg` filled its CephFS volumes with WAL -> memory stack below quorum -> project `tatara` memory phase not-Ready -> EVERY Task hard-gated at `task_controller.go` `Memory.Phase == Ready`. The operator DID fire the alert and DID create incident Task `incident-qe-qjbxl`, but that incident sat in Planning ~4h gated on the same down memory, so the self-heal agent never ran / never opened an issue. Circular dependency: infra-outage self-heal needs the subsystem that is down. FIX (option (a) from the issue, KISS): NEW `InfraIncidentExempt(spec)` + `AlertTargetsCoreInfra(alertRule)` in `api/v1alpha1/task_types.go` - an incident-kind Task whose `spec.AlertRule` (the alertname label) case-insensitively contains any of `infraIncidentKeywords` {memory, lightrag, postgres, cnpg, neo4j, pvc, cephfs, quorum, wal} bypasses the gate. Wired into the generic-path gate in `task_controller.go` (incident is project-scoped, NOT issueLifecycle, so it hits that gate, not the lifecycle.go:613 one): when memory is not Ready AND `InfraIncidentExempt`, log `action=task_memory_gate_bypass` + `Metrics.MemoryGateBypass(project,kind)` and fall through to spawn; ELSE gate as before. NEW counter `operator_memory_gate_bypass_total{project,kind}` (obs/operator_metrics.go) - nonzero rate = memory degraded + self-heal running through the bypass, worth alerting on. NON-OBVIOUS: the BuildPod call site (`task_controller.go`) dereferenced `project.Status.Memory.Endpoint` unconditionally, which the gate previously guaranteed non-nil; on the bypass path Memory can be nil/degraded, so it now derives `memEndpoint` guarded (empty when Memory==nil - fine, incident agents investigate via Grafana MCP, not the memory graph, so an unreachable/empty memory endpoint is acceptable). Only incident kind qualifies; all normal work keeps the gate. OUT OF SCOPE (issue "Also", separate repos): memory-independent human-notify escalation when `operator_memory_stacks{phase!=Ready}` persists, and the PVC-near-full/stack-stuck-not-ready root-cause alerts (already added in tatara-observability). Tests: api InfraIncidentExempt table (infra/non-infra/case-insensitive/non-incident/empty), controller envtest (infra incident reaches pollRequeue spawn path + counter==1 with memory NOT Ready; non-infra incident stays memGateRequeue + counter==0), obs metric. build/vet/golangci-lint(0) + api+obs+controller(envtest) green. Branch tatara/fix-236-incident-self-heal-deadlocks-infra-incid.

- 2026-07-05 (issue #238) **The per-Project CNPG postgres cluster now provisions a dedicated WAL volume and a PodMonitor, closing the disk-exhaustion write-outage and the DB observability blind spot behind the "Memory HTTP 5xx error ratio high" alert.** Incident: `mem-tatara-pg` PVCs (10Gi, single shared volume) filled to 100% (pg-1 99.6%, pg-2 100%) between ~07:30-08:50Z; a full data/WAL volume stopped Postgres writing WAL -> primary crash/restart loop + failovers -> memory API returned 503 "upstream temporarily unavailable" on the WRITE path `/memories:bulk` (~94% of bulk writes) while reads on replicas kept working. Asymmetric per-instance growth (pg-1/pg-2 high, pg-3 low) pointed at WAL accumulation on the shared PGDATA volume. Root cause in THIS repo: `internal/memory/pg.go` `PGCluster()` set only `StorageConfiguration.Size` - no separate `walStorage`, and no `spec.monitoring`, so there were ZERO `cnpg_*` metrics in Prometheus (disk/replication saturation invisible until the API 5xx'd). FIX (3 parts): (1) NEW `spec.memory.pgWalStorage` CRD field (`+kubebuilder:default="2Gi"`, api/v1alpha1/project_types.go) + `pgWalStorage(p)` helper + `defaultPgWalStorage="2Gi"` const (internal/memory/memory.go), wired to `ClusterSpec.WalStorage` so WAL lives on its OWN PVC isolated from PGDATA and is resized independently. (2) NEW `PGPodMonitor` builder (internal/memory/monitoring.go) selecting cnpg's per-pod label `cnpg.io/cluster=<cluster>`, scraping the container port named `metrics` (9187) `/metrics`, gated behind `cfg.MonitorEnabled` alongside the existing MemoryServiceMonitor/PrometheusRule in project_memory.go applyMemoryStack. NON-OBVIOUS: cnpg's built-in `spec.monitoring.enablePodMonitor` is DEPRECATED in cnpg v1.29.1 ("create a PodMonitor manually"), so a native PodMonitor is built instead to avoid tech-debt (rule 4); cnpg pods serve /metrics on 9187 regardless of spec.monitoring, so a manual PodMonitor works standalone. jobLabel left default (no alert keys off the cnpg `job` label; the memory alerts query `http_requests_total`, not `cnpg_*`). (3) CRD crd-bases regenerated with controller-gen v0.18.0 (templates/crds.yaml globs crd-bases at template time, no separate edit; deepcopy unchanged - string field). VERIFIED SAFE on the EXISTING cluster: the cnpg v1.29.1 webhook `validateWalStorageChange` returns nil when `old.Spec.WalStorage==nil` - adding walStorage to a cluster that never had it is permitted; only disabling/shrinking it later is rejected. OUT OF SCOPE (flagged on the issue, separate repo tatara-helmfile not in workspace): (a) the live mem-tatara PVCs were manually expanded ~10Gi->20Gi out-of-band ~12:00Z; helmfile's project-tatara `pgStorage` still declares 10Gi and cnpg REJECTS size decreases, so that value must be reconciled to 20Gi to avoid a reconcile conflict, and `pgWalStorage` optionally set explicitly for mem-tatara. (b) Optional hardening: cap WAL retained for replication slots via `postgresql.parameters.max_slot_wal_keep_size` so a stuck standby cannot fill the WAL volume unbounded (deferred - changes replica-recovery semantics, would force a stalled standby to re-clone). GOTCHA: applying walStorage to the existing degraded cluster triggers cnpg to create the WAL PVC and roll the pg pods to move pg_wal onto it - a brief rolling operation when the operator picks up the change. build/vet/gofmt/golangci-lint(0) + memory+api+controller(full envtest) suites green; the ONLY full-suite failure is the pre-existing `internal/config` `TestLoad_S3DefaultsOff` which the agent container's own `S3_*` runtime env vars contaminate (passes with those cleared; untouched by this change). - 2026-06-27 (#181) **Per-repo deterministic scan jitter spreads mrScan/issueScan fires across the cron interval, killing the synchronized top-of-hour fan-out that re-trips the "queue depth backlog" alert.** Root cause (live telemetry): all 5 infra repos x {issueScan,mrScan} (+brainstorm) share `0 * * * *`, so ~11 normal-class events land at `:00` on one FIFO pool (cap 5), depth jumps ~9->19 and stays >10 for ~30m, satisfying the rule's `for:30m`. A capacity bump (helmfile #72, 3->5) did NOT clear it - the lever is fan-out shape, owned by this repo. Fix (projectscan.go): `scanOffset(project,repo,activity,period)` = fnv32a hash mod period -> a stable per-(project,repo,activity) phase offset in [0,period); `cronPeriod` = interval between two consecutive cron fires (1h for hourly); `repoNextFire(sched,off,after)` = `sched.Next(after-off)+off` (phase-shifted next fire). New `reposDueForScan` returns the repos whose shifted fire is in the `(lastStamp, now]` window plus the soonest upcoming per-repo fire. NON-OBVIOUS / why this is stateless: it REUSES the existing project-level Last*Scan stamp - the stamp advances to `now` on every per-repo fire, so the (stamp, now] window slides and covers each repo's slot exactly once per period WITHOUT any new per-(repo) status field (the rejected alternative). runScans' mrScan/issueScan blocks now fire only `dueRepos` and requeue to the soonest slot. recoverOrphans + backstopSweep are gated behind `periodDue` (the OLD project-level activityDue boundary, computed pre-stamp) so per-repo jitter does NOT multiply the once-per-cycle recovery sweeps. brainstorm/healthCheck unchanged (per-project single events, not the herd). Empty-repo fallback: soonest = unshifted sched.Next(now) to avoid a 0-duration busy-loop requeue. activityDue refactored to share `activityScheduleAndLast`. Config stays a plain `0 * * * *`; offset is pure-hash so it is identical across operator restarts/pods (no rand, no wall clock). Options B (split review pool), C (per-project admitted metric label), D (burst-aware alert) from the issue are deliberately OUT of scope. - 2026-06-27 (#189) **Token-budget admission gate: pause proactive work at 50% / incidents at 80% of token usage within a reset window; off until enabled.** New `internal/budget` leaf package (pure decision engine, no k8s types, unit-tested in isolation) consumed by both the dispatcher (gate) and the turn-complete callback (accumulation). KEY MAPPING (non-obvious): the issue's two thresholds map onto the queue's EXISTING two pools, not a new taxonomy - the normal pool (QueueClassNormal: brainstorm/implement/review/issueLifecycle/...) is held at `ProactivePercent`, the alert pool (QueueClassAlert: kind=incident) only at the higher `EmergencyPercent`, evaluated independently so incidents keep flowing while proactive work is paused. `EmergencyBlocked` implies `ProactiveBlocked` because ResolvePercents orders emergency>=proactive. Two modes: customWindow (operator meters its own per-turn tokens - inputTotal incl. cache-read + output, the same delta behind operator_task_tokens_total - against an absolute TokenLimit) and claudeSubscription (gates on wrapper-reported Claude 5h/weekly percent). WINDOW SEMANTICS (non-obvious): the reset is driven PURELY by `resetSchedule` (a 5-field robfig cron, same parser as the scan crons) - `CurrentWindowStart` is the most-recent fire <= now; `windowDuration` does NOT drive the reset, it only BOUNDS the reset-boundary search to [now-2*duration, now] so a frequent cron isn't an unbounded scan (require it non-zero in customWindow). The accumulator (WindowStart+WindowTokens) lives on Project.Status.TokenBudget and `Roll` resets it to 0 when now crosses a new boundary, then adds. SUBSCRIPTION mode is INERT until the wrapper reports a snapshot whose reset is KNOWN and FUTURE-dated (`active = !reset.IsZero() && reset.After(now)`) - a zero/past reset is ignored so the gate can never get permanently stuck on a snapshot it can't expire (and the whole mode stays off until the cross-repo wrapper PR lands; the 5h/weekly limits are a Claude OAuth subscription feature, NOT the per-minute anthropic-ratelimit-* API headers). PER-TURN ACCUMULATION: recordUsage's signature changed to return (delta, recorded, err) so handleTurnComplete can call updateProjectBudget guarded by the SAME `recorded` flag as the per-Task accounting (a stale/duplicate callback never double-counts the window); one RetryOnConflict status write carries both the window roll and the subscription snapshot, behind a changed-guard (mirrors recordConversation). TRADEOFF ACCEPTED: ProjectReconciler has no GenerationChangedPredicate, so per-turn Project.Status writes DO trigger a Project reconcile - tolerated because turn-completes are low-frequency and the feature is opt-in; Project.Status is the home because the dispatcher already Gets the Project at admit time and reads the accumulator there. Config layers per-Project spec.tokenBudget over operator-wide TOKEN_BUDGET_* env defaults (a nil block inherits verbatim; a present block's `enabled` is authoritative); BudgetDefaults().Validate() fails Load fast on a bad enabled fleet default. Gauge operator_token_budget_used_ratio{scope=used|proactive|emergency} emitted ONLY when enabled (no series for disabled projects); counter operator_admission_blocked_total{class,reason="token_budget"}; budget-held pools requeue near the next cron boundary (budgetRequeueAfter: time-to-next-fire +1s, capped 5m; 60s fallback for no/bad schedule). Off until enabled (zero config disabled = admit path byte-for-byte unchanged, the [[#114]] backwards-compatible pattern). RBAC unchanged - projects/status update was already granted. - 2026-06-27 (#128) **The synthetic memory probe is now an AUTHENTICATED FUNCTIONAL check, not an unauthenticated route-presence ping - it closes the post-routing/auth blind spot that let MemoryReady stay green while every agent read 404'd.** Before, `probeMemoryRoute` sent no token and classified `404->absent`, transport-fail`->error`, and EVERY other status incl. `401` `->present`/healthy, so the whole failure class AFTER routing+auth (a memory-audience/OIDC misconfig that 401s every real token; a LightRAG/Neo4j backend that 5xxs real queries; a 200-with-broken-body after a bad re-ingest) was invisible - and this cycle `POST /queries`+`GET /code-graph/stats` DID 404 end-to-end for a research pod while the operator reported MemoryReady=true. (SP1) `probeMemoryRoute(ctx,httpc,method,url,body,token)` now sends `Authorization: Bearer` + (for POST) a JSON body and asserts HTTP 2xx + well-formed non-null JSON. NON-OBVIOUS mode choice: `naive` (NOT hybrid/local/global) - tatara-memory's `Service.Query` sends `OnlyNeedContext:true` so `/queries` is retrieval-only (no response LLM), and naive further skips the keyword-extraction LLM the graph modes make, so MemoryReady asserts the exact minimal contract every agent retrieval needs (auth->handler->query-embedding->vector store->JSON) WITHOUT coupling the health gate to response-LLM provider uptime or a per-probe LLM cost; the embedding dependency it DOES keep is correct (no retrieval works without it). (SP3) `operator_memory_retrieval_probe_total{route,result}` KEPT present/absent/error and ADDED `unauthorized` (401/403 = a valid token rejected -> auth/contract drift) and `degraded` (auth ok but 5xx OR malformed/empty/non-JSON body); only `present` (2xx+well-formed JSON) is healthy, all of absent/error/unauthorized/degraded count unhealthy. Pre-seed in `obs.NewOperatorMetrics` widened to the 5 results so the alert (#68) keying on this series lights up for the new classes for free. (SP4) UNCHANGED: 60s cadence + 3-consecutive-unhealthy (~3 min) MemoryReady fold at project_memory.go:250. Token-mint failure is metered `error` (unhealthy) and short-circuits the HTTP call (a token path the operator cannot use is, from here, indistinguishable from memory being unreachable; the 3-cycle fold rides out a transient mint blip). Nil `MemoryToken` (tests / unconfigured) sends no token -> memory 401 -> `unauthorized`/unhealthy by design (an operator that cannot authenticate to memory has no basis to report Ready - surface, do not hide). NEW BACKSTOP: `botHadLastWord(ctx, reader, candidate, botLogin)` (projectscan.go) reads the candidate's conversation timeline and returns true when the newest comment (by CreatedAt, robust to SCM list order) is the bot's, via shared `botIsLastCommenter([]IssueComment, botLogin)` (lifecycle.go's `botHasLastWord` refactored onto it). Fail-open (return false = do NOT suppress) on read error / empty botLogin / nil reader / unsplittable repo, matching humanCommentAfter and preserving missed-webhook recovery. KEY SAFETY (why this can't stall autonomous merge): the MRCI->Merge->MainCI flow is a SINGLE LIVE Task polling every 30s (`RequeueAfter=pollRequeue`), guarded by `hasLiveLifecycleTaskForIssue`; the gate only blocks RE-CREATION of an already-TERMINAL Task, never an in-flight one. MRCI posts a comment only on park/terminal (not on pending/success), so suppressing re-creation of a parked-with-comment bot PR ALSO avoids the bogus closeExhaustedPR-after-3 - the parked Task stays and a HUMAN comment reactivates it via the webhook (findReactivatableTask). - 2026-06-27 (#138) **TataraIngestJobFailing now alerts on a live current-state gauge with a `for:`, not the monotonic `operator_ingest_job_total` counter - it no longer mis-narrates a self-healed ingest burst for an hour.** The [[#135]] fix (mode={incremental|full} label + `increase(operator_ingest_job_total{result="failure",mode="full"}[1h])>0`) stopped *incremental* blips paging, but the alert was still recovery-BLIND: any full-ingest failure (or the incremental->full self-heal fallback) kept it firing for a full hour after ingest had already recovered, because `increase(counter[1h])` can't tell "currently broken" from "blipped and self-healed", and it had no `for:`/`repo` label. Maintainer (szymonrychu) approved the current-state-gauge direction. Fix (all operator-side): (1) new per-repo GaugeVec `operator_repository_ingest_failing{repo}` (obs/operator_metrics.go) = 1 when a Repository is currently failing, derived from status (Phase=="Failed" OR IngestFailureCount>0), plus `operator_repository_last_ingest_timestamp_seconds{repo}` from Status.LastIngestTime (staleness computed in PromQL as `time() - gauge`, the standard idiom - a snapshot timestamp doesn't go stale between sparse reconciles the way a baked age would). (2) `RepositoryReconciler.publishIngestHealth` (repository_controller.go) sets both every reconcile right after the Get, BEFORE the IngestEnabled guard, so a disabled repo reports failing=0 (never pages) and a recovered repo clears the instant handleFinishedJob resets Phase=Ingested/count=0 -> next reconcile sets gauge 0. (3) alert `TataraIngestJobFailing` re-expr'd to `operator_repository_ingest_failing > 0` `for: 15m` (15m comfortably clears the ~minutes-long incremental-retry+full-fallback self-heal window; consistent with TataraMemoryStackFailed's Phase=Failed gauge alert), annotation reworded to name `{{ $labels.repo }}` and stop asserting "cron not landing" on a recovered blip. (4) NEW companion alert `TataraIngestStale` = `(time() - operator_repository_last_ingest_timestamp_seconds) > {{ .Values.prometheusRule.ingestStaleAfterSeconds }}` `for: 30m` catches the silent "cron not landing, nothing actively failing" case the failing-gauge misses; threshold is a new chart value `prometheusRule.ingestStaleAfterSeconds` (default 93600s=26h, > the daily 0 6 * * * reingest cron; cluster-agnostic scalar per rule 6/14). The monotonic counter + its mode label STAY (still emitted; still feed the tatara-loop.json success-rate panel) - only the ALERT moved off it. BOY-SCOUT: the `repo` label resolves [[#135]]'s DEFERRED "name the stuck repo" item. CAVEAT (same as [[#135]]): the firing rule is the Grafana-managed mirror UID ffq4pikvg0q2ob; after this chart merges the Grafana copy must be re-synced from the PrometheusRule (infra/helmfile) for the new expr + the new TataraIngestStale rule to take effect. OUT OF SCOPE (maintainer-confirmed): root-causing the 3x transient incremental failures behind the original page. - 2026-06-27 (#129) **Push-metrics prefix allowlist was silently dropping 100% of the wrapper's families and the ingester's non-`ingest_` families; widened to the REAL pushed prefixes + added a regression-guard alert + a WARN-once receiver log.** Root cause (builds on the configurable-allowlist work in [[#46]]): the chart default `pushMetricsAllowedPrefixes` was `"wrapper_,agent_,memory_,ingest_"` - written from ASSUMED names. The wrapper pods actually push `ccw_*` (+ one `tatara_wrapper_internal_issue_total`) and the repo ingester pushes `ingest_*` plus `analyzer_*/semantic_*/scip_*/llm_*`; the receiver filters per metric family on prefix (`parseAndStamp` -> `hasAllowedPrefix`, receiver.go) and drops any non-match into `operator_push_series_dropped_total{reason="reserved_name"}`. (3) Cheap add: `parseAndStamp` now logs one WARN per affected push (`action="push_series_dropped"`, lists dropped family names + the active allowlist) via `slog` default (set in main) so an operator can fix the allowlist without reproducing the push. NON-OBVIOUS: chose to WIDEN the allowlist (option A) over RENAMING the wrapper/ingester metrics to allowed prefixes (option B) - rename is a breaking 2-repo change spanning dashboards/PromQL; widening is one cluster-agnostic scalar and unblocks all pushers immediately. Branch tatara/fix-129-push-metrics-prefix-allowlist-silently-d.

- 2026-06-27 (#168) **Wrapper HTTP 409 "session busy" on SubmitTurn is now transient backpressure, not a hard dispatch failure - stops the retry storm and the false TaskTurnSubmitFailureRatio alert.** Builds directly on [[#164]]'s `operator_turn_submit_total{kind,result,outcome}` split (result in ok|error|transient, granular outcome). #164 DELIBERATELY excluded 409 from the transient path on the assumption that "the wrapper flips Busy->Ready before firing its turn-complete callback, so a 409 on submit is unexpected"; production telemetry disproved it - ~94% of turn-submit failures were 409 (the operator's annCurrentTurn view races the wrapper's session release: callback-driven transition, recordTurn failing to persist annCurrentTurn, or an operator restart between SubmitTurn and recordTurn), so every 409 hit result="error" AND returned a hard `fmt.Errorf("submit ... turn")` -> controller-runtime backoff re-submitted -> tight 409 loop (e.g. one task 13x in 30s). Fix: new `agent.IsSessionBusy(err)` (session.go) matches `*HTTPError{Status:409}`; `handleTurnSubmitFailure` (task_controller.go) gains a 409 branch BEFORE handleTransientWrapper that requeues on `busyRequeue=15s` with NO reconcile error and counts result="transient" (outcome stays http_409). NON-OBVIOUS: 409 is NOT routed through handleTransientWrapper (the 503/425/UnreachableError path) on purpose - that path's annAgentUnreachableSince + agentBootDeadline(5m) termination is for a Ready-but-never-accepting-turns pod; a busy session is legitimately RUNNING a prior turn (could exceed 5m) and must not be killed for it. A session stuck busy forever is still bounded WITHOUT a new deadline: a turn-0 desync (annCurrentTurn=="") is failed by the existing planning-stall watchdog (PollOnce/expireStalledPlanning, planningStallDeadline=20m), an in-flight turn by the turn-timeout backstop. KNOWN LIMITATION (issue suggestion #3, NOT implemented - would need a new wrapper API to report its in-flight turn id, cross-repo): the turn-0 desync self-heals only by re-running turn-0 once the orphaned in-flight turn completes - that turn's callback hits resolveTaskByTurn's "unknown turn" 404 (turncallback.go:170, empty annCurrentTurn is skipped) and is dropped, losing its result; acceptable vs the storm, flagged for a follow-up that adopts the in-flight turn. New counter operator_agent_session_busy_requeue_total (mirrors operator_agent_boot_race_requeue_total; the requeue is reconcile-success, else invisible); turn_submit Help + the stale session.go 409 comment updated. Alert needs NO rule change - reclassifying 409 out of result="error" removes the false positive. Suggestion #4 (exclude UnreachableError boot-race from result="error") was ALREADY done by #164. Tests: agent TestIsSessionBusy (409/wrapped-409 true; 503/425/500/unreachable/nil/other false); controller TestTaskReconcile_WrapperHTTP409_RequeuesWithoutError (mirrors the 503 test: RequeueAfter==busyRequeue, no error, no turn recorded, busy-requeue counter==1, result=transient/outcome=http_409 >=1, result=error==0). go build ./... + golangci-lint (0 issues) + agent/obs/controller(envtest) tests green. Branch tatara/fix-168-operator-misclassifies-wrapper-409-sessi.

- 2026-06-27 (#161) **GitHub remove_label SCM-write failures are now observable AND the burst that drove the SCM-write-failure-ratio alert (0.69) self-heals via rate-limit-aware retry.** Two-part fix in internal/scm/github.go, both intentionally scoped to the scm package (controller untouched -> no envtest needed, see [[#154]]). (1) OBSERVABILITY: GitHub.RemoveLabel's non-404 error branch now emits `slog.WarnContext("github: remove label failed", provider, issue_ref, label, status=ErrorStatus(err), err)`. This failure is best-effort sibling cleanup that setLifecycleLabel (controller/labels.go) tolerates, so before this its ONLY trace was the operator_scm_writes_total{result="error"} increment - finding #6 of the issue: ~58 errors, ZERO queryable log lines. KEY DESIGN (mirrors [[#149]]): logged at WARN via slog (the scm package uses slog directly, which HAS a WARN level, unlike controller logr-over-slog which only has Info/Error) - NOT at ERROR, so it stays out of the `level="ERROR"` log-burst alert while being visible to the on-call `level=~"ERROR|WARN"` query. No new metric: status is ALREADY machine-readable via operator_scm_request_errors_by_status_total{provider,verb,status} (added in [[#163]]/c76a19c), and adding an http_status label to operator_scm_writes_total would change the write-failure-ratio alert math. (2) RESILIENCE: ghDo (the shared GitHub write path, so add_label + remove_label + create_issue etc. all benefit) now retries rate-limit rejections - 429, or 403 carrying Retry-After / X-RateLimit-Remaining:0 / a "rate limit" body - honoring Retry-After secs, else X-RateLimit-Reset epoch, else exp backoff 1s<<attempt + jitter (math/rand/v2 rand.N, de-correlates a concurrent burst). Bounded: ghMaxRetries=3, and a wait > ghMaxBackoff(16s) FAILS FAST (return error -> controller-runtime requeue) rather than blocking a worker goroutine. SAFETY: only rate-limit responses are retried because GitHub rejects them UNPROCESSED (side-effect-free re-send even for non-idempotent POSTs); 5xx is deliberately NOT retried (may have applied server-side -> could duplicate create_issue). Plain 403/401/404/422 carry no rate-limit signal so they still surface immediately (existing TestGitHubRemoveLabelRealErrorSurfaces with body "nope" unchanged). ghRetrySleep is a package var stubbed in tests for instant runs. DIAGNOSIS NOTE: the burst cause (secondary rate limit vs other) was UNCONFIRMED from telemetry (the whole point of the observability gap); the now-present status metric + WARN log will confirm it on recurrence. Did NOT add proactive global write-spacing/throttle (recommendation #3) - unconfirmed cause + KISS; reactive backoff is GitHub's documented mitigation and self-heals the burst. Tests: internal/scm/github_ratelimit_test.go (retry-then-succeed on Retry-After 403, 429 exhaust+surface, plain-403 no-retry, 5xx no-retry, long-Retry-After fail-fast, RemoveLabel end-to-end retry, RemoveLabel WARN-on-non-404 + silent-on-404). go build/vet ./... + golangci-lint ./internal/scm (0 issues) + scm/obs tests green. Branch tatara/fix-161-github-remove-label-scm-writes-fail-in-a.

- 2026-06-27 (#149) **Reaper conversation-GC no longer amplifies a store-wide object-store outage into an ERROR-log burst; it short-circuits the pass on a connection-level failure.** Root cause (see [[#114]] conv-gc): `gcConversations` (reaper.go) probes every key of every fully-closed batch with `ConvStore.Exists` (HeadObject) and, on ANY error, did `l.Error + Metrics.ConversationGC("error") + continue` - so a TCP dial-refused / retry-quota-exhausted RGW blip became one ERROR per backlog key (dozens) every reaper cycle and tripped the Grafana `>20 ERROR/5m` log-burst alert even though the operator was healthy and the dependency was the thing that failed (alert fired 2026-06-25, 57 ERRORs/5m, 100% `connection refused`). Fix: new pure classifier `objstore.IsUnavailable(err)` (internal/objstore/unavailable.go) detects store-wide/connection-level failures - `ratelimit.QuotaExceededError` (wrapped by the SDK's "failed to get rate limit token, %w"), `*net.DNSError`, dial errnos ECONNREFUSED/ECONNRESET/EHOSTUNREACH/ENETUNREACH via `errors.Is`, and any `net.Error` with `Timeout()` - while genuine per-object errors (NotFound/AccessDenied/single 5xx) return false so they still surface individually. gcConversations now wraps the batch loop with a `batchLoop:` label; on an `IsUnavailable` error from Exists OR Delete it calls `skipUnreachable(err)` (one log line + `Metrics.ConversationGC("unavailable")`) and `break batchLoop` - so one outage yields ONE line per pass, not dozens, and the next cycle retries once the store recovers. NON-OBVIOUS DECISION: the issue asked for a "single WARN", but controller code logs via logr-over-slog (`log.FromContext`, bridged in cmd/manager/logr.go) which has NO WARN level (logr only emits Info[+V] or Error; the package imports no slog - confirmed), so the skip is logged at INFO via `l.Info` (non-ERROR is the load-bearing property - it keeps the line out of the `level="ERROR"` burst query); the machine-readable signal for a dedicated/quieter alert is the NEW `operator_conversation_gc_total{result="unavailable"}` label (additive, separate from "error"; metric doc comment updated). No backoff added (KISS - one INFO/pass is cheap and self-heals; a persistently-down store just re-skips next cycle). Tests: objstore TestIsUnavailable (refused/reset/unreachable/quota/dns/timeout -> true; NotFound/AccessDenied/generic -> false) + controller TestGCConversations_SkipsPassWhenStoreUnreachable (unreachableConvGC returns ECONNREFUSED; asserts existsCalls==1 short-circuit, zero deletes, result="unavailable"==1, result="error"==0 via a registry-gather helper). go build/vet, golangci-lint (0 issues), objstore+controller(envtest)+obs tests green. Branch tatara/fix-149-reaper-conversation-gc-amplifies-a-trans.

- 2026-06-25 (#154) **GitHub.RemoveLabel now swallows a 404 "Label does not exist" so benign best-effort sibling-label removals stop counting as SCM write errors - fixes the false-positive TataraSCMWriteFailureRatioHigh alert from [[#133]].** setLifecycleLabel (controller/labels.go) enforces "exactly one of 6 managed phase labels" by removing the other 5 best-effort; its doc comment already promises RemoveLabel "tolerates the label being absent", but GitHub.RemoveLabel (scm/github.go) issued DELETE .../labels/{name} and surfaced GitHub's `404 {"message":"Label does not exist"}` as a hard error. recordSCM(provider,"remove_label",err) then logged result="error" for every absent sibling (~5/reconcile), driving operator_scm_writes_total{verb="remove_label",result="error"} to dominate the ratio (~0.82) while every functionally meaningful write (add_label/comment/create_issue/approve/close_issue) succeeded - the alert was firing on healthy state AND blind to a real outage. Fix (the robust option #1 of three the issue listed): RemoveLabel now `errors.As(err,&he) && he.Status==http.StatusNotFound -> return nil`, mirroring GitLab.RemoveLabel's idempotent `PUT ...?remove_labels=` (which never 404s) and the existing 404-tolerant patterns in gitlab.go:537/547. Real failures (401/403/5xx/network) still return and still count. SCOPED OUT (#3 in the issue, the controller `known`-guard reliability fix so known-absent siblings aren't blindly DELETEd each reconcile): the load-bearing fix is #1 (the closed-issue / list-error fallback path relies on it regardless), and a behavioral change to the reconcile path could NOT be verified in the pod (controller envtest needs /usr/local/kubebuilder/bin/etcd which is absent; `make test` provisions it via setup-envtest in CI). Tests (scm/github_writeback_test.go): RemoveLabel happy-path DELETE, absent-label 404 -> nil (with tatara/approved URL-escape assertion), and 401/403/500 still surface as *HTTPError. go test ./internal/scm + vet + golangci-lint green; controller package compiles (TestMain envtest panic is the missing-etcd harness limit, not a regression).

- 2026-06-24 (#135) **operator_ingest_job_total gained a `mode={incremental|full}` label so the TataraIngestJobFailing alert stops paging on the benign incremental->full self-heal.** A repo whose incremental (`--since`) ingest fails is retried up to incrementalFallbackThreshold=3 (each a BackoffLimit=0 Job that increments `result="failure"`) then falls back to a full ingest that succeeds; the old `{result}`-only counter could not tell that self-heal from a stuck repo, so a single fallback burst tripped the `increase(...{result="failure"}[1h])>0` warning. Fix: BuildJob stamps Job label `tatara.dev/ingest-mode` (ingest.LabelIngestMode; incremental when since!="", else full) on both Job + Pod template; handleFinishedJob reads it back and passes mode to IngestJobResult(result, mode) on BOTH success and failure paths; empty/absent label (a Job in-flight across the rollout) defaults to `full` = fail-loud (page rather than silently drop an unclassifiable failure). Alert expr re-targeted to `increase(operator_ingest_job_total{result="failure", mode="full"}[1h]) > 0` - a failed *full* ingest (first/scheduled full, or the self-heal fallback) is the genuine "graph going stale" signal; transient incremental failures no longer page. Zero-init loop now seeds result x mode (4 series). DEFERRED (not in scope, noted for maintainer): a bounded `repo` label so the alert names the stuck repo (held to keep zero-init clean; Loki runbook already surfaces it), and preserving the last failed ingest Job past its 600s TTL for forensics. CAVEAT: the firing alert is the Grafana-managed mirror (UID ffq4pikvg0q2ob); after this chart merges the Grafana copy must be re-synced from the PrometheusRule (infra/helmfile) for the new expr to take effect. Dashboard success-rate panel left as-is (its unfiltered sum() aggregates correctly over the new label). Tests: job_test ingest-mode label (incremental/full, Job+Pod), operator_metrics_test mode-attributed counts; go test obs/ingest/controller (envtest) + golangci-lint green.

- 2026-06-22 (feat/brainstorm-throughput O1) **Queued-autonomous budget removed; queue bounds CONCURRENCY only.** `remaining *int` param removed from `mrScan`, `issueScan`, `brainstorm`, `healthCheck`, `recoverOrphans`; budget computation block (`QueuedAutonomousCap() - queuedAutonomousCount`) and re-list recompute removed from `runScans`; all `*remaining <= 0` guards and `*remaining--` decrements deleted; `skipped_budget` metric gone. `MaxOpenTasks` and `Queue.QueuedAutonomousCap` fields deprecated in doc comment (retained for CRD backward-compat, ignored at runtime). `recoverOrphans` now always runs after `issueScan` (was gated on `remaining > 0`). healthCheck dedup key is `"healthCheck-" + proj.Name` (constant per-project, correct - no change needed). Tests updated: old `skipped_budget` / cap-truncation assertions replaced with enqueue-all assertions.

- 2026-06-20 (issue #75) **Project CRD gained `spec.agent.hooks` (lifecycle hooks) + `spec.agent.extra*` (pod-shaping).** New `LifecycleHooks` struct (preClone/postClone/conversationStart/conversationRestart/agentTurnFinished/conversationFinished, all optional command strings) on AgentSpec, plus `extraEnvs []corev1.EnvVar`, `extraEnvsFrom []corev1.EnvFromSource`, `extraVolumeMounts []corev1.VolumeMount`, `extraVolumes []corev1.Volume`, `extraSidecarContainers/extraInitContainers []corev1.Container`. DECISIONS: (1) both groups live under AgentSpec because BuildPod is agent-pod-scoped (reads project.Spec.Agent.* throughout); using upstream corev1 types keeps the schema honest (controller-gen embeds the full container/volume schemas, so the projects CRD base grew ~5.7k lines - expected). (2) BuildPod (internal/agent/pod.go) emits one `HOOK_<NAME>` env var per NON-EMPTY hook (guarded on Hooks != nil); extraEnvs are appended LAST, after every operator-set var incl. TATARA_REPOS, so a stray extra named like a required var cannot shadow it (a later dup in a Pod env list does not override an earlier one). extraEnvsFrom->container EnvFrom, extraVolumeMounts->container, extraVolumes->pod, extraSidecarContainers appended after the wrapper (wrapper stays index 0), extraInitContainers->pod InitContainers. (3) hooks are CRD-driven, NOT wrapper-chart values, so no values.yaml plain-env/list rule applies. The wrapper executes them best-effort (see tatara-claude-code-wrapper MEMORY). controller-gen v0.18.0 regenerated zz_generated.deepcopy.go + chart crd-bases. Tests in project_types_test.go/types_fields_test.go/pod_test.go. Branch tatara/task-scan-qe-fg78m.

- 2026-06-20 (feat/agent-work-queue) **Seq allocator is PER-PROJECT DURABLE (per-project ConfigMap CAS); supersedes bot PR #86 in-memory allocator.** #86 made seq per-project but kept it in-memory with a leader-gated SeqRecoverer + ErrSeqNotReady - did NOT fix the multi-replica race (webhook runs on every replica with its own map; followers collide or 503). New `queue.SeqSource{Client,Namespace}.Next(ctx,project)` stores each project's counter in ConfigMap `queue-seq-<sanitized-project>` (data key `next`), allocated via `retry.RetryOnConflict` CAS: Get/parse/+1/Update; NotFound->Create next=1 (Create AlreadyExists -> synthetic Conflict to re-Get winner); empty/missing key = 0 (->alloc 1); PRESENT-but-unparseable = hard error (not swallowed). Any replica allocates safely, no leader dep, no in-memory state. CM is UNOWNED on purpose: ProjectReconciler+RepositoryReconciler both `Owns(&corev1.ConfigMap{})`, so an owned seq CM would fire a reconcile on every CAS Update (storm); Owns filters by ownerRef so an unowned CM is ignored. Tradeoff: seq CM orphaned on Project delete (stale counter at most), no finalizer. Backoff = custom 30-step (not retry.DefaultRetry's 5) so per-project CAS contention doesn't surface spurious Conflicts. Deleted: in-memory SeqAllocator/RecoverProject/MarkReady/SeqRecoverer/ErrSeqNotReady. Re-applied on top: stale-terminal name-collision delete+requeue (admit returns requeue bool -> Reconcile RequeueAfter 1s; pool loop `continue` so siblings not abandoned), project-scoped queue gauges {project,class}, isQueued empty-state heal, reconcileDone GC-deletes Done QE, 30s at-capacity backstop, CooldownSeconds deprecate doc. Full -race suite + lint green; NOT yet merged/deployed.

- 2026-06-19 (#42) **Turn timeout is now a STALL (inactivity) deadline, not a fixed wall-clock cap.** `turnTimedOut` (turncallback.go) gained a `lastActivityRaw` arg and anchors the deadline on `max(turn-started-at, turn-last-activity-at)` + grace; both call sites (`CallbackServer.isTurnTimedOut`, `TaskReconciler.isTurnTimedOut`) pass `annTurnLastActivity`. It falls back to start-only when the activity stamp is empty/unparseable so the bound is never lost (wrapper unreachable). New annotation `AnnTurnLastActivity = tatara.dev/turn-last-activity-at`: the poll backstop OWNS it (refreshed in `PollOnce` from `TurnResult.LastActivityAt`, which `GetTurn`/http.go now deserializes from the wrapper's `lastActivityAt`); the reconcile path only READS it (same shape as turn-started-at). Freshness is bounded by `pollRequeue`=30s / `pollGetTurnTimeout`=5s, fine for a minute-scale window. The stamp is cleared everywhere the other turn annotations are reset (recordTurn new-turn, expireTimedOutTurn, lifecycle reset, webhook reactivation) so it never leaks into the next turn. `turnTimeoutSeconds` field name kept (CRD contract); its doc comment + `operator_turn_timeout_total` Help now say "stall/inactivity". This is the COMPANION to the wrapper change (tatara-claude-code-wrapper #42): the wrapper enforces its own `AfterFunc(TurnTimeout)` reset-on-activity and exposes `lastActivityAt`; the wrapper timer fires first (operator backstop is +60s on the same TURN_TIMEOUT_SECONDS), so the operator change alone would not have fixed it - but without the operator change the +60s backstop would re-kill the productive turns the wrapper now protects.

- 2026-06-16 (fix/audit-2026-06-15, review) **Callback HMAC secret delivered via SecretKeyRef + chart-wired.** Review fix: the r3 HMAC fix injected CALLBACK_HMAC_SECRET into wrapper Pods as a literal env Value (leaked the shared secret into every Pod spec/etcd, contradicting the secretEnv pattern used for every other agent secret and hard rule 6) AND had NO chart wiring (no values key / Secret / envFrom), so the security feature was entirely dormant - the "trust gap closed" claim was false in any real deploy. Fix: new `callbackHmacSecretName`/`callbackHmacSecret` values render a managed Secret (key `callback-hmac-secret`); operator reads CALLBACK_HMAC_SECRET via SecretKeyRef (deployment env) for verification, wrapper Pods reference it via SecretKeyRef (CALLBACK_HMAC_SECRET_NAME). Empty = HMAC disabled, NetworkPolicy remains sole control. Wrapper-side signing of X-Tatara-Signature is still a tatara-claude-code-wrapper change, gate before enabling.

- 2026-06-16 (fix/audit-2026-06-15) **Metrics server unauthenticated /metrics - INTENTIONAL, NetworkPolicy is the sole control.** `metricsserver.Options` binds plain HTTP on `:9090` with no RBAC filter (`filters.WithAuthenticationAndAuthorization` not set). Threat model: /metrics is an internal-only bind, protected by cluster NetworkPolicy limiting access to the Prometheus scraper Service Account. Adding kube-rbac-proxy or the controller-runtime auth filter would require additional RBAC bindings and a sidecar or TLS cert, which adds complexity disproportionate to the risk on a pod-network-only endpoint. Decision reviewed and accepted per hard rule 4. Revisit if the operator gains an external-facing ingress or the NetworkPolicy is relaxed.

- 2026-06-16 (fix/audit-2026-06-15) **Empty agentScheduling = unconstrained pod placement.** The agent package and chart are correct (cluster-specific scheduling is helmfile-supplied per rule 14). An empty agentScheduling (the chart default) means no nodeSelector/tolerations/affinity on spawned wrapper pods - they can land on control-plane nodes. The tatara-helmfile MUST set agentScheduling with a nodeSelector or toleration omission to repel control-plane taints. See MEMORY global: agent-pods-unbounded-control-plane.

- 2026-06-16 (fix/audit-2026-06-15) **Webhook audit fixes (7 findings).** Fixes applied to `internal/webhook/server.go`: (1) HIGH panic on GitLab MR IssueRef - `strings.LastIndex("#")` returned -1 for `group/proj!N`; replaced with `strings.LastIndexAny("#!")` via new `issueRefRepoSlug` helper (3 sites). (2) MEDIUM TOCTOU duplicate create - `GenerateName` let concurrent deliveries both succeed; switched issueLifecycle to deterministic `issueLifecycleTaskName` (SHA-256 of projectName+issueRef), treat `AlreadyExists` as duplicate. (3) MEDIUM empty webhookSecret accepted - added `len(v)==0` guard (same path as missing-key). (4) MEDIUM GitLab MR kind misclassified as issueLifecycle when bot is actor - restricted `AuthorLogin==bot` branch to `provider=="github"` only (GitLab actor!=author; authoritative gate stays in GetPRState per scm-author-vs-actor-egress-gate). (5) LOW replay protection absent - ACCEPTED RISK, documented here per hard rule 4; no delivery-id dedup, window attack feasible for issue_comment re-queue/re-activate; mitigated by idempotency of most paths; full dedup needs in-memory LRU or ConfigMap store (out of scope this cycle). (6) LOW label-unfiltered List - added `MatchingLabels` to dedup query in `handleWorkItem` and to `findLifecycleTask`/`findReactivatableTask` via `taskListOpts`. (7) LOW nil Metrics - panic in `NewServer` with clear message if `cfg.Metrics==nil` (consistent with explicit requirement contract, mirrors how nil Logger is handled via a default). All covered by new tests in `audit_fixes_test.go`.

Past decisions and their context. One line per entry, dated. Append-only
in spirit; prune only when a decision is reversed.

- 2026-06-15 (feat/project-level-brainstorm) **Brainstorm is now PROJECT-LEVEL (one Task per project per cycle).** Old: one brainstorm Task per repo per cycle (O(#repos) creates). New: one Task per cycle for the whole project. Three guards: (1) project-scoped in-flight: ANY non-terminal brainstorm Task blocks (`brainstormInFlightProject`, drops RepositoryRef clause); (2) summed backlog across repos with short-circuit once total >= maxProp (avoids extra SCM calls); (3) shared budget as before. Primary repo for pod/branch stamping: deterministic sort by Task CR name (alphabetically first valid slug). Goal text changed: `brainstormGoalProject(slugs)` instructs agent to survey ALL repos (available via TATARA_REPOS in the pod) and call `propose_issue` with the chosen target `repo` arg. Old `brainstormGoal(slug)` kept as compat wrapper -> delegates to `brainstormGoalProject`. CRD: `MaxOpenProposals` default bumped 3->5, doc updated to "across ALL repos in the project". CRD manifests regenerated. `brainstormInFlight(existing, repoName)` per-repo helper removed (was unused after the refactor). PR: feat/project-level-brainstorm.

- 2026-06-14 (#29) **tatara_lifecycle_state gauge recomputed from cluster state (no more deltas).** The gauge was maintained ONLY by `AddLifecycleState(from,-1)/+(to,1)` deltas in `setLifecycleState` (lifecycle.go), so every operator restart (set-image deploy, replicas=1) reset it to 0 and the first post-restart transition drove the `from` series NEGATIVE, while GC'd terminal Tasks (e.g. the MaxOpenTasks 40-Task purge) left `Done/Stopped/Parked` monotonically climbing. FIX (mirrors the `updateMemoryStackCounts`/`SetMemoryStackCounts` precedent the team already adopted for `operator_memory_stacks`): new `ProjectReconciler.updateLifecycleStateCounts` lists every Task, counts `Status.LifecycleState` for `Kind=="issueLifecycle"`, and `Set`s ALL 9 known states (`lifecycleStates` var: Triage/Implement/Conversation/MRCI/Merge/MainCI/Done/Stopped/Parked) including 0 for drained states, so an emptied state reads 0 not its last value. Called from `Reconcile` right after `updateMemoryStackCounts` (hourly + 60s backlogRequeue cadence; runs regardless of cron config, unlike runScans which early-returns on nil Scm/Cron/ReaderFor). Maintainer go-ahead on all 3 open Qs: (1) home in ProjectReconciler next to the precedent, (2) DROP the per-transition deltas entirely - the absolute `Set` is the single source of truth, staleness bounded to <=60s, and `tatara_lifecycle_transition_total` already gives per-event resolution, (3) explicit `Kind` filter so no `state=""` series. Dead `AddLifecycleState` method removed (no callers left). `LifecycleMetrics` field added to ProjectReconciler + wired in wire.go. TDD: TestUpdateLifecycleStateCounts_RecomputeCorrectsSkewedGauge skews a state high, one negative, one terminal, asserts recompute converges every state to truth (zeros included) and a non-issueLifecycle Task in a lifecycle state is NOT counted. Full `go test ./...` green.
- 2026-06-14 **Push-metrics receiver for short-lived wrapper pods (tatara-operator#42 B1).** New `internal/pushmetrics` package: a `Receiver` that is both an HTTP push endpoint and an unchecked `prometheus.Collector`. Wrappers POST their /metrics text to `POST /internal/metrics/push?run_id=&pod=&job=` on the INTERNAL_ADDR listener (not ingress, no OIDC, mounted alongside the turn-complete callback in `turncallback.go`); the receiver parses the text (`expfmt.NewTextParser(model.UTF8Validation)` - the zero-value TextParser PANICS in common v0.67 because NameValidationScheme is unset), force-stamps run_id/pod/job identity labels on every series (so a run can't spoof another's identity), and keys the snapshot by run_id. `Collect` re-exposes all live runs on the operator's own /metrics (registered on `ctrlmetrics.Registry` in main.go) and is union-label-padded per metric name so two runs pushing the same metric with different label sets gather cleanly instead of erroring the whole scrape; `Describe` sends NOTHING (required to register as an unchecked collector that may emit arbitrary wrapper-chosen descriptors). TTL eviction (config `PUSH_METRICS_TTL`, default 5m) ages out a hard-killed pod's series at Collect time; DELETE on the same path is the wrapper's best-effort graceful cleanup. Self-metrics: `operator_pushed_runs` gauge, `operator_push_receive_total{result}`, `operator_pushed_runs_evicted_total`. Deliberately NOT the upstream Pushgateway (no expiry = silent-staleness footgun). The human approved the issue's proposed-default design with "go". REMAINING (subtasks, separate PRs): B2 wrapper-side push client in tatara-claude-code-wrapper, B3 per-repo instrumentation gaps for the long-lived services. TDD, gofmt/lint/`go test ./...` all green.
- 2026-06-14 **Operator instrumentation gaps filled (tatara-operator#42 B3, operator PR).** Fleet-audit found the operator's happy-path was well-metered but several silent failure/timeout paths in background reconcile/scan/callback loops had NO metric (they never surface as HTTP errors). Added three counters to OperatorMetrics (obs/operator_metrics.go): `operator_turn_timeout_total{source}` (source=reconcile|poll_backstop) wired at task_controller.go isTurnTimedOut and turncallback.go poll backstop; `operator_ingest_job_total{result}` (success|failure) wired at repository_controller.go handleFinishedJob both branches (pairs with the existing duration histogram which only fires on success); `operator_agent_unreachable_termination_total` wired at task_controller.go handleAgentUnreachable boot-deadline termination. Label combos pre-initialised. obs unit tests added; controller envtest suite + lint + gofmt green. AUDIT FOLLOW-UPS (not done, lower value / spread across many call sites - candidates for a later PR): REST API handler outcome counter, agent SubmitTurn/Interject error counters, scan-loop SCM read-error counter, memory-provision failure counter, conflict-retry counter, wrapper pod/svc cleanup counter. tatara-chat audit: HTTP+domain metrics already solid; remaining gaps are store-layer durations whose failures already surface as HTTP 500s (lower value) - separate subtask. tatara-memory-repo-ingester: ZERO metrics but it is a run-to-completion Job (pull-scraping not viable) - needs a push-vs-pull design decision (issue says pull, but a Job can't be reliably scraped; B1 push receiver is the natural fit) - separate subtask, NOT self-implemented. tatara-memory: confirmed complete baseline, no change.
- 2026-06-14 **Wrapper push-metrics env wiring (tatara-operator#42 B2, operator side).** `BuildPod` (internal/agent/pod.go) now sets three env vars so the short-lived wrapper Pod can push its /metrics to the B1 receiver: `OPERATOR_PUSH_URL` = `TrimSuffix(cfg.CallbackURL,"/") + "/internal/metrics/push"` (same internal listener as the turn-complete callback), and `RUN_ID` = `POD_NAME` = `PodName(task)` (the wrapper Pod name; one pod per run, so it is the run identity - successive runs of a task reuse the name but never run concurrently, and the old pod's series are DELETE'd on graceful exit or TTL'd otherwise). The wrapper-side client lives in tatara-claude-code-wrapper (`internal/pushclient`).
- 2026-06-14 **mise toolchain rollout (chore/mise-toolchain).** .mise.toml added (go 1.26.3, golangci-lint 2.12.2, helm 4.2.1; min_version 2026.6.3; tasks lint/test/build -> make). Same step kept in lint/build jobs to match origin/main baseline.

- 2026-06-14 **Issue/MR comments interrupt the agent nursing them (tatara-operator#25).** New `Status.PendingInterjections []string`. Webhook `handleIssueComment` (server.go) now also routes MR comments (intercept on `ev.Action=="created"`, dropping the `!IsPR` gate): when the live task has a turn in flight (`taskHasInflightTurn`: current-turn set, turn-complete unset) it queues the COMMENT text (new `WebhookEvent.CommentBody`, surfaced from GitHub `comment.body` / GitLab note `object_attributes.note`) onto PendingInterjections (capped 20) instead of bumping the deadline; idle tasks keep the re-triage path; no-live-task now reactivates Parked OR creates a fresh Triage task for MRs too. Reconciler drains PendingInterjections at the top of `reconcileLifecycle` (mirrors PendingComments): in-flight -> `Session.Interject` each -> wrapper `POST /v1/interject` -> live PTY; UnreachableError retains+retries, no in-flight turn drops the stale queue. All TDD, lint+test green.

- 2026-06-14 **Brainstorm follow-up no longer interrogates; brainstorm yield is honest.** Two fixes shipped with the starvation fix. (1) FOLLOW-UP SILENCE: the issueLifecycle discuss arm (`finishTriage`, lifecycle.go) now gates `triagePostComment` on `tataraAuthoredIssue && hasHumanComment` - a bot-authored issue with no human reply gets NO repeated "still awaiting go-ahead" comment (live bug: tatara-operator#29 got 3 near-identical re-asks ~1h apart). `lifecycleTriageText` (turnloop.go) prompt softened to emit `action=discuss` with empty comment + NOT use the comment tool when no human replied. Fail-open on check errors; human-replied + human-filed paths still always comment. The silently-held task idles to the 60min Conversation deadline -> Stopped (no loop). (2) PROPOSE HONESTY: `brainstormGoal` (projectscan.go) now mandates `propose_issue` + single-decision framing (no open-questions list); writeback (writeback.go) sets reason `BrainstormProposed` ONLY when `brainstormHasProposal` finds a proposal child Task (spec.proposedIssue + same project/repo) created at/after THIS brainstorm run (creation-time scoped, since proposals carry no per-run linkage), else neutral `BrainstormComplete` - so the >50% no-yield rate is no longer masked. All TDD, opus-reviewed (1 medium = per-run scoping, fixed), make test green. NOTE: the deep-research SKILL itself is still unbuilt (designed only) - the goal names it but the wrapper image ships no such skill; building it is the remaining depth fix.
- 2026-06-14 **Brainstorm starvation FIXED (option A): Conversation excluded from creation budget.** `taskOpen()` now returns false for `LifecycleState=="Conversation"` (awaiting-human). Previously 3 Conversation issueLifecycle tasks (maxOpenTasks=3) drove budget=0 every hourly fire -> 0 new brainstorm tasks in 6h. Conversation is externally gated so it must not consume an autonomous concurrency slot. TaskActive (concurrency cap, fix #30) is unchanged - that uses a separate predicate. TDD: TestTaskOpen_TerminalPhases added Conversation cases, TestOpenTaskCount_ConversationExcluded validates the starvation scenario end-to-end. All green make test.
- 2026-06-14 **Concurrency-cap deadlock FIXED (live incident: operator stopped processing).** `atConcurrencyCap` (task_controller.go) counted tasks toward the per-Project cap by `isActive(phase)` (Planning/Running) only, NOT excluding terminal lifecycleState - unlike `taskOpen`/`laneOccupancy`, which both use `isLifecycleTerminal` (Done/Stopped/Parked). When a Task gives up at maxIterations, `setLifecycleState` flips LifecycleState=Parked but LEAVES Status.Phase=="Planning" (+ leaves the wrapper pod running). So 3 Parked-but-Planning zombies (scan-6g447, task-h8p6d, task-nvzr2) permanently counted as 3 active -> every new task "gated at concurrency cap" forever -> operator processed nothing. FIX: new `taskActive(t)=isActive(phase) && !isLifecycleTerminal(lc)`; `atConcurrencyCap` + `updateInflightGauge` (boy-scout: same latent phase-only bug, was over-counting the inflight gauge) both use it. TDD (TestTaskActive_ExcludesTerminalLifecycle), opus-reviewed, make test green. Operationally unblocked live by patching the 3 zombies `phase=Failed` + deleting their idle pods (cap freed, processing resumed). FOLLOW-UP (NOT fixed): a Park/terminal transition does NOT tear down the wrapper Pod+Service -> idle zombie pods leak (had to manually delete; also seen for Succeeded tasks). With the cap fix they no longer deadlock, but terminal-lifecycle should delete pod+svc. SEPARATE same-incident regression (fixed elsewhere): the wrapper agent.image was bumped to the CHART tag `0.0.0-468668a`; container tag is bare `468668a` -> agents ImagePullBackOff'd (tatara-helmfile PR #3 corrected it).
- 2026-06-13 (deployed 306f596, set-image) **Phase-label dedup + orphan-recovery (presence+state, Option A).** Fixes duplicate-assignment + orphaned-MR. Four operator-managed phase labels (tatara-brainstorming/-approved/-implementation/-declined) = issue state-of-truth, set at lifecycle state ENTRY (brainstorming on Triage, approved on finishTriage-implement, implementation on Implement entry, declined on triage-close; issue sources only, skip PRs - ensurePhaseLabel in lifecycle.go). Dedup + backstop key on label PRESENCE + Task STATE, NOT label-added-time: the approved spec's label-time-vs-task-creation rule (+ new IssueLabelAddedAt) was WITHDRAWN because a Task always predates the labels it sets, so it re-spawned a duplicate triage on every orphaned terminal Task (see [[phase-label-dedup-presence-not-time]]). isDeduped(c,existing,managed) issue arm: non-terminal Task=active (fast path unchanged); only-terminal + any managed label present=orphan->dedup; no managed label->fallback updatedAt-vs-creation. Backstop recoverOrphans (runScans after issueScan, gated budget>0): re-lists Tasks (sees same-cycle mrScan MRCI tasks for open MRs so an open bot MR is not double-recovered), per OPEN issue with an active label + no live Task starts the right entry (implementation/approved->Implement, brainstorming/idea->Triage, declined->skip), MaxOpenTasks-bounded. Webhook handleIssueComment: a human comment on an issue whose only owning Task is Parked REACTIVATES it (clean reset: Phase="", 5 turn annotations cleared via shared api/v1alpha1.AnnCurrentTurn consts, pod+svc deleted) instead of duplicating; Done/none create fresh. Lazy legacy migration: managedPhaseLabels includes tatara-idea/-rejected so setLifecycleLabel strips them on next egress + dedup/backstop treat legacy idea as active - no migration job. Built via Workflow (5-task sequential subagent-driven TDD: sonnet impl + opus review per task + final review); all green (go test ./..., golangci-lint 0). Merged operator main 306f596 (clean auto-merge over bot #24/#26). Deployed push->CI->set-image (helm clean-apply STILL blocked on tatara-scm SSA token). Spec+plan in parent tatara repo docs/superpowers/{specs/2026-06-13-tatara-phase-label-dedup-design.md AMENDMENT, plans/2026-06-13-tatara-phase-label-dedup.md}. Live: pod 306f596 healthy 0-restart, cap+lifecycle working, zero errors; backstop gated while at cap=3, so label/backstop behavior verifies on the next hourly issueScan once budget frees. KNOWN cosmetic: proposalBacklog doc comment still says "idea label" (function counts brainstorming+legacy idea) - optional cleanup.
- 2026-06-13 (deployed d045a9d) **Issue close is now gated: never close an issue that has an unmerged change.** Bug: tatara closed issues whose MR was unmerged/conflicting + main CI not green. Root cause (workflow-investigated): two AGENT-driven close paths fired writer.CloseIssue with zero merge/CI guard - finishTriage close arm -> triageCloseIssue (lifecycle.go) and writeBackIssue close arm (writeback.go, triageIssue kind), both from the agent's issue_outcome=close. The demonstrated incident is the issueLifecycle RE-TRIAGE path: handleIssueComment resets a task that already has an open/conflicting MR back to Triage; the agent re-triages and emits close; the old code closed the issue, orphaning the unmerged MR. The ONLY correct close is handleMainCI (MergeCommitSHA recorded on a successful Merge + that commit's main CI == "success"). FIX: hasUnmergedChange(task) = PrURL!="" || HeadBranch!=""; both agent-close paths now WITHHOLD the close when it's true (finishTriage routes to Conversation as tatara-idea + posts a "not closing - unmerged change" comment; writeBackIssue clears writeback with CloseWithheldUnmerged); triageCloseIssue also has a defensive guard. A pure triage REJECT (no code artifact) still closes + labels tatara-rejected - that is not an unmerged-code case. handleMainCI (the merged+green close) is unchanged. NOTE (not fixed, low-prob): handleMainCI trusts MergeCommitSHA + the commit's main-CI status without re-checking PR.merged_at; a merge that returned a SHA but didn't persist could still close - hardening would add a GetPRState merged check.
- 2026-06-13 (deployed d045a9d) **propose_issue RepositoryRef slug bug FIXED; brainstorm re-enabled.** createProposal now calls resolveRepository(namespace, projectRef, ref): tries the CR name (only if ref has no "/", else the API server rejects "owner/repo" as an invalid name - this was a test-caught trap), then matches the ref against each Project Repository by owner/repo of its URL. So the agent may pass either "tatara-cli" or "owner/tatara-cli". Re-enabled brainstorm on Project tatara (was disabled during the runaway). Verified live: the "Repository ... not found" createProposal error-loop is gone; open Tasks hold at the MaxOpenTasks cap (3). Both this and the close-guard deployed via buildx -> set-image (helm clean apply still blocked on the tatara-scm token SSA conflict - see prior entry).

- 2026-06-13 (deployed 4dffcc2) **MaxOpenTasks hard cap (default 3) on AUTONOMOUS task creation.** Trigger incident: deploying the 3-label lifecycle (which REMOVED the ApprovalRequired gate) unparked 40 proposal Tasks that had been safely held at AwaitingApproval, freeing them to error-loop/self-implement. Root flood cause: brainstorm kept minting proposals AND `propose_issue`/createProposal stored the repo SLUG `szymonrychu/<repo>` in `ProposedIssue.RepositoryRef` instead of the Repository CR name `<repo>` -> createProposal's `r.Get(Name: RepositoryRef)` 404s ("Repository ... not found") -> issue never opens -> the issue-count backpressure (proposalBacklog) never trips -> unbounded proposal Tasks. Containment: scaled operator deploy to 0 (reversible freeze), deleted the 40 AwaitingApproval proposal Tasks (their SCM issues persist + re-triage as tatara-idea). Fix: new `ProjectSpec.MaxOpenTasks` (kubebuilder default 3); `runScans` computes `budget = MaxOpenTasks - openTaskCount(existing)` and threads a SHARED `*budget` through mrScan/issueScan/brainstorm; each breaks at `*budget<=0` and decrements only on successful create -> total autonomous creations hard-capped. `maxOpenTasks()` defaults to 3 IN CODE, so set-image alone enforces it even before the CRD field reaches the cluster. Webhook is EXEMPT (human-initiated, must not silently drop). taskOpen() = not Succeeded/Failed phase AND lifecycleState not Done/Stopped/Parked. VERIFIED live: log "scan: at open-task cap; skipping autonomous creation cap=3", open Tasks held at 3. brainstorm DISABLED on Project tatara (kubectl patch spec.scm.cron.brainstorm.enabled=false) until the RepositoryRef bug is fixed (else it mints failing proposals that consume the budget).
- 2026-06-13 **OPEN BUG (not yet fixed): propose_issue RepositoryRef = slug not CR name.** internal/restapi/handlers.go proposeIssue sets `ProposedIssue.RepositoryRef = req.RepositoryRef` from the agent, which passes "szymonrychu/<repo>" (slug). createProposal does `r.Get(client.ObjectKey{Name: RepositoryRef})` -> Repository CRs are named "<repo>" (no slash, k8s-valid) -> always 404. Blocks all brainstorm idea creation; brainstorm stays disabled until fixed.
- 2026-06-13 **Operator deploy path is currently set-image, NOT clean helm.** helm release v42 (chart 0.0.0-7d45bd9) FAILED on server-side-apply field-ownership conflicts: Deployment `.image` owned by "kubectl-set" (prior manual image pins / the drift) and Secret tatara-scm `.data.token` owned by "kubectl-patch" (bot PAT patched 2026-06-13T06:16Z, AFTER sops's last apply -> live token is almost certainly NEWER than sops). helmfile uses `--server-side`; forcing (`--force-conflicts`) would overwrite the token with the stale sops value and break the bot. So label-lifecycle (7d45bd9) and the cap (4dffcc2) were deployed via `kubectl set image` (urgent buildx -> harbor containers/tatara-operator:<sha>, then set-image + scale). Infra MR !1108 bumped chart 0.0.0-7d45bd9 + image tag but the helm APPLY child-pipeline fails on these conflicts (job reports success; helm release is `failed`). CLEAN apply is BLOCKED until the tatara-scm token is reconciled: confirm sops scmToken == live PAT (or re-encrypt the current PAT into default.secrets.yaml), then a force-apply is safe and re-establishes helm ownership of image+token. New ScmSpec label fields (ideaLabel/approvedLabel/rejectedLabel) won't reach the cluster CRD until that clean apply, but the operator defaults them in code so function is unaffected.

- 2026-06-13 (#16, NOT yet deployed) Resolved the M5 deferred follow-up "GitLab Comment targets /issues/{iid}/notes". GitHub/GitLab parity bug: `scm.GitLab.Comment` parsed only the `#` separator (`glHashRef`) and unconditionally posted to `/projects/{p}/issues/{iid}/notes`, so every write-back aimed at a GitLab MR either errored (`!` ref -> malformed) or silently hit a different *issue* with the same iid. FIX: `Comment` now routes on the ref separator - a `!` ref goes through the existing `mrNote` (`/merge_requests/{iid}/notes`, previously ClosePR-only), a `#` ref keeps the issues path; added `glBangRef` mirroring `glHashRef`. Second defect: `createScanTask` (projectscan.go) hardcoded `#` for ALL candidates incl. MRs, so a scan-created GitLab MR Task carried `group/proj#42` (wrong object); now emits `!` when `srcCand.isPR && provider=="gitlab"`. GitHub stays on `#` for both (shared `/issues/{n}/comments` endpoint). Bot-PR-entry binder is createScanTask (covered); `recordExistingProposal` is issue-only so `#` is correct there. Tests: TestGitLabCommentMR (asserts `/merge_requests/42/notes`), TestGitLabBangRef, TestCreateScanTaskGitLabMR (`!` for MR, `#` for issue). NOTE: go toolchain absent in triage env - not locally built/tested, relying on CI.
- 2026-06-13 (48ea02b, DEPLOYED live, VERIFIED) Per-repo backpressured brainstorm + approval backstop. brainstorm() was repos[0]-only/MaxPerCycle/daily; now per-repo, hourly, capped: for each repo skip if an in-flight brainstorm Task already targets it (the live-SCM proposal count lags until the issue is opened), else count open non-PR issues bearing spec.scm.approvalLabel via ListOpenIssues; if >= maxOpenProposals (new BrainstormActivity CRD field, default 3) skip, else create exactly ONE brainstorm Task -> saturates to 3 over ~3h then pauses. New approvalBackstop() (every scan cycle) recovers a missed approval webhook: for each AwaitingApproval proposal Task it reads the issue and, if approved (label removed) + open + no impl running for that issue + ApprovalRequired + bot-authored, flips ConditionApprovalApproved (RetryOnConflict) mirroring the webhook's flipApproval guard. KEY BUG caught in review: the backstop first matched the issue by Source.Number, but createProposal records Source.Number=0 (real number lives only in Source.IssueRef) -> it was a production no-op masked by a test that fabricated Number; fixed to match Source.IssueRef (build "owner/repo#n" from the listing). Identity signal: an OPEN issue carrying approvalLabel == an agent proposal awaiting approval (operator applies the label on proposal creation; human removes it to approve), so no author lookup needed for the cap. Config (infra MR !1102): brainstorm.schedule 0 6 -> 0 * * * * hourly, maxOpenProposals 3; Project CRD re-applied (kubectl, Helm skips crds/).
