- 2026-06-13 (b0d0554, DEPLOYED live, VERIFIED) Triage agent was BLIND to the issue. `lifecycleTriageText` rendered `task.Spec.Goal` (the operator string "Triage issue owner/repo#N") into the prompt's "Issue body:" and showed no title -> the agent saw its own goal as the body and triaged every issue as empty (observed: on a fully-populated issue it commented "the title is empty and the body only contains the placeholder text 'Triage issue ...'"). Root cause: no issue-content reader (SCMReader had ListIssueComments but no GetIssue) + the scanned body is dropped at Task creation, so the prompt fell back to the goal. FIX: add `scm.IssueContent` + `SCMReader.GetIssue` (GitHub GET /repos/{o}/{r}/issues/{n} json "body"; GitLab GET /projects/{esc}/issues/{n} json "description"); `buildTriagePromptFor` now live-fetches title+body (comments already were) and renders them, never falling back to the goal. VERIFIED live: re-triggered tatara-cli#21 (comment reactivation) -> agent flipped Triage->Implement (was `discuss`/"no actionable content") = it now sees the real bug. Branch fix/triage-sees-issue.
- 2026-06-13 (b0d0554, DEPLOYED live, VERIFIED) Agent-pod BOOT-RACE no longer backs off. A turn submit to a wrapper whose turn server is still booting (pod Ready + Service endpoints up, listener/route not yet) returned a transport error to Reconcile -> controller-runtime EXPONENTIAL backoff -> task idled at Planning for minutes; amplified by resetAgentRun (fresh pod per lifecycle state). FIX: agent classifies transport failures from http.Client.Do as `*agent.UnreachableError` (`isUnreachable` EXCLUDES timeouts + context-cancel, which keep erroring -> a hung server still backs off, not loops); `handleAgentUnreachable` requeues those on a 5s FIXED interval (no backoff) at BOTH submit sites, and BOUNDS a never-reachable pod via `annAgentUnreachableSince`+`agentBootDeadline=5m` -> terminate Failed/AgentUnreachable; marker cleared on successful submit (recordTurn) + on resetAgentRun. New counter `operator_agent_boot_race_requeue_total` (the requeue is now reconcile-success, else invisible). VERIFIED live: the Implement-state fresh pod for tatara-cli#21 logged `"agent not yet accepting turns; requeuing" requeueAfter:"5s"` x2 then converged (turn submitted, marker cleared). Branch fix/agent-boot-race-requeue. Both fixes opus-reviewed (2 rounds for boot-race: classification-breadth + terminal-bound closed).
- 2026-06-13 (43be6f3, DEPLOYED live) Lifecycle conflict-spin FIX + deploy. Live bug found during in-cluster verification: the implement handler writes status (the iteration counter) just before `driveAgentRun`'s plain `Phase="Planning"` Status().Update; the cached client lags the API server so that Update raced/errored the reconcile, the retry re-entered at Phase=="" and re-ran the increment, spinning `lifecycleIterations` 0->10 in ~2s -> EVERY lifecycle task Parked at iter=10/turns=0 (agents never ran a turn; Triage even reached implement with turns=0). Fix: RetryOnConflict the Planning-phase set in `driveAgentRun` (absorb the conflict internally so the reconcile does not error->retry->re-increment). LESSON: a cached re-read after a write does NOT cure the conflict (cache is stale right after the write); use RetryOnConflict or an uncached read. Deployed live: operator c274cc9 then 43be6f3, cli 8978d4d, wrapper a7eab9b - images BUILT LOCALLY via buildx (CI was broken, see global memory arc-runners-die-on-job-pickup). 405-loop death verified live.
- 2026-06-13 (issue-lifecycle, on main 6976ae7, NOT yet deployed) New `issueLifecycle` Task kind: one persistent Task per issue carries an S1..S7 state machine in `Status.LifecycleState` (Triage->Conversation->Implement->MRCI->Merge->MainCI->Done/Stopped/Parked), reusing the existing agent-run + writeback primitives. Binders (issueScan/mrScan/webhook) now create `issueLifecycle` (Triage for issues, MRCI-entry for bot PRs) instead of `triageIssue`/`selfImprove`; legacy arms retained reachable for in-flight migration. KILLS the live `selfImprove ... merge -> 405 merge conflicts` controller-runtime backoff loop: the Merge state classifies a 405 as a conflict and spawns a resolve-conflict re-implement turn returning nil error (regression test `TestLifecycleMerge_405ConflictSpawnsResolveAttempt_ErrNil`); the legacy `writeBackSelfImprove` 405 path was ALSO guarded (absorb->clearWritebackPending) so the loop dies for any in-flight selfImprove Task without a manual deploy step. Spec/plans `docs/superpowers/{specs/2026-06-12-issue-lifecycle-agent-design.md,plans/2026-06-12-issue-lifecycle-m*}` (parent tatara repo).
- 2026-06-13 (issue-lifecycle) M3 context-guard ADAPTATION: the literal spec "context >50% after S7" does NOT map, because each implement run spawns a FRESH wrapper pod (resetAgentRun tears it down at run-end) - no long-lived session accumulates context across S4-S7 iterations. Realized as operator-computed-at-transitions: at each failure transition into Implement (MRCI/Merge-405/MainCI fail) the operator computes `LastTurnInputTokens*100/contextWindowTokens`; >= handoverThresholdPercent (default 50) marks `tatara.dev/pending-handover-resume` + populates `Status.Handover` (agent's `submit_handover` doc, else operator-built from ResultSummary+ImplementContext+branch); the next fresh Implement run injects it. Wrapper needs NO change (its `turn.Record.usage` was already posted to the callback; operator just deserializes it). Still honors the "operator-computed from usage" decision.

- 2026-06-08 (0.2.5) lightrag `OPENAI_API_KEY` bug: `lightragEnv`
  (`internal/memory/lightrag.go`) set `LLM_BINDING_API_KEY` but not
  `OPENAI_API_KEY`. LightRAG's openai LLM/embedding paths fall back to the raw
  `OPENAI_API_KEY` env, so its async processing pipeline failed
  `KeyError 'OPENAI_API_KEY'` and every queued doc went `doc_status=failed`
  (963 on the cluster) - chunks/entities/relations never materialized even though
  `/documents/text` returned 200. Fix: source `OPENAI_API_KEY` from the same
  openai Secret (key `LLM_BINDING_API_KEY`). Surfaced only once the upstream
  chunk path drained end-to-end (memory 0.2.2/0.2.3 + ingester 0.2.2 kubectl
  fixes) - the dogfood was the first real exercise of LightRAG doc processing;
  earlier "index built" was schema/HNSW init, not document processing.
- 2026-06-08 (0.2.4) imagePullSecrets bug: operator-spawned **ingest Jobs**
  (`internal/ingest/job.go`) and **agent wrapper Pods** (`internal/agent/pod.go`)
  set their container image from a private Harbor registry but had no
  `imagePullSecrets`, so both failed `ErrImagePull` ("no basic auth credentials").
  The 0.2.1 fix only covered the per-Project memory pods (`internal/memory`).
  Fixed by mirroring the memory `imagePullSecrets(cfg)` helper in both packages,
  fed from `IMAGE_PULL_SECRET` (regcred) via `wire.go`. Surfaced only on the first
  real dogfood ingest (envtest never pulls images). Rule: every operator-spawned
  workload that pulls a private image needs imagePullSecrets wired from config.

- 2026-06-08 (0.2.2) Spawned agent auth switched from console API key to a
  long-lived Claude Code OAuth token: `pod.go` BuildPod now injects
  `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN` from Secret `<anthropicSecretName>` data key
  `oauth-token` (was `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`/`api-key`). Pure replace, not additive:
  claude auth precedence puts `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` above the OAuth token, so
  injecting both would leave the OAuth token inert. Wrapper needs no change
  (it passes os.Environ() straight to the claude child; OAuth login does not
  trigger the API-key dialog claudejson.go seeds). The `tatara-anthropic`
  Secret must carry `oauth-token` (from `claude setup-token`); the old `api-key`
  key is no longer read. Drives subscription billing instead of console API.

- 2026-06-06 (M1) Ingest result SHA flows via a per-Repository ConfigMap

  in-cluster API after `git rev-parse HEAD`; the reconciler pre-creates it
  (owner-ref Repository) and reads it on Job success. Chosen over pod-log
  parsing (brittle) and Job annotations (Job cannot patch itself cleanly).
  REQUIRES M6 chart to create ServiceAccount `tatara-ingest` + a Role granting

  kubectl presence in M6, else switch the patch step to a tiny `curl` against

2026-06-09 - **Agent-native tools were dead until cli 0.4.3.** Every wrapper agent run Succeeded with 0 subtasks / empty issue comments because tatara-cli's `tatara mcp` returned an error on tools/list (NewTool+WithRawInputSchema set both InputSchema and RawInputSchema; mcp-go refuses to marshal). claude loaded ZERO tatara tools while `claude mcp list` still said "Connected" (initialize handshake only). Root cause + fix in tatara-cli MEMORY (0.4.3, NewToolWithRawSchema). Rebuilt wrapper 0.1.8 (bundles cli 0.4.3); Project tatara agent.image -> 0.1.8 (kubectl patch; Project is kubectl-managed, not helm). Validated: bare Task -> agent called subtask_create via MCP -> Subtask created. Auth (operator/memory OIDC) was never the blocker; the curl probes bypassed claude.

2026-06-11 - **autonomous-cron ACTIVATED on Project tatara via personal PAT (no bot account, no Project board).** Cron scans iterate the Project's Repository CRs (projectReposForScan: RepositoryList filtered by Spec.ProjectRef); the GitHub Projects-v2 board is OPTIONAL (issueScan adds board items only when Spec.Scm.Board != nil). Activation gate is purely `Scm != nil && Cron != nil` - no botLogin/board/org dependency. botLogin == the PAT owner (szymonrychu), so mrScan routes the owner's own PRs to selfImprove and others' to review (author/actor egress gate via GetPRState). prReactionScope does NOT gate cron mrScan (it scans all open PRs); it only gates the reactive webhook path. First fire verified: listed 5 PRs/7 issues, created selfImprove+triageIssue+brainstorm Tasks; agent pods run wrapper 0.1.12.
2026-06-11 - **Wrapper image version numbering diverged from the repo.** Deployed agent image was 0.1.11, but wrapper repo appVersion only ever went 0.1.4->0.1.5->0.1.7->0.1.8 - the 0.1.9/0.1.10/0.1.11 tags were ad-hoc `make image VERSION=...` overrides during the graphify deploys, never committed to Chart.yaml. Resolution: re-cut wrapper 0.1.12 (forward of the deployed 0.1.11). Content is determined by the BAKED CLI, not the wrapper number: wrapper 0.1.12 bakes cli 0.6.0, a linear superset (17 graphify code_* tools + SCM propose/review/pr_outcome + issue_outcome), so it strictly supersedes 0.1.11 (older graphify-era cli) despite numbers. RULE: always cut wrapper forward of the deployed tag and verify content via the baked cli version.
2026-06-11 - **stampScan lacks RetryOnConflict (minor, 0.4.1 backlog).** projectscan.go stampScan does Get + Status().Update without retry, so a scan racing the main reconcile logs a benign "object has been modified" ERROR; the stamp succeeds on the next reconcile (timestamps ARE recorded; hourly schedule means no hot loop, dedup prevents duplicate Tasks). Wrap in retry.RetryOnConflict to kill the ERROR noise.
2026-06-11 - **Egress: applied the additive tatara-egress-internet allow ONLY (ipBlock 0.0.0.0/0:443 + DNS, keyed on tatara.io/egress=internet), NOT the runbook's namespace-wide default-deny-egress.** ns tatara today: only tatara-operator-managed-pods selects pods (managed-by=tatara-operator); chat/memory/cnpg/neo4j are selected by NO egress policy -> open egress. A blanket default-deny would newly restrict and likely break them. Manager pod is NOT managed-by -> open egress -> cron SCM calls (443) unrestricted. Hardening the namespace needs a per-pod egress audit first.
2026-06-12 (issue #3) memoryStackHealth tolerates NotFound: a NotFound read on any of the 4 owned objects (cnpg Cluster, neo4j STS, lightrag/memory Deployments) is treated as not-yet-ready (count stays 0 -> memoryPhase=Provisioning) instead of erroring. reconcileMemory no longer calls failMemory("HealthError") on a health read error: a non-NotFound (transient API/cache) error leaves phase+MemoryReady untouched and requeues with backoff. Failed is now reserved for password/apply errors only. Key insight: genuine provisioning stalls (objects exist but never become ready) already surface as a stuck Provisioning phase via memoryPhase, never Failed - so health-read-error->Failed only ever caused the spurious flap the issue describes; removing it needs no grace-period state.
2026-06-12 - **Per-repo fan-out (improvement #1): scan creation is intentionally O(#repos), not the old global maxPerCycle.** mrScan/issueScan now top up each repo's lane to MaxPerRepo (CronActivity field, was MaxPerCycle; default 1) via selectPerRepo + laneOccupancy. laneOccupancy counts a repo's Tasks in {Pending,Planning,Running} (EXCLUDES AwaitingApproval/Succeeded/Failed) so an awaiting-approval proposal does NOT hold the lane. Consequence: a single scan can create up to #repos Tasks (vs <=maxPerCycle before). This is BOUNDED, not unbounded: occupancy counts Pending, so each lane caps at MaxPerRepo and total in-flight Task CRs <= 2*#repos*MaxPerRepo (12 for tatara's 6 repos). Execution is throttled by spec.maxConcurrentTasks (atConcurrencyCap, EXECUTION-time gate on isActive only - it never throttles CREATION). A 60s backlogRequeue refills freed lanes. Rationale: a creation-side cap would defeat the fan-out; for tatara (6 repos) the bound is trivial. If a Project ever has very many repos, add a per-scan creation cap. brainstorm (BrainstormActivity.MaxPerCycle) is untouched (genuinely per-cycle). Branch feat/per-repo-fanout; awaiting deploy.
2026-06-13 - **3-label issue lifecycle (tatara-idea / tatara-approved / tatara-rejected) replaces the label-toggle approval model.** Approval is now CONVERSATION-driven: the Triage agent reads the full thread (handleIssueComment already resets a live lifecycle Task to Triage on any non-bot comment) and emits issue_outcome; the operator projects it onto exactly one managed label via setLifecycleLabel egress (internal/controller/labels.go) at each finishTriage transition: implement->approved+Implement, discuss->idea+Conversation, close->rejected+close+Done. Self-approve guard: a bot-authored issue (Source.AuthorLogin==BotLogin) can only reach approved/Implement if hasHumanComment is true; otherwise it parks as idea/Conversation (fail-closed on a ListIssueComments error). Brainstorm now opens the proposal issue with the IDEA label and the proposal Task COMPLETES (Succeeded) - the old AwaitingApproval parking + propose_issue ApprovalRequired + flipApproval(webhook unlabeled) + approvalBackstop + the task_controller approval gate are all REMOVED (incl. the proposeIssue REST handler's vestigial AwaitingApproval status stamp). proposalBacklog now counts open non-PR idea-labelled issues (subsumes bot proposals + human-filed parked ideas; IssueRef has no Author so cannot filter to bot-only - conservative backpressure). setLifecycleLabel reads current labels to stay idempotent + scope-safe (never touches triggerLabel/priorityLabel); when the label set is unreadable (nil reader / list error / just-closed issue not in open list) it falls back to add+remove unconditionally so the one-label contract holds. DEPRECATED-but-kept no-ops (avoid CRD/DTO/enum churn): ScmSpec.ApprovalLabel field, ConditionApprovalApproved const, AwaitingApproval phase enum, Task.GateEnteredAt. New ScmSpec fields ideaLabel/approvedLabel/rejectedLabel (kubebuilder defaults tatara-idea/approved/rejected). Both GitHub + GitLab AddLabel auto-create labels, so no provisioning step. Branch feat/label-lifecycle; design+plan in tatara repo docs/superpowers/{specs,plans}/2026-06-13-tatara-label-lifecycle*. DEPLOY MIGRATION (one-time, manual, in plan T12): relabel existing open `tatara/awaiting-approval` issues to `tatara-idea` (gh/glab loop); supersede any lingering AwaitingApproval Tasks. REVIEW-FIX (final adversarial review): the self-approve guard detects tatara-authorship via the `tataraAuthoredMarker` in the issue BODY (GetIssue), NOT Source.AuthorLogin - because issueScan-created lifecycle Tasks leave AuthorLogin EMPTY (the cron path brainstorm ideas actually flow through) and the webhook AuthorLogin is untrusted; keying on AuthorLogin would have let every cron-scanned tatara idea auto-approve with no human comment. IssueOutcome is now cleared AFTER the action arm commits its state transition (clearIssueOutcome), so a mid-arm SCM error retries the SAME outcome instead of silently downgrading a close/discuss to implement; accepted tradeoff = a rare duplicate triage comment if the post-SCM status update exhausts retries (cosmetic, preferred over wrong-implement). LATENT (pre-existing, GitLab-only, not fixed): hasHumanComment/tataraAuthoredIssue/buildTriagePromptFor pass scm.OwnerRepo (2-segment) to ListIssueComments/GetIssue, wrong for GitLab subgroup project paths -> those reads fail -> bot ideas fail-closed (never self-approve) on GitLab; live deploy is GitHub so unaffected; fix needs a provider-correct project-path helper. Awaiting deploy.

2026-06-13 (issue #23) **Descriptive wrapper Pod/Service names.** PodName(task) was `wrapper-<task-name>` (random suffix, opaque). New format: `tatara-<project>-<gh|gl>-<repo>-<issue-N|mr-N|brainstorm|scan>` (repo segment dropped when RepositoryRef empty, e.g. project-board items). KEY CONSTRAINT that drove the design: PodName(task) must be a PURE fn of the Task because ~8 delete/lookup sites (terminate, resetAgentRun, turncallback recreate, task_controller Get) call it with only the Task (no Project loaded) - so provider can't be re-derived there (brainstorm Tasks carry no Source.Provider). Solution: stamp the computed name into annotation `tatara.dev/pod-name` at the 5 creation sites (webhook x2, restapi proposeIssue, projectscan createScanTask + createBrainstormTask, all of which have provider+repo in scope), and PodName reads the annotation with a `wrapper-<name>` fallback for legacy in-flight Tasks. Builder agent.BuildPodName + agent.StampPodName in internal/agent/pod.go; sanitizeDNS1123 caps at 63 (Service-name limit) - for tatara's repos max real name ~56 chars so no truncation. Suffix logic: Kind==brainstorm->brainstorm; Source.Number>0 -> mr-N (IsPR) / issue-N; else scan. Branch tatara/task-task-b5km7.

2026-06-14 (issue #34) **Empty Implement run = retry-then-escalate, not silent no-change park.** An issueLifecycle Implement turn that produced ZERO commits used to flow Succeeded -> writeBackOpenChange -> every repo 422 (empty/absent branch) -> len(prURLs)==0 -> finishImplement parked it `Parked/no-change`, indistinguishable from a report/question task that correctly produces no diff -> the issue fix silently vanished and never retried (live: scan-fgqtt for #29, and tatara-chat#26). Fix in finishImplement's PrURL=="" block: new Status.ImplementEmptyRetries counter (CRD field), retry up to cap 2 (3 attempts total) by setImplementContext(emptyImplementReentryPrompt)+resetAgentRun (leaves LifecycleState=Implement, clears Phase, so handleImplement re-spawns with the nudge), then parkWithComment reason=`implement-empty` + one human-handoff comment. Counter reset to 0 (a) on the PR-opened success path and (b) in setLifecycleState whenever to=="Implement" (DRY chokepoint - every operator-driven Implement entry/revival gets a fresh budget; the retry loop never calls setLifecycleState so it can't clobber an in-progress count). Scoping is automatic: report/question/verify reach writeback via doWriteBack, NEVER finishImplement (handleImplement-only), so no Kind check needed. Anti-spam: writeBackOpenChange's no-PR ResultSummary echo is suppressed when LifecycleState=="Implement" (finishImplement owns those issue comments), else a stuck task accrued 3-4 comments. DELIBERATELY NOT DONE (KISS/YAGNI): no SCMWriter.CompareCommits method - the existing no-PR detection (every repo's OpenChange returns 4xx on an empty OR absent head branch -> len(prURLs)==0) already catches empty runs authoritatively for both old-wrapper (empty branch pushed) and new-wrapper (branch absent after skip-push); an interface method + GitHub/GitLab impls + fakes buys only avoiding one already-handled failing API call. Also no wrapper `noChange` webhook field (operator detects independently). Paired wrapper change: CommitAndPush skips git push when the tree is clean (no empty tatara/task-* branch accumulation). Branch fix/implement-empty-retry; design+plan in tatara repo docs/superpowers/plans/2026-06-14-issue34-empty-implement-retry.md.

2026-06-14 (task-p6rhl) **Wrapper Pod+Service torn down on terminal lifecycle, not just terminal phase.** terminate (Succeeded/Failed) already deleted the wrapper, but a Task entering a terminal LIFECYCLE state (Done/Stopped/Parked) left its idle claude session running (CPU/mem + a Ceph work PVC) - the leak behind the 2026-06-14 concurrency-cap incident where Parked/Succeeded wrappers ran 9-14h. Fix: setLifecycleState (the single chokepoint every terminal lifecycle transition routes through - park/triage-failed/triage-close/idle-stop/maxIterations/implement-failed/implement-empty/mainci-success) now calls deleteWrapper when isLifecycleTerminal(to). deleteWrapper is a new shared best-effort helper (lifecycle.go) extracted from the duplicated pod+svc Delete blocks in terminate and resetAgentRun (DRY); reactivateTask in webhook/server.go keeps its own copy (different receiver type). Best-effort: a delete error is logged, never blocks the already-applied state transition. KISS: no new state/condition - reactivation already deletes+re-spawns, so deleting on Park is safe. Branch tatara/task-task-p6rhl.

2026-06-15 (issue #35) **atConcurrencyCap now excludes Conversation, aligning the concurrency cap with the creation budget.** taskActive (task_controller.go, the predicate atConcurrencyCap counts) gated only on isLifecycleTerminal (Done/Stopped/Parked), so an active-phase (Planning/Running) Conversation task still pinched a concurrency slot - the inconsistency observed right after the taskOpen creation-budget fix, where brainstorm briefly gated at the cap while awaiting-human Conversation tasks held slots. Fix: taskActive returns false for LifecycleState=="Conversation" (one guard), matching taskOpen (projectscan.go) which already excludes Conversation. Did NOT touch isLifecycleTerminal: it is shared by the dedup path (frees the repo,number key on newer activity) where a Conversation task legitimately still holds its issue, so Conversation must stay non-terminal there. KISS: a local guard in taskActive rather than reconciling the two predicates into one (taskOpen also keys on isTerminal phase + has its own comment contract). Test: TestTaskActive_ExcludesTerminalLifecycle gains Running/Planning x Conversation -> false cases. Branch tatara/task-scan-2fk4d.

2026-06-15 (issue #21) **MRCI duplicate-of-merged guard: post-merge re-implement on the reused task branch no longer re-proposes the already-merged change.** Residual MR-nursing flakiness after PR#26 (clearMergedChangeState on MainCI failure) + wrapper#20 (resume the deterministic remote task branch on re-entry): the two COMPOSE into a new failure mode. On a post-merge MainCI failure, clearMergedChangeState clears PrURL/PRNumber so finishImplement opens a FRESH MR, but the wrapper resumes the SAME branch tatara/task-<name> which was just squash-merged; if the re-implement does not advance it, writeBackOpenChange opens a PR re-proposing the identical already-merged commits (main moved past the squash so OpenChange does NOT 422). Concrete in-repo evidence: operator PR #50 duplicated merged PR #46 with an IDENTICAL head SHA 82073dbd7d (also issue #29's #39 dup of merged #54). Nursing the dup re-merges identical code -> MainCI fails again -> bounces to maxLifecycleIterations (the "6 tasks parked at iters=10" the maintainer cited) with no diagnostic. Fix: new Status.MergedHeadSHA records the merged source-branch head (captured via GetPRState just before writer.Merge; best-effort, "" on error = guard disabled); it is DELIBERATELY preserved across clearMergedChangeState. handleMRCI, after the authorship gate, parks (closes the dup PR + RecordGiveup("duplicate-merged-change") + human comment) when st.HeadSHA == MergedHeadSHA. Fail-fast-and-loud beats silently burning 10 iterations. NOT fixed here (out of operator scope): the deeper root cause is the PR-vs-main CI asymmetry (chart job skipped on the PR head, runs+fails on main) so the MR pipeline can never validate the fix - that is a per-repo CI-config concern, not operator logic. Tests TestLifecycleMRCI_DuplicateOfMergedHeadParks + _AdvancedHeadAfterMergeProceeds (FIX 10). Branch tatara/task-scan-8826z.

2026-06-15 (task-pb9ng) **Periodic orphan-pod reaper backstops the one-shot wrapper teardown.** The terminate/resetAgentRun/terminal-lifecycle deletes (keyed on PodName(task)) are one-shot: if missed (older pod-naming scheme, transient delete error, or Task already terminal at operator restart) nothing re-reaps, leaving zombie wrapper pods that leak CPU/mem/image-cache and (with the pod-name collision bug) can block a new Task's pod. Observed live 2026-06-14: wrapper-task-2mwsk/-d6p5d Running 20h/19h past Succeeded; ...-<repo>-scan pods lingering. Fix: new `CallbackServer.ReapOrphans` (internal/controller/reaper.go) runs each poll tick (turncallback.go Start loop, alongside PollOnce but NOT gated on Session - orphans outlive their session). It LISTS pods by label (agent.WrapperPodSelector = managed-by=tatara-operator + component=agent), correlates each back to its Task via the `tatara.dev/task` label (NO PodName reconstruction), and reaps pod+same-named service when: Task absent (NotFound), `tatara.dev/task-uid` label disagrees with the live Task UID (leftover from a prior incarnation that reused the name), phase terminal (isTerminal: Succeeded/Failed), or lifecycle terminal (isLifecycleTerminal: Done/Parked/Stopped). Transient Get errors -> do NOT reap (no reap-on-uncertainty); unlabelled pods left for a human. Added the `tatara.dev/task-uid` label (+ exported label-key consts LabelManagedBy/LabelComponent/LabelTask/LabelTaskUID, ManagedByValue/ComponentAgent, WrapperPodSelector) in agent/pod.go podLabels; UID omitted when empty (unit-test Tasks). Owner-references already GC pods on Task delete; the reaper is the backstop for the terminal-but-Task-still-present and missed-delete cases owner-refs DON'T cover. Pairs with [[the terminal-lifecycle teardown from task-p6rhl]]. Tests reaper_test.go (absent/terminal-phase/terminal-lifecycle/stale-uid reap, live-task kept). Branch tatara/task-task-pb9ng.

2026-06-15 (issue #45) **Boot-crash detection: a wrapper Pod that dies before /readyz no longer wedges its Task in Planning forever.** Gap-2 companion to recoverOrphans (Gap-1, already shipped: the issueScan lifecycle-orphan sweep that re-Implements an implementation-labelled issue with no live Task). The wedge: RestartPolicy=Never, so a wrapper that exits non-zero on boot lands the Pod in phase=Failed; driveAgentRun's `!podReady` arm just requeued every 2s with no deadline, and since no turn ever started (annTurnStartedAt unset) BOTH turn-timeout backstops (reconcile isTurnTimedOut + PollOnce) skip it -> invisible, never recovers (the #44 secondary-hardening case). Fix in task_controller.go: the `!ready` arm now calls handleBootCrash, which inspects the Pod via bootCrashReason (PodFailed | container CrashLoopBackOff | container Terminated non-zero, init or main) and bootDeadlineExceeded (not-Ready longer than agentBootDeadline=5m, anchored on pod.CreationTimestamp -> reason "BootTimeout"). On a hit it resetAgentRun-respawns, bounded by maxPodRecreations(3) boot attempts tracked in annotation `tatara.dev/boot-crash-attempts`; once exhausted it terminates Failed/BootCrashLoop so recoverOrphans re-picks it (the two gaps compose: fail-fast -> orphan sweep). KEY: the attempts annotation is DELIBERATELY preserved across resetAgentRun (unlike annPodRecreations, which reset clears) so the budget accumulates across respawns; it is cleared in recordTurn on the first successful turn submit (same site as annAgentUnreachableSince), so each lifecycle state that boots cleanly starts with a fresh budget and only a never-booting state accrues. Distinct from handleAgentUnreachable (that one is Ready-but-not-accepting-turns, keyed on SubmitTurn UnreachableError + annAgentUnreachableSince; this one is never-Ready). Covers both generic and issueLifecycle Tasks (Triage+Implement both route through driveAgentRun). Metric operator_agent_boot_crash_total{reason,outcome=respawn|failed}. Tests in bootcrash_test.go. Branch tatara/task-task-5pm4h.

2026-06-15 (issue #44) **Duplicate lifecycle Task wedge: dedup now counts Conversation Tasks + a spawn watchdog fails Planning-forever Tasks.** Two issueLifecycle Tasks for one issue (live: chat#24 had scan-tnc6s/Implement + scan-gxcsw/Triage) BOTH map to the same descriptive pod name `...-issue-N`; the second can't spawn (name taken), sits in Planning with no current-turn annotation, and is invisible to both turn-timeout backstops (they need annTurnStartedAt) -> wedged forever. Maintainer DECISION (issue thread): keep the existing scan pod-naming scheme (root-cause #1 was NOT a numberless-`scan` collision but this duplicate `issue-N` name), so pod.go/podNameSuffix is UNCHANGED; the real fixes are dedup idempotency (#2) + the spawn watchdog (#3). Brainstorm-per-project (the other thread ask) already landed. FIX #2 (the dedup gap): recoverOrphans used `hasNonTerminalTaskForIssue` -> taskOpen, which EXCLUDES Conversation (taskOpen rightly drops Conversation for the creation BUDGET, since a human-blocked task holds no slot). But for DEDUP a Conversation task still owns the issue's pod name, so excluding it let the backstop spawn a second Implement Task when an issue with a live Conversation Task later gained an implementation/approved label. Replaced with `hasLiveLifecycleTaskForIssue` (projectscan.go): counts any (repo,number) Task that is NOT terminal-phase AND NOT lifecycle-terminal (Done/Stopped/Parked) -> Conversation now blocks. isDeduped (issueScan/mrScan path) already caught Conversation as non-terminal, so the gap was recoverOrphans-only. KEY distinction kept: budget/lane/concurrency exclude Conversation (no slot held); dedup includes it (a Task object exists for the issue -> don't make a second). FIX #3 (spawn watchdog, defense-in-depth for ANY duplicate-induced wedge incl. the latent mrScan->issueScan same-cycle race that uses a stale `existing` snapshot): PollOnce now detects a Task in Planning with empty current-turn past `planningStallDeadline` (= 4*agentBootDeadline = 20m, DELIBERATELY beyond the boot-crash budget maxPodRecreations*agentBootDeadline so it never preempts a legitimately slow/crashing boot) and fails it Failed/PlanningStalled -> recoverOrphans re-picks cleanly. The deadline is anchored on new annotation `tatara.dev/planning-since` (AnnPlanningSince), stamped in driveAgentRun at the Phase=="" -> Planning transition via a SEPARATE metadata Update (annotations aren't status; the existing Planning flip uses Status().Update), overwritten every spawn so a reset+respawn measures from its own start. CRITICAL: expireStalledPlanning sets ONLY Task phase - it does NOT delete the Pod/Service (unlike expireTimedOutTurn), because a duplicate shares the LIVE Task's pod name and deleting by name would kill the live agent; the orphan reaper instead reaps this Task's own pod (if any) by UID once terminal. Healthy tasks never trip: turn-0 submit sets annCurrentTurn within boot time and the watchdog only looks at Planning+empty-turn. Tests: TestBackstopSkipsIssueWithConversationTask (dedup), TestPollOnce_FailsStalledPlanning + _LeavesFreshPlanning (watchdog). Pairs with [[the boot-crash detection from issue #45]] and [[recoverOrphans lifecycle-orphan sweep]]. Branch tatara/task-scan-5mltx.

2026-06-15 (issue #56, track A) **Author-tiered autoapprove gate: a captured third-party issue author bypasses the self-approve hold.** Builds on the same-issue scan-author capture (scm.IssueRef.Author now populated by GitHub/GitLab ListOpenIssues -> candidate.author -> Task.Source.AuthorLogin; this OBSOLETES the 2026-06-13 note's premise that "issueScan-created lifecycle Tasks leave AuthorLogin EMPTY" - it is now filled for per-repo issue listings, still empty only for board-sourced candidates). DECISION - AuthorLogin is now authoritative for the third-party determination because it comes from our authenticated ListOpenIssues (cron path) or the HMAC-verified webhook payload, and a genuine tatara idea is opened BY THE BOT so it carries BotLogin and never reads as third-party; the body marker remains the fallback guard for the EMPTY-author case (board/legacy path). 2026-06-23 (issue #82) **Boot-crash diagnostics: a BootCrashLoop terminal now carries the exit code + log tail instead of just the coarse signal.** Builds directly on [[the boot-crash detection from issue #45]], which terminated Failed/BootCrashLoop with only the bucket (PodFailed/CrashLoopBackOff/ContainerExited/BootTimeout) - no exit code, no log, and each respawn deletes the crashed pod so the cause was gone before a human looked. KISS capture without a clientset/`pods/log` RBAC: set `TerminationMessagePolicy: FallbackToLogsOnError` on the wrapper container (pod.go) so the kubelet writes the ~stdout/stderr tail into `ContainerStatus.State.Terminated.Message` on a non-zero exit; new `bootCrashDetail(pod)` (task_controller.go) then reads it as a pure walk of the same init+main status slice `bootCrashReason` already builds, formatting a bounded "container=.. waiting=.. exit=.. reason=.. log=.." string (CrashLoopBackOff pulls its tail from LastTerminationState; bare PodFailed falls back to pod.Status.Reason/Message; capped at bootCrashDetailCap=1024). DECISION - kept `bootCrashReason` UNCHANGED (a sibling helper, not an extended signature) so the metric label semantics + its table test stay identical; `bootCrashDetail` is independent and reason-agnostic. PERSISTENCE: captured into annotation `tatara.dev/boot-crash-diagnostics` in handleBootCrash BEFORE resetAgentRun/terminate delete the pod (last-write-wins via captureBootCrashDiagnostics, which also updates the in-memory task), DELIBERATELY preserved across resetAgentRun exactly like annBootCrashAttempts (reset only deletes its explicit list), and cleared in BOTH recordTurn and setLifecycleState alongside annBootCrashAttempts so a clean boot / new state never inherits a stale cause. SURFACING (3 channels): the detail is threaded into the agent_boot_crash / agent_boot_crash_exhausted structured logs (rule 12 `diagnostics` field), folded into the terminal `BootCrashLoop` condition message (`wrapper pod failed to boot (ContainerExited: container=wrapper exit=1 ... log=...) after 3 attempts`), and - because #81's terminal-Task GC deletes Status-only diagnostics exactly when a human looks - posted ONCE to the linked issue via commentBootCrashDiagnostics (mirrors the handleImplement max-iterations backstop comment pattern; gated on SCMFor!=nil + Source.IssueRef, so project-scoped brainstorm tasks with no issue silently skip and rely on the log). CRITICAL idempotency: the comment is posted only AFTER terminate commits Failed (terr==nil) so a terminate retry cannot double-post, and once Failed the lifecycle routes to finishImplement, never re-entering handleBootCrash. maxPodRecreations budget + respawn cadence + operator_agent_boot_crash_total metric all UNCHANGED. Tests: bootcrash_test.go (bootCrashDetail table + truncation cap; capture-survives-respawn; exhaustion folds detail into condition msg + posts exactly one issue comment + ContainerExited/failed metric) and pod_test.go (TerminationMessagePolicy assertion). Branch tatara/fix-82.

2026-06-23 (issue #110) **MemoryReady now probes the retrieval contract, not just replica counts.** memoryStackHealth/memoryPhase read only cnpg/neo4j/lightrag/memory replica readiness, so a memory pod that is Available but serving a stale or drifted HTTP contract read MemoryReady=True falsely-green (observed live: every retrieval call into mem-tatara 404'd while status said Ready) - silently zeroing the research premise of the autonomous loop. Fix MIRRORS [[the operator_lightrag_documents poller from issue #68]]: new updateMemoryRetrievalProbe (project_memory_probe.go) runs inside the same maybeRecomputeGauges 60s throttle, only for Ready stacks, and is best-effort (never fails the reconcile). It sends UNAUTHENTICATED requests to two representative agent-facing routes (POST /queries, GET /code-graph/stats) at memory.Endpoint(project,ns). KEY SIGNAL: both routes sit inside tatara-memory's cfg.Verify OIDC group (router.go), so a route-present binary answers 401 (auth rejects before the handler) while a drifted/stale binary 404s - probeMemoryRoute classifies 404="absent", transport-failure="error", any other served status (401/400/200/500)="present". Zero-credential contract-presence signal, no memory-audience token wiring. Metric operator_memory_retrieval_probe_total{route,result} (route label = the path, must stay in sync with the obs pre-seed); each unhealthy route logged at INFO (logr has no WARN). FOLD-IN: consecutive-unhealthy-cycle count tracked per-project in r.memoryUnhealthyCycles (map on the reconciler, safe under MaxConcurrentReconciles=1; reads of a nil map return 0 so reconcileMemory needs no init). A cycle is unhealthy if ANY probed route is absent/error; a fully-present cycle clears the run; entries for projects no longer Ready are pruned each pass so a stale run cannot leak or carry back. reconcileMemory folds a SUSTAINED run (>= memoryRetrievalUnhealthyThreshold=3, ~3 min, rides out a transient blip / rolling restart) into the condition: a replica-Available stack reads MemoryReady=False/reason=RetrievalUnreachable instead of falsely green. DELIBERATE: the replica gate stays the precondition (a still-Provisioning stack is never probed) and status.memory.phase STAYS "Ready" - only the condition flips - so the probe keeps running and the condition self-clears on recovery. Like the lightrag gauge, the probe depends on ambient reconciles firing (owned-object watches + cron scans drive maybeRecomputeGauges, which sweeps ALL Ready projects on any project's reconcile); no special requeue added (KISS, consistent with the existing poller). SCOPE: detection only - authenticated query correctness / ranking quality stay out (memory eval-harness), and fixing the underlying deploy version-skew is a helmfile concern. Tests: probeMemoryRoute classification table + transport-fail; updateMemoryRetrievalProbe increments/clears/prunes/skips-non-Ready (httptest, toggleable 404<->401); reconcileMemory fold-in at/below threshold + recovery; obs metric + pre-seed. Branch tatara/fix-110.

2026-06-23 **Systemic-group implementation dedup: one brainstorm producing N connected issues no longer spawns N implementation agents.** Partial mechanism pre-existed: brainstorm calls propose_issue per repo sharing a `systemicId`, writeback stamps label `tatara/systemic-<id>` + footer, and proposalBacklogCount groups by that label for the backlog cap - but issueScan dedup keyed only on `repo#number`, so every issue in a systemic group spawned its own issueLifecycle Task. Fix = LEAD-PER-REPO: within each (systemicId, repo) the lowest open issue number is the lead and gets the only agent; it resolves all same-repo siblings in ONE combined PR (`Closes #A, Closes #C`) and is told about cross-repo siblings as reference-only context; non-lead siblings spawn no Task and get an idempotent `Tracked by #<lead> (systemic group). No separate agent.` comment (comment-only marking, no new label). Election is STATELESS - re-derived every scan from the open-issue candidates issueScan already lists across ALL project repos (electSystemicLeads(cands)); if a lead closes before the group drains, next-lowest auto-elects. Threading mirrors ReposInScope: new SystemicGroup{SystemicID, SameRepoSiblings []int, CrossRepo []string} on TaskSpec + QueuedEventPayload, mapped in BuildTaskFromQueuedEvent, injected into implementPrompt. New helpers in projectscan.go: systemicIDOf, electSystemicLeads, systemicMarker, commentSiblingMarker (idempotency keyed on the marker substring via ListIssueComments). createScanTask gained a trailing `systemicGroup *SystemicGroup` param (mrScan x2 + backstop pass nil). Metrics tatara_systemic_siblings_collapsed_total + tatara_systemic_groups_led_total. CRITICAL bug caught in opus review + regression-tested: election MUST run on the full pre-dedup `cands`, NOT the post-dedup `eligible` set - once a lead's Task is in-flight isDeduped drops the lead, the group shrinks to size<2, electSystemicLeads ignores it, and the surviving sibling (independent per-number dedup key) gets promoted to a second lead every cron cycle, defeating the dedup; the collapse gate still iterates `eligible` so a deduped lead is never re-enqueued. Out of scope: sequential re-election (chose combined PR), MaxPerRepo lane revival (see [[operator-laneoccupancy-starves-recovery-2026-06-15]]), DAG ordering. Spec docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-23-systemic-impl-dedup-design.md, plan docs/superpowers/plans/2026-06-23-systemic-impl-dedup.md. Branch feat/systemic-impl-dedup -> PR #124; deploy owed via tatara-helmfile (dual chart+image.tag pin) after merge.

2026-06-23 (issue #116) **Terminal-Failed diagnostics generalized beyond boot-crash: AgentUnreachable / TurnTimeout / PodLost now post their cause to the linked issue too.** Follow-up to [[issue #82]] (boot-crash diagnostics), which only commented on the BootCrashLoop terminal. The SCM plumbing of commentBootCrashDiagnostics was extracted into a reason-agnostic postTerminalComment(ctx,task,body) (gated on SCMFor!=nil + Source.IssueRef; project-scoped tasks with no repo skip via scmContext error - best-effort, log-and-continue). commentBootCrashDiagnostics keeps its richer pod.Status body (so its bootcrash_test assertions are unchanged) and now delegates the post; new commentTerminalDiagnostics(ctx,task,reason,detail) builds the generic "Task run terminated (`Failed` / `<reason>`)." body. Wired into the three TaskReconciler terminal-Failed call sites that previously commented nothing: PodLost (driveAgentRun exhausted), AgentUnreachable (handleAgentUnreachable past agentBootDeadline), TurnTimeout (driveTurns reconcile poll). These call sites live in SHARED agent-run code reached from BOTH Reconcile and reconcileLifecycle, so coverage is uniform across plain and issueLifecycle tasks. CRITICAL idempotency mirrors the boot-crash ordering: comment only AFTER terminate returns terr==nil (terminate commits Failed -> isTerminal short-circuits / lifecycle parks the run, so the call site never re-fires), so no marker annotation is needed and no double-post can occur. SCOPE DECISIONS: (1) merge-conflict is NOT terminal (lifecycle.go re-enters Implement on scm.ErrMergeConflict), so the issue body example does not apply - nothing to do there. (2) KNOWN GAP / deferred: the CallbackServer poll-backstop + planning-watchdog terminal writes (expireTimedOutTurn TurnTimeout, expireStalledPlanning PlanningStalled in turncallback.go) do NOT post a comment - the CallbackServer has no SCM wiring (no SCMFor/scmContext) and adding it would duplicate scmContext+token logic into a second struct. The reconcile path is the PRIMARY timeout detector (driveTurns self-requeues every pollRequeue), so the common turn-timeout case is covered; backstop-caught timeouts fall back to the terminal condition message + structured log (same as before, not a regression). Covering the backstop is a focused additive follow-up if desired. (3) live Pod-log streaming + crash-metric alerting (#68) remain deferred per the approved #82 design. Tests: terminal_diag_test.go (handleAgentUnreachable posts exactly one comment with reason+detail on the linked issue; generic body format; no-Source no-op) + unchanged bootcrash_test. Branch tatara/fix-116-follow-up-triage-issue-szymonrychu-tatar.

2026-06-24 (ledger Phase-3 review fixes) **Two-tier backstop sweep: opus review caught 4 critical/high correctness+migration bugs in the as-merged P3 code; all fixed on feat/task-work-item-ledger.** (1) CRITICAL podname-false-guard: backstopAction gated "no live pod" on `Status.PodName != ""`, but PodName is a deterministic name stamped ONCE at pod creation (task_controller.go:335) and NEVER cleared on Done/Stopped/Parked - every real stranded MR task already ran a pod so PodName is permanently non-empty -> Tier-2 was INERT for the entire stranded-MR population (the exact class the feature rescues, e.g. wrapper!50). Fix = backstopAction(task, podLive bool); sweep computes podLive via an actual pod Get (new ProjectReconciler.podIsLive: NotFound or Failed/Succeeded phase = not-live), mirroring the reconciler's own r.Get(agent.PodName(task)) liveness check. Fixtures now stamp PodName + LifecycleState=Parked (the production state) so they can't mask it. (2) CRITICAL seed-open mass-action hazard: refreshLedger did `continue` on any ListOpenPRs error, leaving lazily-seeded WIOpen unconfirmed, and backstopAction acted on it -> a single transient list error during the first post-deploy sweep could mass-Reactivate/CloseObsolete across ~1148 migrated terminal tasks. Fix = refreshLedger now returns (changed, confirmedPRRepos map[string]bool); the sweep SKIPS any Tier-2 action whose openedPR repo was not SCM-confirmed this sweep. (3) CRITICAL cross-mechanism dedup mismatch: backstop built createScanTask with labelCand=PR-number (dedupKey issueLifecycle\x00<repo>#<PRnum>) while mrScan keys on the linked issue (#<issueNum>); both run same tick (runScans) -> two QEs / two agents on one MR. Fix = new linkedIssueForPR(task,repo) derives the open role:source/closes issue # from the ledger and passes it as labelCand.number with srcCand=PR (createScanTask sets DedupNumber when they differ), so both paths share one dedup key; added hasLiveLifecycleTaskForIssue guard before create (mirrors mrScan). Regression-pinned by a test that runs mrScan+backstop with an ADVANCED PR head SHA (so mrScan isn't same-head-deduped and genuinely creates its own QE) and asserts exactly 1 QE - verified to FAIL (2 QEs) when labelCand reverts to PR#. (4) HIGH close-obsolete mislabel: the obsolete branch reused closeExhaustedPR -> posted "after 3 attempts" body + stamped tatara-recovery-exhausted on a 0-attempt PR (corrupts priorTerminalAttempts/adoption). Fix = separate closeObsoletePR posting a superseded note, no exhausted label. (5) MEDIUM off-by-one: a Parked stranded task counts toward its OWN priorTerminalAttempts; new priorTerminalAttemptsExcluding(...,excludeName) excludes the swept task (priorTerminalAttempts delegates with ""). (6) MEDIUM reactivate-with-no-source: backstopAction returned Reactivate even with zero source/closes issues; now requires an OPEN source issue else None (spec section 4). (7) MEDIUM role-predicate: hasOpenPR loop now uses Role==RoleOpenedPR (matching openPRCandidate) so a human role:reviewed PR is never targeted. DEFERRED (low, tracked here per reviewer guidance, NOT silently): refreshLedger records a PR absent from the open list as WIClosed even when MERGED (SCMReader has no merge signal; only SCMWriter.GetPRState does). Safe today (backstopAction only checks WIOpen, isWITerminal treats closed==merged), but Phase-4/5 prompt/backlog projection reads ledger State as authoritative - those phases MUST NOT treat a backstop-written WIClosed as a merge signal, or refreshLedger must gain GetPRState merged/closed disambiguation. Tests added: backstopAction(podLive) cases incl PodName-set-but-pod-gone->Reactivate, openPR-no-source->None, role:reviewed->None; sweep idempotency (twice -> 1 QE), cross-mechanism single-QE, no-action-on-fetch-error, Tier-1 persist round-trip (Re-Get asserts State==WIClosed + LastRefreshedAt), close-obsolete body+no-exhausted-label. Full suite + golangci-lint green.

(1) OBSERVABILITY: a failed *-ingest-* Job left no retained evidence (pods GC'd at TTL 600s, not promtail-scraped), so the operator logged only action=ingest_failed job=.. failure_count=.. Fix MIRRORS [[issue #82]]'s boot-crash capture: BuildJob (internal/ingest/job.go) now sets TerminationMessagePolicy=FallbackToLogsOnError on BOTH the clone init container and the ingest container, so the kubelet writes the failing container's log tail into ContainerStatus.State.Terminated.Message; handleFinishedJob (repository_controller.go) gained failedPodReason(job) which lists the Job's pods by label batch.kubernetes.io/job-name (canonical/non-deprecated; reuses the Pod informer TaskReconciler already Owns), picks the most-recently-started, walks init+main statuses for the first non-zero exit, and formats "<reason> (exit N): <msg>" (msg capped 512). The reason is folded into the Ingested=False condition Message (was generic "ingest job X failed"), the "ingest failed" structured log (reason field), and a NEW Warning Event "IngestFailed" on the Repository (survives pod GC). (2) 409-STORM: the six condition Status().Update(ctx,&repo) calls in Reconcile (clear-jobName, set/clear MemoryNotReady, clear/set IngestBackoff, launch) were the only status writes NOT wrapped in RetryOnConflict, losing to concurrent writers (handleFinishedJob/REST/webhook) and returning "the object has been modified" - a reconcile-error storm co-occurring with the alert. New patchStatus(ctx,repo,mutate func(*Repository) bool) error helper: RetryOnConflict + fresh-Get + idempotent re-apply on the fresh object, skips the write when mutate reports no change, copies persisted state back into repo; all six sites converted (the launch path also folds the formerly-standalone IngestRetrying SetStatusCondition into the same closure). The in-container ROOT CAUSE (most likely stale --since SHA / clone failure) and the ingester-side fix (emit a structured final ERROR to stderr + /dev/termination-log before exit) belong in tatara-memory-repo-ingester - a FOLLOW-UP (that repo was not on disk this turn); FallbackToLogsOnError captures whatever it prints today. Tests: job_test.go termination-policy on both containers; repository_ingest_reason_test.go (reason into condition+Event; no-pod fallback stays generic; patchStatus retries-on-conflict + skips-when-unchanged). Full controller suite + ingest + lint green. Branch tatara/fix-175-repository-controller-chronic-ingest-job.

2026-06-27 (issue #174, minor-bug fixup) **restapi PATCH /subtasks now normalizes status.phase case-insensitively to the CRD enum and 400s on unknown values.** Root cause of the `subtask_update` 500 incident: a caller-supplied lowercase `"done"` was written straight to SubtaskStatus.Phase, which the CRD `+kubebuilder:validation:Enum=Pending;Running;Done;Failed` schema rejects as an opaque k8s admission `Invalid` error; writeClientErr then surfaced it as a generic 500. 2026-06-27 (issue #143) **The SubmitTurn p95 latency alert is now a NaN-safe, version-controlled PrometheusRule instead of a hand-made Grafana rule.** The firing "Operator turn submit p95 latency high" rule lived only in Grafana (folder uid feod6r1mownpcc, not in any repo) and false-fired on every idle window >15m: `histogram_quantile(0.95, {all-zero bucket rates})` returns NaN, and Grafana's Reduce->Math->Threshold chain treats `NaN > 30` as firing (note: native PromQL `NaN > thr` actually FILTERS OUT, so a bare quantile rule would not fire on NaN - but the explicit traffic gate is belt-and-suspenders and self-documenting, which is what the maintainer approved). FIX: new alert `TataraTurnSubmitLatencyHigh` appended to the `tatara-loop` group in charts/tatara-operator/templates/prometheusrule.yaml as a NEW "Class C: latency / saturation" - the ONLY histogram_quantile alert in the group (every other alert is a counter/deadman `increase(...)>0` pattern, deliberately quantile-free; the inline comment explains why this one deviates and how the gate keeps it NaN-safe). Expression gates the quantile on traffic: `histogram_quantile(0.95, sum(rate(operator_turn_submit_duration_seconds_bucket[15m])) by (le)) > <thr> and sum(rate(operator_turn_submit_duration_seconds_count[15m])) > 0` - both sides reduce to an EMPTY label set so the `and` matches, and an idle window makes the count side empty so the whole expr yields NO series (never a NaN), for:15m. NON-OBVIOUS: (a) NO `namespace=`/`job=` selector baked (cluster-agnostic rule 14; the un-versioned Grafana rule hard-coded namespace="tatara",job="tatara-operator" - dropped, the operator_* metric name is already operator-scoped). (b) THRESHOLD reconciled against the histogram CEILING: operator_turn_submit_duration_seconds uses ExponentialBuckets(0.05,2,10) (obs/operator_metrics.go:177) -> top finite bucket 0.05*2^9 = 25.6s + +Inf, so histogram_quantile can never return >25.6s; the old 30s threshold was unreachable by a true p95 (only the NaN path could trip it). Lowered to 5s, configurable via NEW values.yaml scalar `prometheusRule.turnSubmitP95LatencyThreshold: 5` (mirrors the tasksInflightThreshold precedent) - ~6.7x the ~0.77s steady-state p95 (verified live: bare quantile = 0.7697 under traffic), well under the 25.6s ceiling. (c) $value escaped as `{{ "{{" }} $value {{ "}}" }}` so Prometheus (not Helm) renders the measured p95 in the summary - the literal "NaNs" tell from the old alert is gone. Validated read-only via Grafana MCP (datasource prometheus): full gated expr parses and returns EMPTY now (0.77 < 5 = correctly not firing); helm template + helm lint green. Chart version bumped 0.4.8 -> 0.4.9 (chart-content change; appVersion unchanged, no Go code touched). Secondary ~20% SubmitTurn error-ratio observation left OUT OF SCOPE (overlaps [[issue #174]]). Branch tatara/fix-143-operator-turn-submit-p95-latency-high-al.

2026-07-04 (issue #215) **Memory readiness gates on a serving QUORUM of CNPG instances, not all of them, so a single replica loss no longer cascades to a full memory outage.** Incident: an infra event dropped the `pg-1` streaming REPLICA of BOTH memory CNPG clusters (`mem-tatara-pg`, `mem-infrastructure-pg`, both `pgInstances: 3`) for ~10h (17:16Z->03:30Z 07-03/04); LightRAG call error ratio sat at 100% until a manual restart. Root-cause AMPLIFIER (confirmed in code, not just logs): `memoryPhase` (internal/controller/project_memory.go) required `readyInstances >= wantInstances` with `wantInstances = memory.PgInstances(p) = 3`, so `Cluster.Status.ReadyInstances=2 < 3` flipped memory phase to Provisioning and gated ALL tasks - turning a degraded-but-primary-serving cluster into a fully not-ready subsystem. FIX: new `memoryQuorum(wantInstances) = wantInstances/2 + 1` (strict majority, floored at 1); memoryPhase now gates `readyInstances >= memoryQuorum(...)` (neo4j/lightrag/memory `>=1` checks unchanged). Single-instance default keeps quorum 1 (unchanged behavior); a 3-node HA cluster is Ready at 2/3 (primary + 1 replica) and only Provisioning at <=1/3. NON-OBVIOUS: the generated CNPG Cluster (internal/memory/pg.go) carries NO PostgresConfiguration, so CNPG defaults to ASYNC replication - the primary already serves through a replica loss at the DB level, so NO sync-replication/cluster change was needed (and adding synchronous replication would be COUNTERPRODUCTIVE: it would stall the primary's writes whenever a standby is missing). The over-strict operator gate was the ONLY defect in this repo; `memory.PgInstances` stays the single source of truth (only the threshold transform changed from identity to quorum, preserving the R3F1 invariant). Tests: updated project_memory_r3_audit_test.go (2/3 now asserts Ready, <quorum asserts Provisioning), extended TestMemoryPhase_Transitions (single-pg-down / below-quorum / quorum / full boundary), new TestMemoryQuorum. OUT OF SCOPE (separate repos, flagged on the issue): tatara-memory app-level LightRAG resilience (retry/circuit-break/degrade-not-fail so a transient backend blip doesn't yield 100% errors), tatara-observability Prometheus TSDB retention + shipping tatara-memory app logs to Loki (the two forensics gaps). build/vet/gofmt/golangci-lint + controller(full)+memory suites green; -race NOT run locally (sandbox has no gcc; CI runs it). Branch tatara/fix-215-memory-lightrag-100-error-ratio-10h-sing.

2026-07-04 (issue #189, usage-gate whole-branch review) **claudeSubscription per-kind spawn ceiling now actually governs (was inert), plus poller-produced metrics, resume requeue, and kind+activity keying.** Whole-branch review of feat/usage-window-gating found the headline per-kind ladder was dead: `admitPool` short-circuited on the coarse pool-class Decision (`ProactiveBlocked`/`EmergencyBlocked`, default 50/80) and RETURNED before the per-kind loop, so the whole normal pool froze at 50% and incidents at 80% - `incident:98`/`refine:55` never took effect. FIXES: (F1) the account-usage hold is now decided PER EVENT in `admit` (queue_controller.go): in claudeSubscription mode there is NO wholesale short-circuit; each queued event is held iff its resolved ceiling key is in `SpawnCeilingByKind` (`budget.KindBlocked`, reason `kind_ceiling`) else it falls through to the pool-class proactive/emergency decision (reason `token_budget`). customWindow (and disabled) mode keeps the exact old per-pool short-circuit (`subscription := cfg.Enabled && Mode==claudeSubscription` guards it). (F5) `ceilingKey(cfg,q)` resolves activity-then-kind, mirroring `modelForKind`/`effortForKind` precedence: a non-empty `LabelActivity` value that is itself a configured ceiling key wins, so healthCheck work (enqueued Kind=brainstorm + activity=healthCheck) is governed by the healthCheck ceiling not brainstorm's. (F2) `admit` now also returns `heldOnUsage`; Reconcile requeues held work after `usageRequeueAfter()` (the poll interval when the new `DispatcherReconciler.UsagePollInterval` is wired, else 60s) because the fleet Store is not a watched resource and nothing else re-triggers when usage later drops. (F3/F4/F8) the POLLER is now the sole metrics producer via a `PollerMetrics` interface (accountusage/poller.go): every successful poll emits utilization+reset for all four windows + overage + poll-health=true; every failure increments the NEW `tatara_account_usage_poll_failures_total` and, at the failure threshold, sets poll-health=false (the old code left the gauge 1-forever because the success-only onUpdate hook was the only producer - a dead endpoint read healthy). `onUpdate` (wire.go) now mirrors the ConfigMap ONLY. Poll-health is seeded to a defined value before the first poll. (F6) wire.go now `slog.Warn`s on mirror Load/Save errors (rule 12) instead of dropping them. F7 (CONSCIOUS DE-SCOPE, do-not-build): the spec's "fall back to customWindow when the snapshot is stale" is moot - a claudeSubscription Project has NO customWindow inputs (TokenLimit/ResetSchedule) to fall back to. Kept the current stale behavior (gate on last-known windows until each expires via `budget.active()`, i.e. eventual fail-open), which the reviewer rated safety-acceptable now that F3 makes staleness VISIBLE and the wrapper OTel 429 floor is the hard backstop; a one-line comment marks the stale-read site in Reconcile. NEW envtest coverage (the gap that let F1/F2/F5 through), queue_usage_gate_test.go: incident:98 admits at 85% while brainstorm:40 is held (proves the fix escapes the old emergency-80 short-circuit); per-kind hold requeues at 60s with pool-class NOT blocked and resumes when usage drops to 30%; healthCheck-activity event governed by healthCheck:60 not brainstorm:40. build/vet/golangci-lint(2.12.2) + full suite incl controller envtest green. Branch feat/usage-window-gating.

2026-07-05 (usage-gate follow-up) **`refine` is now NEVER held on the account-usage gate, even when `spawnCeilingByKind["refine"]` is configured.** Root cause: `refine` is a scan-pipeline BARRIER, not ordinary per-kind work - `projectscan.go` `runScans` (~line 2751) defers mrScan/issueScan/brainstorm/healthCheck until a refine Task reaches a terminal state (Succeeded or Failed), with the barrier's only safety valve being that terminal check. The per-event account-usage hold in `admit`/`admitPool` (queue_controller.go) held ANY kind whose `ceilingKey` crossed its ceiling, including refine - so a held refine sat Queued forever (never runs, never terminates), wedging the barrier and every scan behind it, silently defeating the graduated ladder for the whole project. FIX: in the per-event subscription hold block, `if key == "refine" { held = false }` short-circuits after the normal ceiling computation - refine always admits regardless of any configured ceiling; all other kinds are unaffected. Consequence: `refine` is deliberately dropped from the default `spawnCeilingByKind` ladder in the design spec/plan (parent tatara repo docs) but stays a valid CRD CEL enum key (harmless if set, just never enforced). New envtest `TestDispatcherSubscription_RefineNeverGated` (queue_usage_gate_test.go): refine:55 + brainstorm:40 ceilings at 60% usage - refine admits, brainstorm held. build/vet/golangci-lint + full suite incl controller envtest green.

2026-07-05: push-CD live - agents must not self-merge; release.yml + cd-release cut tags and propagate pins; deploys land via tatara-helmfile deploy-train.

2026-07-06 **Documentation bot PRs now auto-merge without a declared significance.** tatara-documentation is not a versioned artifact (only a `Build` mkdocs check; no `release.yml` / semver tag). The push-CD auto-merge (`applySemverAutoMerge`, writeback.go) enables GitHub native auto-merge ONLY when the agent declared a change significance - it stamps the `semver:<level>` label AND enables auto-merge together (returns early on `cs == nil || cs.Significance == ""`). So documentation bot PRs, which declare no significance, never auto-merged - they were merged by hand (tatara-documentation #1/#2, mergedBy szymonrychu). FIX: extracted the bot-login-gated `EnableAutoMerge` tail into a shared `enableNativeAutoMerge` helper; the writeback PR-open path branches on kind - `documentation` calls the helper directly (auto-merge on the Build check, gated only on a configured bot login, NO inert semver label), all other kinds keep the significance-gated `applySemverAutoMerge` unchanged. Chose direct-unconditional over synthesizing a `patch` significance (which would stamp a meaningless label on docs and misuse the semver cascade). Repo side already configured: tatara-documentation has `allow_auto_merge=true` + branch protection requiring `Build`. New envtest subtest `TestWriteBackOpenChange_SemverLabelAndAutoMerge/documentation kind` asserts a documentation task with nil ChangeSummary enables auto-merge + stamps no label. Full suite + golangci-lint green. NOTE: the doc kind also has no cli tool profile (fail-open full surface) and `toolProfileForKind`->"documentation" has no matching cli `profiles` key - unrelated to this fix but worth a look.

2026-07-11 (task-kind-redesign Phase 7 + Phase-8 item 3) **Permission-layer comment guard, clarify 1h kill, discrete-flow enterDeploying.** (1) `controller.PermitComment` (comment_gate.go, exported) is the MCP/REST self-comment refusal: bot-last-word -> refuse, SOLE exception `kind=="refine"`. Enforced at restapi `commentOnIssue` (the shared brainstorm+refine comment egress; the ONLY agent-initiated direct SCM comment write - clarify/implement/review post via issue_outcome/the reconciler drain). restapi IMPORTS internal/controller for this (+ exported `CommentSilenceBreakers`); verified no import cycle (controller has zero restapi dep). Kind at that endpoint is inferred (shared-OIDC, same limit as authorizeCaller): owning-Task-by-Source-issue else in-flight-refine-Task -> "refine". This loosened brainstorm from cap-1 "one comment ever" to bot-last-word turn-taking (intended uniform guard). (2) Clarify's live discuss window is a FIXED 60min wall-clock kill (`clarifyDiscussTimeoutMinutes`), decoupled from project ConversationIdleMinutes (enterConversation kind-branch). handleClarifyConversation replaces the shared handleConversation for clarify: it OMITS observeProposalLabelReadback (which drives approved->Implement, a deploy-half state clarify must never reach) - a correctness fix, not just a timeout. Stall (no interjection at deadline) -> deleteWrapper + Parked/"clarify-timeout" (Parked not Stopped so ParkReason persists). (3) The discrete implement Task goes TERMINAL (Succeeded) after opening its PR, so `superviseMergedPRs` (ProjectReconciler) RESURRECTS it into Phase=Deploying on merge (safe: task_controller.go:167 routes any Phase=Deploying task to reconcileDeploying regardless of kind). Merge detected READ-ONLY via GetPRState (catches native-auto-merge + superviseApprovedPRs; NO new writer.Merge - single egress mergePRSquash preserved). Durable double-deploy fence = DeployLedger seen-set (a resolved-but-not-yet-GC'd terminal implement task would otherwise re-resurrect every tick). Shared `stampDeploying` free func is the single deploy-transition impl (enterDeploying refactored to it - keeps the "orphaned enterDeploying" landmine at bay). Full gate green (envtest); exactly one writer.Merge site.

2026-07-11 (task-kind-redesign FINAL cleanup: LifecycleState->DeployState rename + bridge assessment) **DeployState rename kept the JSON tag `lifecycleState`.** Renamed Go `Status.LifecycleState`->`DeployState` (agent-invisible, deploy-supervisor-only) and the whole identifier family (const DeployStateDeploying, setDeployState, obs SetDeployState/updateDeployStateCounts/gatherDeployState) via a case-sensitive global `LifecycleState`->`DeployState`. DELIBERATELY did NOT change the struct tag: it stays `json:"lifecycleState,omitempty"`. Rationale over the plan's "deployState tag + Deprecated LifecycleState alias field" (task_types.go 3a Step 3): keeping the lowercase JSON key means (a) grep-gate `LifecycleState`=0 with no reintroduced alias identifier, (b) stored CRs deserialize unchanged, (c) ZERO CRD drift (printcolumn `.status.lifecycleState`, enum, key all stable - no manifests churn), (d) the AGENT-visible task_list field stays `lifecycleState`, so refine/goal.go's `lifecycleState == "Parked"` selection directive stays valid, (e) no first-reconcile mirror. The enum keeps all 10 values (Triage..Parked) because the issueLifecycle drain still writes the front-half states. obs metric NAMES (tatara_lifecycle_*) are lowercase -> untouched -> observability contract preserved. **issueLifecycle bridge is webhook-retired but NOT strictly drain-only:** webhook produces clarify/review (tested), but the CRON issueScan(1666)/mrScan-bot-PR(1279)/backstop(2778, backstop.go 383/420)/recoverOrphans still PRODUCE issueLifecycle as the catch-all + bot-PR-CI-recovery + orphan-drain. Kept because converting them is a shared-machinery rework: issueScan adoption (adoptLifecycleTask re-enters DeployState=Triage) is a bridge op with no clarify analogue AND is shared with the drain; mrScan bot-PR enters MRCI supervision the discrete flow replaces with superviseApprovedPRs/superviseMergedPRs (kind-gated to skip issueLifecycle = no double-deploy); backstop/recoverOrphans re-adopting in-flight issueLifecycle IS the drain. Full producer conversion (~15 test files, adoption/systemic/bot-PR-recovery core) is a dedicated follow-up, deferred to protect drain + green. **Dropped dead retired-healthCheck code:** healthCheck()/createHealthCheckTask()/healthCheckInFlightProject() had zero production callers (Phase-5 dropped the cron dispatch) - deleted them + their TestHealthCheck_* tests. Kept healthCheckGoalProject (still a goal-render test fixture in 6 files) + seedHealthCheckProject/listHealthCheckQEs (used by TestHealthCheckCronDropped) + inert ScmCron.HealthCheck/Status.LastHealthCheck back-compat fields.

2026-07-11 (concurrency/race hardening - 6 findings) **Get-fresh-then-blind-overwrite under RetryOnConflict gives zero protection** (a full overwrite never conflicts); each fix now mutates `fresh` from its OWN contents / re-asserts the precondition inside the retry. (1) umbrella.go buildUmbrellaPromptFor + backstop.go backstopSweep persisted refreshed members via `fresh.Status.WorkItems = <snapshot>`, dropping a concurrently-appended PR (joinStreamReview) -> review approves a stream MISSING a PR. FIX: merge per-member via `UpsertWorkItem` into the fresh read; extended UpsertWorkItem to also carry the umbrella member-state fields (Labels/Body/CIStatus/Mergeable) so the merge-refresh stays lossless. (2) cdScan reroll (setTaskImplementContext+adoptLifecycleTaskAt) blindly overwrote a Task that resolveDeployedSweep had concurrently resolved to Done -> duplicate prod deploy. FIX: new guarded `cdRerollStalled` re-asserts TaskDeploying(fresh)+deadline-exceeded in ONE status write, aborts otherwise (removed setTaskImplementContext). (3) webhook handleWorkItem had no bot-SENDER check on labeled events (unlike the comment path) -> operator's own tatara-implementation write on a clarify->implement handoff re-spawned a clarify Task that re-stamped brainstorming. FIX: drop bot-actor issues.labeled/unlabeled (scoped `!ev.IsPR` so GitLab MR bot-actor still reviews), AND setLifecycleLabel now refuses a brainstorming re-stamp when the issue already carries the implementation label (enforces one-of-4). (4) concurrent stream PR-creates: loser accepted as "duplicate", PR never joined. FIX: createStreamReview created==false arm falls through to joinStreamReview. RESIDUAL: only effective once the winner's review Task has materialized from its QueuedEvent (async), so NOT synchronously unit-testable; bot PRs are covered anyway by seedReviewSpanFromUmbrella (they land in the umbrella ledger), the gap is an external PR on a bot branch in the tight pre-materialization window. (5) setLifecycleLabel list->add->remove is 3 non-atomic SCM calls, no CAS; TaskReconciler/ProjectReconciler/webhook interleave -> 0 or 2 managed phase labels. FIX: re-list current labels immediately before the removes (remove only labels the FRESH read still shows), add-then-verify re-adds a concurrently-stripped desired. RESIDUAL (documented in code): two controllers asserting DIFFERENT desired phase labels at the same instant stay logically racy - re-list narrows the mechanical window but can't serialize conflicting intents without a distributed lock; in practice one producer drives a given issue's phase and the impl-guard blocks the highest-impact conflict. (6) handleMerge + superviseApprovedPRs both merge an approved issueLifecycle PR; the loser's GitHub 405 -> ErrMergeConflict -> handleMerge rerolled an ALREADY-MERGED change to Implement. FIX: before classifying a merge error as conflict, re-fetch GetPRState; if Merged, treat as success and advance to MainCI idempotently (records mergedHead as MergeCommitSHA - PRState carries no squash SHA; downstream deploy matches by version tag not commit). Full gate green (generate/manifests no drift, lint 0, envtest, build); single writer.Merge egress (mergePRSquash) preserved.

2026-07-11 (task-kind-redesign: discrete-flow deploy cascade made reachable + per-member) **superviseMergedPRs/reconcileDeploying/resolve now drive off `role:openedPR` WorkItem MEMBERS, not the single `Status.PRNumber` scalar - the discrete `implement` deploy-supervision + issue-auto-close was DEAD.** Root cause: `superviseMergedPRs` gated `PRNumber==0 -> continue`, but `Status.PRNumber` is written ONLY on the issueLifecycle path (lifecycle_implement finishImplement); the discrete umbrella writeback (writeBackOpenChange) sets only `Status.PrURL` + `role:openedPR` members, never PRNumber. So every discrete implement Task was skipped forever -> never Deploying -> issue never auto-closed (and `Closes #N` is suppressed for pushCDEligible, by design). Also the whole supervisor was single-artifact (scalar RepositoryRef/DeployArtifact/DeployedVersion) while a discrete umbrella carries N openedPR members across N repos. FIX (per-member tracking via WorkItemRef, NOT a new ledger): extended `WorkItemRef` with `DeployedVersion` + `DeployState` (""|deploying|applied), carried through the conflict-safe `UpsertWorkItem` merge primitive (the concurrency chunk's contract - mutate fresh in place, never blind-overwrite Status.WorkItems). (1) `superviseMergedPRs` rewritten member-driven: polls each member READ-ONLY via GetPRState (no new writer.Merge - single egress mergePRSquash preserved), flips WIMerged/WIClosed on the ledger; enters Deploying (`enterDeployingUmbrella`) only once EVERY non-closed member merged; seeds each merged member DeployState=deploying. Gate = `umbrellaDeployEligible` (implement kind, issue source, pushCDEligible, not Deploying/Done/Parked) - the durable double-deploy fence is now the Task's own phase, NOT the deploy-ledger (umbrella uses per-member WorkItem fields; the ledger stays for the scalar issueLifecycle path). NOTE: `isWITerminal` treats WIMerged as terminal, so `umbrellaPRMembers` (review path) EXCLUDES merged - the deploy path needs its OWN `openedPRDeployMembers` iterator that INCLUDES WIMerged (merged is exactly what deploys). (2) `reconcileDeploying` branches on `Kind=="implement"` -> `reconcileDeployingUmbrella` (per-member: learn each member's cut tag via LatestSemverTag, confirm each member's OWN pin via pinCarriesArtifactVersion(pinState, memberRepoName, ver), persist DeployState=applied per member so applies across DIFFERENT helmfile apply runs accumulate); scalar path unchanged for issueLifecycle. (3) CONFIRM-ALL: `resolveDeployedUmbrella` closes the issue ONLY when `allMembersApplied` (every merged member DeployState==applied), with a combined `<art@ver>, ...` comment. Extracted `closeIssueOnDeploy` shared by scalar+umbrella resolve (single close-egress). A stuck member keeps the issue open. (4) PRE-MERGE DEADLINE (was: discrete implement went Succeeded terminal, only superviseApprovedPRs watched merge with NO deadline -> a member stuck non-green sat open+approved forever): new `Status.MergeWaitDeadline` stamped on first sight; a stream whose member(s) stay unmerged past `Project.Spec.MergeWaitBudgetMinutes` (default 720/12h) is parked recoverable (`mergeParkReason="merge-timeout"`) with an issue comment NAMING the stuck member repo(s); cdScan CD-health failed gauge now counts mergeParkReason too. (5) cdScan DEFAULT-ON: `ScmCron.CDScan` is now its OWN type `CDScanActivity` with a field-level `Schedule` default `*/10 * * * *`. CRITICAL: an object-level `+kubebuilder:default={schedule:...}` on the old `CronActivity` field DID NOT WORK - a struct field with omitempty is ALWAYS serialized, so the apiserver saw cdScan present-but-empty and never applied the object default; a defaulted STRING field IS omitted-when-empty so its field default fires. Reroll/park machinery (rerollDeploy) unchanged - umbrella deadline reroll names stuck members in the fix prompt. Kept issueLifecycle scalar path byte-for-byte. New tests deploy_umbrella_test.go: enters-Deploying-when-all-merged; waits-when-a-member-unmerged; parks-stuck-member-with-comment-past-deadline; stays-open-until-all-applied; closes-when-all-applied; cdScan-defaults-on. Full gate green; single writer.Merge egress.

2026-07-11 (human-approval gate: EXPLICIT MAINTAINER APPROVAL is the ONLY release into implement) **Core safety promise made real in the operator - previously a drive-by comment OR open-by-default third-party authorship OR raw approved-label PRESENCE released the whole autonomous implement->review->merge->deploy chain with NO verified human approval.** New durable `Task.Status.ApprovedByMaintainer` (login string) records the identity-verified fact that a MaintainerLogins member applied the approved label. Set ONLY by the webhook (server.go handleWorkItem) on `issues.labeled{approved}` whose ACTOR is `IsMaintainer` (new api/v1alpha1 helper: EffectiveMaintainerLogins membership, CLOSED-by-default = empty list approves nobody, bot structurally excluded even if misconfigured into the list). Bot-set approved labels never reach recording (dropped by the pre-existing bot-actor labeled-event guard) - that IS the structural agent/bot exclusion. EVERY front-half->implement release path now gates on the recorded fact, fail-closed to Conversation otherwise: (1) finishFrontHalf implement arm (lifecycle_triage.go) - REMOVED thirdPartyAuthor + hasHumanReply release entirely (deleted thirdPartyAuthor + its tests; hasHumanReply retained only for discuss/close-withheld comment-silence gates); (2) handleConversation approved-label readback (lifecycle_conversation.go) - label presence still projects WIApproved onto the ledger for observability but drives Implement ONLY when ApprovedByMaintainer set (an agent could set the label; ListOpenIssues can't tell who applied it); (3) webhook trigger-label Conversation->Implement jump - now gated on IsMaintainer(actor) + records the approval (was: ANY non-bot actor jumped an issueLifecycle Conversation task straight to Implement); (4) backstop recoverOrphans approved-labeled orphan now recovers at Triage not Implement (implementation-labeled orphan still resumes at Implement - past-the-gate in-flight work). Webhook records approval + re-drives Conversation/Stopped/Parked->Triage so the gate re-evaluates (mirrors comment reactivation). RESIDUAL: backstop still trusts `tatara-implementation` label PRESENCE for orphan resume (an agent forging that label could resurrect at Implement) - the proper fix is SCM label-write ACLs, out of this gate's scope; GitLab actor IS available on label events (p.User.Username) so the maintainer-actor check works both providers. Docs/skills (tatara-mcp-scm-lifecycle / tatara-clarify-conversation) must say: a MAINTAINER approves by applying the `tatara-approved` label to the issue (a comment does NOT approve; the project MUST configure MaintainerLogins or nothing ever implements). Full gate green (generate/manifests no drift, lint 0, envtest -race, build); single writer.Merge egress preserved.

- 2026-07-11: Hardened bot identity behind the approval gate. `Effective{Maintainer,Reporter}Logins` now strip the project bot login (no runtime effect if misconfigured into a list, incl. per-repo overrides); CRD CEL + MinLength reject a Project with empty `botLogin` or the bot login in `maintainerLogins`/`reporterLogins`. Deliberately left the bot's IMPLICIT trust in `IsAllowedReporter`/`IsTrustedAuthor` (hardcoded, load-bearing for bot-authored issue intake + unlabeled bot-PR review) untouched - both check the bot before the stripped list. The two object-level CEL rules (`self.maintainerLogins.all(...)`) blew the apiserver's CEL cost budget (>100x) against the previously-unbounded `[]string` fields - added `MaxItems=100` + item `MaxLength=100` on `maintainerLogins`/`reporterLogins` and `MaxLength=100` on `botLogin` to bound the estimate; not anticipated by the task brief but required for the CRD to even install (envtest caught it). Two pre-existing tests constructed an empty-`botLogin` `ScmSpec` via `k8sClient.Create` to exercise runtime "no bot configured" branches - now admission-blocked; fixed by giving `TestLifecycleImplement_LegacyImplementTaskDoesNotClose` a real bot login (incidental to that test) and switching `TestWriteBackOpenChange_SemverLabelAndAutoMerge`'s "no bot login" subtest to a nil `Scm` (still optional at the `ProjectSpec` level, same runtime branch, same as several sibling subtests already do).
