2026-07-11 (scan stale-event cutoff: durable per-item high-water mark, issue #285) **A fresh operator restart re-triaged still-open GitHub issues whose "already handled" record was gone - the cron issueScan/mrScan create a Task for any open item with no LIVE matching Task, but terminal Tasks are GC'd after TaskRetention, so a long-handled issue looked brand-new on boot and spawned a stale agent pod (e.g. tatara-tatara-gh-tatara-operator-issue-285).** Root cause was purely the cron poll, not informer relist (ensurePodAndService is Get-or-Create idempotent) nor webhook redelivery (webhook ingress dedups on live Tasks with deterministic names). Fix: new durable `ProjectStatus.ScanMarks []ScanMark` (repo, number, isPR, accountedAt) recording the last GitHub UpdatedAt each scan accounted for; a freshness gate in issueScanPickOne and mrScan's bot-PR branch skips re-triage when `UpdatedAt <= mark` (metric outcome `skipped_stale_mark`), and every scanned candidate's mark is upserted + pruned-to-open-set via persistScanMarks (RetryOnConflict merge, scoped by isPR so the two scans never clobber). Rejected a process-start-timestamp cutoff (clock skew; silently drops issues genuinely created during downtime, whose UpdatedAt predates the new start). The existing issue #188 botHadLastWord gate already covers first-sight bot-engaged items, so "adopt-baseline" needed no special branch - the mark is simply recorded for those items too. Files: api/v1alpha1/project_types.go (type+field), internal/controller/scanmarks.go (helpers+persist), internal/controller/projectscan.go (both gates + persist), scan_stale_mark_test.go. OUT OF SCOPE / follow-up: mrScan's priorTerminalAttempts recovery-exhaustion counter reads live Tasks only and silently resets to 0 on GC - a separate recovery-cap defect, not a stale-spawn defect.

2026-07-11 (autonomy/dedup/CRD-hygiene Phase 1: comment gate closed-state + dedup + gatedCommentCore) **Comment posting consolidated through one gate for both reconcilers.** `decideCommentGate` gained `gateClosed`/`gateDedup` rules (GetPRState/new `SCMWriter.GetIssueState` for closed; `duplicateRecentBotComment` normalizes turn-counter/timestamp-stripped body match) and an `incident` `PermitComment` carve-out (sequential evidence comments on its own tracker issue are expected, not a loop). Extracted receiver-independent `gatedCommentCore`; `TaskReconciler.gatedComment` and new `ProjectReconciler.gatedComment` both wrap it. Converted the 9 remaining raw `writer.Comment()` sites (writeback.go x3, lifecycle_implement.go x2, writeback_review.go, deploy_supervision.go x2, projectscan.go x2); `lifecycle.go:627`/`:940` left unconverted per their own in-code "intentional bypass" comments. Two judgment calls that deviated from the plan as drafted: (1) the plan's two dedup test fixtures were unreachable under existing `botHasLastWordAmong` semantics (a lone bot comment with no breaker always trips rule-1 first) - fixed the fixtures to include a breaker reply rather than reordering rule priority, which would have silently widened rule-1's existing turn-taking silence; (2) the plan's `gatedComment` wrapper only called `recordSCM` `if posted`, silently dropping the SCM-write-error metric for a real (non-suppressed) post that failed - changed to `if posted || err != nil`. `deploy_supervision.go`'s two ProjectReconciler sites pass `repo=nil` (accepted gap, no Repository CR resolvable there without an extra List) per the design's own risk note; `projectscan.go`'s two sites instead resolve a real repo from the already-in-scope `repos` slice, so closed/dedup fully apply there. Also added the item-1 root-cause adjacent fix (PR #295): `TaskReconciler.reviewTargetClosed` (GetPRState) checked both before a fresh review turn spawns (task_controller.go) and before `writeBackReview` posts any verdict verb, independent of the comment gate (covers approve/request_changes, not just the comment decision). Webhook `isBotActor` extracted + applied at `handleIssueComment` and defensively at `createClarifyTask`'s entry. REST `commentOnIssue` gained `IsPR` (PRCommentLister + '!' separator on GitLab, fixing the PR-thread read bug) + closed-state/dedup parity with the reconciler gate. `make test -race` + `golangci-lint` + `make build` green throughout.

2026-07-11 (follow-up) Final review found the clarify->implement handoff producer (issueScan's second Task-creating loop, `needsImplementProducer`) had the same GC-rescan gap as the gated triage/mrScan paths: a GC'd implement Task left an open implementation-labeled issue re-satisfying the producer on every scan. Gated it with the same ScanMarks freshness check. Two same-class gaps left intentionally unfixed (spec scope): mrScan's human-authored-PR review branch (`c.author != bot`) - re-reviewing an unchanged open PR is low-harm, gate it too if stale review pods become a problem - and `buildScanMarks` pruning only within repos scanned this cycle, so marks for a repo removed from a Project leak permanently (bounded by repo churn; add a cap or full reconcile if churn grows).

2026-07-12 (post-Phase-8 review fixes, 9 findings) Adversarial review of the Phase 1-8 work above surfaced 9 findings; all fixed, 6 commits. **HIGH/prod-blocking:** (1) auto-approve (item 4a) never checked whether a human had closed the tracked proposal issue - the operator would still implement+deploy after a human veto. Fixed by reading `GetIssueState` live before `recordAutoApproval` (withhold+park on Closed or any read error, fail closed) plus a companion webhook handler (`handleWorkItem`) that parks any owning non-terminal Task on an inbound issue-`closed` event from a non-bot actor (the operator's own `triageCloseIssue` close is bot-actor and explicitly excluded). (2) `RepositoryReconciler.computeRepoCounts` sat AFTER the `IngestEnabled` early-return, so non-ingested repos never got their printcolumn counts - moved above it. **MED:** (3) `recordAutoApproval` blindly overwrote `Status.ApprovedByMaintainer` inside its `RetryOnConflict` closure - a concurrent label/conversational approval landing in the race window got clobbered. Now re-checks inside the closure and no-ops (reflects the winning value, returns `recorded=false`) when another approval already landed; signature changed to `(bool, error)`. (4) `isBotAuthoredProposal` trusted `Source.AuthorLogin` unconditionally, but that's the webhook ACTOR on GitLab (not the author) - gated the same way `resolveBotMR` already was: trust the hint only for `provider=="github"`, verify live via `GetIssueState` on GitLab, fail closed (not bot-authored) on a nil writer or read error. Signature grew `(ctx, writer, repoURL, token, provider, proj, task)`; both call sites (`labels.go` ledger producer, `lifecycle_triage.go` auto-approve gate) updated. (5) `maybeOpenFollowupIssue` never called `syncSiblingLinks` after appending to `DiscoveredIssues` - item-5 cross-links only ever seeded via the brainstorm path; added the same `discoveredIssueSiblings`-gated call `completeProposal` already makes. (6) `triagePostComment`'s bypass of the comment gate was justified only for rule-1 (already turn-taking-gated upstream) but silently also skipped the closed-state and content-dedup rules for its OTHER callers (auto-approve audit comment, close-withheld note) - routed through `gatedComment` (all 4 rules); costs one extra non-memoized `ListIssueComments` call per post (accepted, updated the two hardcoded call-count assertions in `lifecycle_comments_memoize_test.go`). **LOW:** (7) follow-up issues only stamped `tataraAuthoredMarker`, not `tataraProposedByMarker("followup")` - added for provenance-spec completeness. (8) The two `deploy_supervision.go` nil-Repository `gatedComment` sites skipped the WHOLE gate (all 4 rules) because `gatedCommentCore` required `repo!=nil` unconditionally - turned out cheap to fix in full: owner/repo is derivable from `ref` alone via `RepoFromIssueRef`, and `CommentSilenceBreakers`/`Effective*Logins` were already nil-repo-safe (fall back to project level), so ALL 4 rules (not just closed+dedup as originally scoped) now apply without a Repository CR. Required adding a `ListIssueComments` stub to the `umbReader` test fixture (`deploy_umbrella_test.go`), which the gate is now reachable through at those two sites for the first time - a pre-existing test (`TestParkUmbrellaMergeTimeout_StillPostsViaGate`) still passes unaffected because its `ProjectReconciler` never sets `ReaderFor`, so the gate short-circuits there regardless of `repo`. (9) `matchIncidentByDedupKey` compared a caller's AlertRule-name dedup-fallback identity against candidates' raw (often empty) `DedupKey` field, so a legacy pre-migration incident Task could never match - fixed by having candidates degrade to the same AlertRule fallback when their own `DedupKey` is empty, mirroring `incidentAlertGroup`'s own fallback logic (duplicated inline rather than shared cross-package, since `incidentAlertGroup` lives in `internal/restapi`). TDD throughout (new failing test per fix, confirmed red, then green); `go test ./... -race -count=1` + `golangci-lint run ./...` (0 issues) + `make build` all green after every commit. No `api/` changes, so no `make generate manifests` needed this pass.

2026-07-11 (autonomy/dedup/CRD-hygiene Phases 5-8: printcolumns/counts, Subtask rollup, issue/PR links, autoclean) **Task 7/9 derived-status fields (ShortDescription, IssueLinks, PRLinks) are computed at the very TOP of `TaskReconciler.Reconcile`, in one combined `patchTaskStatus` call, not at the plan's suggested "same site as `deriveResultSummary`" (which only runs once at termination).** Deviation was deliberate: the whole point of "kubectl get is scannable without describe" is visibility while a Task is still Running/Planning, and issueLifecycle/clarify kinds return early via `reconcileLifecycle`/`reconcileClarify` before ever reaching termination - so the narrower site would leave those two kinds (most of the fleet) permanently blank. Cost: this adds one extra `Status().Update` at the front of every Task reconcile pass, which broke `TestDoWriteBack_ClearErrorPropagated`'s injected-first-call-fails test double (`errOnClearClient`) - fixed by parameterizing it with a `callNum` (now targets call #2, with a comment explaining why). Same combined patch also derives `deriveIssuePRLinks` (item 9): its dedup needed a `linkKey`/`parseURLRepoNumber` normalizer the plan's own sketch omitted - a full SCM URL (`.../o/n/issues/1`) and a `WorkItemRef`-derived `"o/n#1"` ref are the same artifact but different strings, so naive string-equality dedup (as literally drafted in the plan) fails `TestDeriveIssuePRLinks_Dedupes`. Project/Repository per-kind open-issue/incident counts (item 7) are computed unconditionally near the top of their reconciles too, for the same reason. Subtask rollup (item 8): `markSubtaskDone` now takes the parent `*Task` (was namespace+name) so it can upsert the completed entry via a second `patchTaskStatus` call after the Subtask status write; the plan-turn (turn 0, no backing Subtask) synthetic order-0 "Planning" entry is captured in `turncallback.go`'s `recordResult` else-branch. `UpsertSubtaskRollup` exported from `internal/controller` (not moved to `api/v1alpha1`) since `internal/restapi` already imports `internal/controller` - no new cross-package dependency. Item 10 (autoclean) needed zero production code: `DefaultTaskRetention=168h` and the delivered->terminal (`DeployState=Done`) path were already correct, and the incident-retention exception was already wired in reaper.go from Phase 2 - added confirmation tests only. **Skipped per explicit task scope** (operator worktree only): the plan's Phase 6 Task 3 Step 5 `tatara-agent-skills` SKILL.md re-entry note - not done, would need a follow-up pass in that repo's own worktree. Full `make generate manifests test lint build` green; chart-lint CRD count still 5; all new printcolumns confirmed present in the regenerated CRD YAML.

2026-07-12 (drop operator-internal termination issue comments) **Removed the 4 termination-comment call sites** (`commentTerminalDiagnostics` at PodLost/AgentUnreachable/TurnTimeout, `commentBootCrashDiagnostics` at BootCrashLoop) and deleted the now-fully-dead `commentTerminalDiagnostics`/`commentBootCrashDiagnostics`/`postTerminalComment` functions - user-requested noise reduction (these termination reasons are operator-internal operational failures, not conversational content, and were spamming the linked issue/PR with "wrapper agent unreachable for over 5m0s"-style comments). `terminate()`, its structured log (`action":"task_terminate"`), and the `operator_task_terminal_total` / per-reason metrics (`operator_agent_unreachable_termination_total`, `operator_agent_boot_crash_total`) are UNCHANGED - those remain the observability surface, backed by a sibling PR adding the missing PodLost Grafana alert. Kept `annBootCrashDiagnostics`/`annAgentUnreachableSince` annotations and the BootCrashLoop condition-message diag fold-in (`captureBootCrashDiagnostics`) - those are the kubectl-inspect fallback, unrelated to the SCM comment. Updated `terminal_diag_test.go` (renamed/repurposed to `TestHandleAgentUnreachableDoesNotComment`, asserting Failed/AgentUnreachable + the termination metric fire but the fake SCM writer sees zero comments) and `TestHandleBootCrashExhaustedSurfacesDiagnostics` (dropped its 1-comment assertion, kept the condition-message diag assertions, added an empty-comments assertion) and removed `comment_gate_sites_test.go`'s two `postTerminalComment` bot-last-word-gate tests (tested a now-deleted function; the gate itself is still covered by the 8 remaining conversational `gatedComment` call sites' own tests).

2026-07-12 (Request C review-fix pass, 7 findings) A rigorous review of the full-scope-no-followups branch found 7 defects, all fixed with a failing-then-passing regression test each. **F1/F4 (critical/important, ordering):** the `ChangeSummary.RemainingScope` hard-fail ran AFTER `writeBackOpenChange` in `finishImplement` (issueLifecycle bridge), so an incomplete change got its PR opened, semver-labeled, and auto-merge enabled before the Task terminated Failed - CI green would then auto-merge the gap. Also entirely absent on the generic `kind=implement` path (`doWriteBack`'s default case, the redesign's primary route via `tatara-implementation`). Fixed with one shared `checkRemainingScopeHardFail` helper (writeback.go) called BEFORE `writeBackOpenChange` from both `finishImplement` and `doWriteBack`, so the two paths cannot drift again. **F2 (critical, self-match):** `TaskMatchesItem` matches on ANY `Status.WorkItems` ledger entry regardless of role, but `seedLedgerFromSpec` seeds a systemic lead's OWN ledger with a `role:closes` entry for every sibling it references - so `issueHasRecordedApproval`/`issueIsImplementationLocked` (systemic_approval.go) treated the lead's own approval/lock as belonging to every sibling, making the sibling-approval gate vacuous and the fan-out log/metric dead code. Added `TaskMatchesItemAsSource` (api/v1alpha1/workitem_types.go: matches only Spec.Source or a `role:source` ledger entry, never `role:closes`) and use it in both functions. **F3 (important, staleness):** `issueIsImplementationLocked` scanned ALL Tasks (any-match), so a stale terminal locked Task from an earlier triage cycle could outlive a newer, unlocked re-triage successor (Task GC retention is 168h). Verified re-triage always spawns a NEW Task CR (adoptLifecycleTaskAt/findConvTaskToReactivate only reactivate from Conversation/Stopped, never a Done+locked Task), so "newest Task wins" (new `newestTaskForSource` helper, systemic_approval.go) is sufficient - no separate "clear on re-entry" path was needed or added. Reused the same helper in `umbrella.go`'s `systemicGroupSiblingsSummary.find` (previously its own any-match/self-match-prone inline scan) so the clarify-bundle sibling view and the approval fan-out can never disagree. **F5 (important, read amplification):** `syncAllSiblingLinksIfNeeded` ran on every reconcile of every multi-issue Task with no gate, one `GetIssue` per sibling per reconcile forever. Added `Status.LinksSyncedURLs` (new CRD field) - the sync now skips when the sibling URL set is unchanged since the last sync, and the `reader.GetIssue` call is now `r.recordSCM`-instrumented. **F6 (minor):** `allIssueSiblingURLs` hardcoded `"github"` as the provider default for both untagged WorkItemRefs and all CrossRepo refs; now threads the owning Project's `Spec.Scm.Provider` through (falls back to "github" only when that too is empty). **F7 (minor):** the clarify turn-0 bundle rendered any Found+unlocked sibling as "still open (&lt;Phase&gt;)" even when Phase was a terminal DeployState like Done/Parked - only Conversation/Triage are genuinely "open" now; anything else renders "not implementation-locked (state: X)". Full `make generate manifests` (new `LinksSyncedURLs` CRD field regenerated), `go test ./... -race -count=1`, `golangci-lint run` (0 issues), and `pre-commit run --all-files` all green.

2026-07-12 (de-scope pass: ship a/b/c, DEFER d) The product owner shipped the full-scope-or-decline work in three parts and **deferred item Request C/d (implementation-lock + systemic approval fan-out) entirely**. Removed: `Task.Status.ImplementationLocked`/`ImplementationLockedAt` and `IssueOutcome.Locked` (CRD + REST wire), `setImplementationLocked`/`clearImplementationLock`, the `projectscan` stale-lock clear branch, `issueIsImplementationLocked`, the `filterSystemicGroupByApproval` fan-out branch (and its `leadApproved` param / `fannedOut` return), the `systemic_approval_fanout` log line, and the `tatara_systemic_approval_fanout_total` + `tatara_implementation_locked_total` counters. `systemic_approval.go` is back to its ORIGINAL conservative rule: **an unapproved sibling is ALWAYS stripped from a close directive (`Closes #N` -> `refs #N`), unconditionally** - no lock exception, no fan-out exception. WHY deferred: three rounds of adversarial review kept finding load-bearing holes in the design rather than in its implementation. The lock-clear path was effectively unreachable (a collapsed systemic sibling never gets a superseding Task, so the ONLY place a stale lock could ever be noticed was a single branch in `issueScanPickOne` that a candidate reaches only after passing the human-activity/dedup gates - a lock could therefore outlive the conversation that justified it), and the close-directive net that the fan-out relies on to be safe does not cover cross-repo refs at all (below). A feature whose safety net has a known hole and whose invalidation path is unreachable is not shippable; the conservative always-strip rule has neither problem. KEPT from the hardening rounds: the fail-CLOSED List-error handling in `unapprovedSystemicSiblings`/`withApprovedSystemicGroup`, the widened `closeDirectiveRE`, the source-identity + newest-wins task resolver (`newestTaskForSource`, still used by `issueHasRecordedApproval` and the clarify bundle), and the turn-0 bundle sibling surfacing (C/c) - now rendering phase only, no locked state.

2026-07-12 (KNOWN GAP, deferred with C/d) **`closeDirectiveRE` does not cover cross-repo close directives.** It matches `close|fix|resolve|implement` (+ inflections, optional colon, optional `issue`/`issues` word, comma/`and` lists) followed by BARE `#N` refs only. An agent-authored `Closes owner/repo#3` or `Closes https://github.com/owner/repo/issues/3` is NOT matched and therefore NOT neutralized, so it survives into the PR body verbatim. Today that is harmless-by-construction: systemic `CrossRepo` members are reference-only and the operator itself never emits a cross-repo close, so the only way one appears is an agent writing it by hand. It stays uncovered deliberately - widening the regex is only worth doing together with the fan-out feature it would protect, and both are deferred.

2026-07-12 (3 defects fixed, TDD each) **D1 (critical): auto-merge armed at PR-open time was never disarmed.** The lifecycle re-enters Implement with the PR still open on four paths (mrci-failure, merge-conflict, mainci-failure, deploy-failure), so a turn-2 `change_summary{remainingScope}` hard-failed the Task while the forge happily merged the incomplete PR as soon as CI went green (push-CD then tagged and released it). `checkRemainingScopeHardFail` now calls `disarmOpenChanges` first: disable native auto-merge, strip the `semver:<level>` label, close the PR - for EVERY PR on the `openedPR` ledger, not just `Status.PrURL` (a cross-repo umbrella arms one per repo). Added `SCMWriter.DisableAutoMerge` (GitHub `disablePullRequestAutoMerge`, GitLab `cancel_merge_when_pipeline_succeeds`). **D2: links-sync livelock.** `isPermanentTargetGone` only classifies 404/410 as terminal, so any other permanent failure (403 conversation-locked, no `issues:write`, 422 body over the 65536-char limit) kept the sweep unclean forever, `LinksSyncedURLs` unstamped, and one `GetIssue` per sibling running on EVERY reconcile - the read amplification the F5 gate exists to bound. Bounded with `Status.LinksSyncFailures` + `linksSyncFailureCap`, mirroring `WritebackSkip4xxAttempts`/`writebackSkip4xxCap`: at the cap the sweep gives up, stamps the URL set anyway (reads stop), and resets the counter so a CHANGED sibling set gets a fresh budget. **D3: the change_summary kind gate was too wide.** It rejected only project-scoped kinds, so `kind=review` could post one - and since the hard-fail is hoisted above `doWriteBack`'s kind switch, a review agent misfiring `remainingScope` (describing what the PR UNDER REVIEW still lacks) hard-failed its own review Task before the verdict posted, leaving the PR unreviewed. New `IsChangeOpeningKind` (= not project-scoped, not `review`; exactly the kinds reaching `writeBackOpenChange`) now gates both the REST endpoint and `checkRemainingScopeHardFail`.

2026-07-13 (Task 18 test coverage, task-centric redesign) `pending_events.go` (`AppendTaskEvent`/`ClearDeliveredEvents`/`deliverPendingEvent`/`reverifyParked`) had zero tests. Audited against the plan + contract Section I: the implementation already satisfied every named property (bot filter before enqueue, Go-side cap-20-before-write, set-difference clear, sync-then-grammar C3-3 wiring) - no logic fix was needed, only tests. One production fix WAS required for testability: `webhook.Config` had no way to inject a fake `scm.SCMReader` for the identity-unverified re-verify path (`scmReader` called `scm.ReaderByProvider` directly, which hits a real forge over the network) - added `Config.ReaderFor func(provider, token string) (scm.SCMReader, error)`, defaulting to `scm.ReaderByProvider` in `NewServer`, mirroring the existing `ReaderFor` idiom in `internal/controller/issue_controller.go`. The concurrent "webhook arrives between render and clear" property needed a REAL race, not a fake-client simulation (fake client has no genuine concurrency and doesn't enforce CRD `MaxItems`): added `internal/webhook/pending_events_envtest_test.go` with its own envtest `TestMain` (the package's first) and a `blockingStatusClient` wrapper that intercepts a Task's first `Status().Update` call to hold `ClearDeliveredEvents` between its Get and its write while a concurrent `AppendTaskEvent` lands on the real API server - forcing a genuine `RetryOnConflict` retry. 10 new tests across 3 files (`pending_events_test.go` white-box, `pending_events_http_test.go` + `pending_events_envtest_test.go` black-box), all race-clean.

2026-07-13 (G2/G3: the StageDriver had no callers, and nothing stamped deployedAt) Two gaps the plan has no step for, both closed here. **G2 - `StageDriver` was dead code.** `ReconcileMerging`/`CloseIssuesOnDelivery`/`DrainPendingReview`/`DrainPendingComments`/`advanceAfterReview` (Task 13's whole output) had ZERO production callers: `wire.go` never built a driver and the mirror reconcilers never drained, so `reviewing` never advanced and no review was ever posted. Wired: one shared `StageDriver` in `cmd/manager/wire.go` (client + SCMFor + ReaderFor + spillerFor + clock, the same deps the mirror reconcilers get), drained from `MergeRequestReconciler.Reconcile` (pendingComments then pendingReview) and `IssueReconciler.Reconcile` (pendingComments), and a NEW `StageReconciler` (`internal/controller/stage_controller.go`, controller name `taskstage`) that owns the two pod-less operator stages: `merging -> ReconcileMerging`, `deploying -> ReconcileDeploying`. It is a SEPARATE controller from `TaskReconciler` on purpose (the merge and the delivery are irreversible writes to a human's repo, and they run through the single merge egress and nothing else); it watches MergeRequests mapped to the controller-owning Task, because both signals that move a Task off `reviewing`/`deploying` land on the MR first. **G3 - `deployedAt` had a reader and no writer.** `merge.go:464` gates `deploying -> delivered` on `state==merged && deployedAt != nil`; the field had exactly one reference in the repo and it was that read, so every Task wedged at `deploying` until the 2h budget parked it. The CONTRACT never names the writer either - this was a contract gap, and it is closed by `StageDriver.ReconcileDeploying` (`internal/controller/deploy_stage.go`): **the MergeRequest CR IS the deploy ledger** (per-artifact, durable in etcd, Task-owned, and already what the delivery gate reads), so the per-Project `deploy_ledger.go` ConfigMap CAS is NOT used by the new path (kept, unused, for the dying push-CD sweep). It re-points the SURVIVING machinery (the `scm.DeployWatcher` poll, `helmfilePinState`, `deployPinFiles`, `releaseArtifact`'s pin attribution rules) off Phase/WorkItems and onto the MR: merged MR -> component semver tag -> pin propagates -> tatara-helmfile `apply.yaml` green carrying it -> stamp `deployedAt` + `deployedVersion`, then C.4 delivery IN ORDER (close every owned Issue, THEN `deliveredAt`). Three deliberate design calls: (a) the pin match is `pinAtOrPastArtifactVersion` (SEMVER >=, not the old exact-token `pinCarriesArtifactVersion`) because pins only move forward - exact equality wedges any Task whose apply was superseded by the next release; (b) an apply run that STARTED BEFORE the MR merged can never be credited with it (`applyPostdatesMerge`), which is what makes (a) safe; (c) TWO FAIL-OPEN rules, because a wedge is worse than an early delivery on a change that is already merged - no observable cascade (non-GitHub reader, or the Project enrols no tatara-helmfile) and no helmfile pin for the repo AT ALL (tatara-documentation, tatara-observability) both mean MERGE IS DELIVERY. **G4 stays dead:** nothing here calls `superviseApprovedPRs`/`superviseMergedPRs`/the umbrella deploy path; `mergePRSquash` remains the single `writer.Merge` egress and `TestSingleMergeEgress` (stage_controller_test.go) now asserts that on the package AST, not in review. `helmfilePinState` was de-methodised off `TaskReconciler` so it survives the reap of that machine.

2026-07-13 (the MergeRequest orphan / re-mint gap: a human's still-open PR silently lost its mirror) A production bug the contract and the plan both missed, and it is the MIRROR half of the rule V6-2 only ever enforced on the FORGE half. Fix C3-2 makes every `review`-kind Task non-bot-authored BY CONSTRUCTION, so a review Task controller-owns a CONTRIBUTOR'S `MergeRequest`; its only terminal is `parked(awaiting-human)` (V7-1: a human's PR is fixed and merged by the human) and B.6 reaps a non-backlog park at 7d. B.6 step 4 (`closeOwnMRs`) correctly left the human's PR completely alone - clause (a) `author == botLogin` fails, so no close, no branch delete, zero forge writes. But step 3 (`releaseOwnership`) passed `dropWhenOrphaned=false` for **every** MR, justified by "a bot MR we are about to close must never be re-adopted". **That is right for a BOT MR and wrong for a HUMAN's:** keeping the ownerRef makes the CR CASCADE with the Task, so after the 7d reap the contributor's PR sat open on the forge with NO mirror and their next comment landed on nothing. Fixed by making `dropWhenOrphaned` for an MR true exactly when step 4 will NOT close it (`!ourMR`) AND it is still `open` - the same "an OPEN artifact must be re-mintable RIGHT NOW" rule fix H13 already gave the Issue path one loop above. Clauses (a)+(b) are now ONE predicate (`ourMR`) shared by steps 3 and 4, because a disagreement between them IS this bug. Three deliberate design calls: **(a) the re-mint disposition is `parked(awaiting-human)`, not `triaging`** (`MintReviewStage`). Re-minting ACTIVE would spawn a review pod that re-reviews a PR nobody touched and RE-POSTS the same review - every 7 days, forever. The predicate is `mr.status.status`, which is operator-owned and written ONLY once a review has LANDED on the forge (C.5.3 `clearPendingReview`); `""`/`"new"` (never reviewed, or the head moved) still mints ACTIVE, because that review is genuinely owed. The parked re-mint re-anchors the mirror at zero agent cost and hands the PR back to F.6: the next genuine human comment un-parks it to `reviewing`. **(b) `humanReviewRounds` is CARRIED across the reap** on a new `tatara.dev/human-review-rounds` annotation on the MergeRequest CR - the only thing that survives. The V7-9 cap (5) lives on the Task and the reap deletes the Task, so without the carry a PR parked AT the cap is worth five MORE review pods every seven days: the same cost amplifier, one week slower. **(c) An already-CLOSED not-ours MR still cascades** - nothing left to mirror, and orphaning it would leak a zero-owner CR nothing collects and nothing re-adopts (the sweep only lists OPEN PRs). Found and fixed alongside: **`ClassifyPR` had no orphan clause at all**, the MR analogue of `IsOrphanIssue`'s clause (b). A human's PR never has a `task/<name>` head branch, so `taskForBranch` always returned nil for it and nothing else could tell "a PR we are already reviewing" from "a PR we have never seen" - a PR under ACTIVE review therefore re-classified as `PRReview` on EVERY hourly pass, minting a second review Task whose `ownMergeRequest` then failed on the existing controller owner, leaving a stage-less junk Task behind AND erroring the whole sweep pass (which suppresses the heartbeat gauge the sweep-stalled alert reads). `ClassifyPR` now takes the MR CR: owned -> IGNORE, ownerless -> ADOPT (`SyncMergeRequest` is already ensure-then-upsert, so the mirrored review thread is preserved and nothing AlreadyExists). Known, accepted residue: an orphaned BOT PR on a dead task's branch now also survives as an ownerless mirror, which `ClassifyPR` clause 2 deliberately never re-adopts - a slow, harmless leak of zero-owner CRs, preferred over cascading away the mirror of a PR that is still open.

2026-07-13 (Task 20 steps 2+3: the stage machine DRIVES, and the D1 metric is finally TOTAL) `TaskReconciler.Reconcile` is now stage-driven end to end (mint -> terminal check -> F.4 clocks -> F.4 caps -> pod-less stage / pod stage) and no longer reads `Status.Phase` at all. Three decisions worth recording. **(a) ONE transition choke point, and the metric lives INSIDE it.** `internal/controller/transition.go` `EnterStage` is the single door: it pre-validates with `stage.LegalFor` (so an illegal edge costs one `operator_illegal_stage_transition_total{from,to}` - a metric that until now was NAMED and never emitted, exactly the defect contract K.1 calls out twice - and ZERO API calls), stamps the clocks via `stage.Enter`, deletes the pod of the stage being LEFT, logs `action=stage_transition`, and fires `operator_task_terminal_total{kind,stage,stageReason}` on every terminal entry. **The D1 hole was much wider than SHARED-CONTEXT said**: not just `StageDriver`, but `internal/restapi/outcome.go`'s ELEVEN `stage.Enter` sites (parked(implement-declined|awaiting-human|identity-unverified), rejected(declined|false-positive), delivered - i.e. most terminal outcomes the platform ever produces), `docbatch.go:217` delivered(doc-timeout), and both `podwatch.go` terminals. All are now routed through the choke point, except `restapi`'s, which fires the same emit from its own single `outcomeCtx.commit` (it cannot use `EnterStage` because it bundles the idempotency condition into the same write). **The emit CANNOT go inside `stage.Enter`**: `objbudget.FitTask` runs its mutate closure at least twice (once to size the write, once per conflict retry), so a counter fired there is inflated 2-3x. It fires once, AFTER the write lands. **(b) The pod is per-TASK, not per-stage** (`agent.PodName`), so a Task advancing implementing -> reviewing would have found its implement pod still Running under the review pod's name and REUSED it - running the previous stage's agent kind, model and skills. Pods now carry a `tatara.dev/pod-stage` annotation and a pod from a stage the Task has left is deleted before the next one is created; `EnterStage` also tears the pod down on any transition out of a pod stage. **(c) CLOCK 2 stays with `PodWatchReconciler`, deliberately.** It is the single writer of `stats.podRecreations`; `TaskReconciler` treats a `Respawn` edge as "not mine" and only requeues. But podwatch's Pod predicate DROPS delete events, so a pod that is DELETED while never Ready produces no event and would wedge forever - `reconcilePodStage` owns that one case (gone pod + `podStartedAt != nil`) and respawns it, with `parked(no-outcome)` when the pod had become Ready and `failed(pod-recreation-exhausted)` when it never did. Also: `triageTarget` has NO `implement` row on purpose - F.3 has no `triaging -> implementing` edge, and code execution is reachable ONLY through clarifying -> approved -> implementing, i.e. only through the C.6 gate.

2026-07-13 (Task 20 plan errata, traced to the code) **`UpsertSubtaskRollup` cannot be deleted as Task 20 step 2 says**: it has two live callers outside the dying machine (`internal/restapi/handlers.go:353` createSubtask, `internal/controller/turncallback.go:520`). Kept; it dies with the Subtask CRD in Task 21. **`Reconcile` and the old machine cannot coexist, and neither can their tests**: 120 tests across 27 files drove the phase-driven `Reconcile` (spawn -> Planning -> subtask turns -> terminate) and test behaviour this task deletes. They are retired here with the entry point they exercised; the writeback/lifecycle CODE they covered survives one more commit and is deleted by Task 21. `preSpawnIncidentDuplicate`, `incidentDedupRefireComment` (task_controller.go) and `reviewTargetClosed` (writeback.go) became callerless the moment `Reconcile` stopped calling them and were deleted to keep lint green.

2026-07-13 (Task 20 steps 4+5: the lifecycle machine is DELETED, and what the reap actually exposed) ~12,800 lines of production code gone: 19 whole files (`lifecycle*.go`, `turnloop.go`, `umbrella.go`, `backstop.go`, `systemic_approval.go`, `clarify.go`, `links.go`, `writeback_{review,proposal,issue}.go`, `approval.go`, `thread.go`, plus `handoff.go`, `scanmarks.go` and `bootcrash.go`, which the deletion orphaned) and deep prunes of six survivors (`projectscan.go` -2064, `deploy_supervision.go` -1493, `writeback.go` -1428, `task_controller.go` -541, `labels.go` -442, `comment_gate.go` -190). 126 test files retired with the behaviour they exercised. The reap was driven by `golangci-lint run --tests=false -E unused` as the dead-code oracle, NOT by grep: everything below was found that way, and none of it was in the plan. **`closeIssueOnDeploy` is NOT live** (the brief said keep it): its only callers were `reconcileDeploying`/`resolveDeployedTask`/`resolveDeployedUmbrella`, all dead. The live delivery-close is `StageDriver.CloseIssuesOnDelivery` (merge.go:476 <- deploy_stage.go:99). Deleted. **The whole agent spawn/drive-turns block in `task_controller.go` was already unreachable** before this task - `Reconcile` delegates to `reconcileStage`, so `driveAgentRun`, `ensurePodAndService`, `driveTurns`, `recordTurn`, `turnCap`, `isTurnTimedOut` and all of `bootcrash.go` had zero callers. `bootcrash.go` is properly superseded (`podwatch.go:200 handleNotReady` says so itself: CLOCK 2 budget-exit replaces the crash-loop respawn, `podGone`+`respawnLostPod` replace the lost-pod path); its only real loss is the boot-crash DIAGNOSTICS capture (failing container, exit code, log tail), which the new path does not carry. **`cdScan` and the whole Phase/DeployState CD supervision are deleted too.** They still FIRED from `runScans` but were dead in practice: every predicate reads `Status.DeployState` / `TaskDeploying()`, which the stage machine never writes, so the loop was a no-op and `tatara_cd_cascade_{failed,stalled}` published a constant 0. Keeping them would have meant resurrecting a whole umbrella/WorkItems test harness for code that can never fire. The new deploy-stall path is F.4's CLOCK -> `parked(deploy-timeout)`, surfaced by `operator_task_terminal_total`. The two CD gauges are now never set - drop them from the dashboards. `parkStalledDeploy` died with it, and with it the ONLY caller of the reconciler-side forge-write comment gate (`gatedComment`/`gatedCommentCore`/`decideCommentGate`), which is also deleted; the PERMISSION-layer gate (`PermitComment`, `CommentSilenceBreakers`, `DuplicateRecentBotComment`) is untouched and is what `restapi/handlers_v2.go:1153` uses. Note the behaviour that went with it: the operator no longer suppresses a comment on a CLOSED issue/PR, because the operator no longer posts comments through that path.

2026-07-13 (two REGRESSIONS the reap exposed, one fixed here, one still open) **FIXED: `operator_task_terminal_tokens_total` had lost its only emitter.** `AddTerminalTokens` was called from the old machine's `setDeployState`; `obs/task_metrics.go` still defines the counter and NOTHING fired it, so the platform's only per-Task token-spend accounting was silently dead. Re-wired into `EnterStage` (`transition.go`), the same choke point D1 uses, so it now covers EVERY terminal entry (TaskReconciler's, StageDriver's, the doc batch's) - which the old site never did. The `outcome` label is now the terminal STAGE (delivered/failed/rejected/...), matching D1's relabel; the old delivered/churned/abandoned trichotomy described lifecycle states that no longer exist, so **any dashboard selecting on those three label values must be re-pointed.** **STILL OPEN (G6): nothing applies the `semver:<level>` PR label any more.** The only appliers were `semverLabel`/`ensureSemverLabelColor`/`addSemverLabelToPR`, reached from `applySemverAutoMerge` <- `writeBackOpenChange` - the PR-open path the new machine REPLACED with `restapi/handlers_v2.go:1359`, which opens the change and never labels it. `MergeRequest.Status.Significance` carries the level and is never written to the forge. Per the platform contract the CI cuts the semver tag FROM THAT LABEL, so push-CD currently has no tag source: no tag -> no publish -> no pin -> `deploying` never resolves. The label names and colours survive in `labels.go` (`semverLabelMajor/Minor/Patch`, `managedLabelColors`); the three deleted appliers are recoverable from `git show HEAD:internal/controller/labels.go` (lines 96-155). Whoever owns the new PR-open path must stamp the label there.

2026-07-13 (THE FRONT DOOR: `tatara.dev/webhook-originated`, and why the `tatara-parked` label now beats it) Task 21 deleted the webhook's Task-minting surface (correctly - the B.4 sweep is the sole intake), but it ORPHANED the `webhookOriginated` signal: `MintStage`'s only caller passed a hardcoded `false`, and `humanHasLastWord` is false on an EMPTY thread, so **a freshly-opened human issue minted `parked(backlog-sweep)` - zero pods - and sat there until the human commented a SECOND time on their own issue.** The platform's primary entry point was dead. **The signal is LIVENESS, and it cannot be recovered from thread shape**: a brand-new human issue and a three-year-old backlog issue are BOTH open, human-authored and zero-comment, so reading "zero comments" as "a human has the last word" would mint the entire cutover backlog ACTIVE - decision B2's 150-issue, 17-to-100-pod-hour re-triage storm. Liveness only comes from the forge saying something JUST HAPPENED. **Mechanism:** a non-bot, allowlisted `issues.opened`/`issues.reopened` delivery stamps `tatara.dev/webhook-originated` (RFC3339, audit-only; presence is what matters) on the mirror Issue CR via `controller.MarkWebhookOriginated`, CREATING the CR ownerless if absent (B.2 permits it, B.1 never GCs a zero-owner object, and the sweep's mint is adopt-or-create, so it adopts rather than collides). It never marks an issue a Task already OWNS - that marker could not be consumed by a mint and would re-activate the issue after a later park+reap. **The webhook still mints NOTHING.** The sweep reads the marker, passes it to `MintStage`, and CLEARS it on the mint that read it (whatever stage that mint chose); a marker whose mint the creation budget DEFERRED is deliberately kept, or the budget would silently demote a live human issue into the backlog. **The `MintStage` ordering FLIPPED, and that is the whole design decision:** `tatara-parked` is now checked BEFORE the marker. As an in-process bool the signal could not disagree with a label (the webhook was minting from the delivery it was handling right then); as a DURABLE annotation it can outlive its delivery and meet a label stamped afterwards - by the reaper on a park, or by a human parking the issue by hand. If the marker won, a human parking a just-opened issue would be overruled, and any uncleared marker would re-open the M25 loop from the other side (mint ACTIVE -> pod re-triages -> parks -> reaper stamps `tatara-parked` -> sweep reads the marker again -> ACTIVE, forever). So fix M25 holds unconditionally and the marker only decides ACTIVE-vs-backlog for an issue NOBODY has parked. **Accepted residue:** an issue that is opened and then closed before the next sweep leaves an ownerless Issue CR that nothing collects (same class as the orphaned-bot-PR mirror already on the ROADMAP; B.1 never GCs zero-owner objects by design). Bounded and benign.

2026-07-13 (Task 20 step 5 plan errata) Step 5's five dedup mechanisms: items 1 (`createScanTask`'s kind-scoped key), 2 (`scanmarks.go`) and 5 (the backstop's key recomputation) are done - all three died with their files. Item 4 (`TaskMatchesItem`) was already known to collide with Task 21. **Item 3 (`DedupNumber`) collides the SAME way and is deferred with it**: there is no `Task.Status.DedupNumber` - the field is `Task.Spec.Source.DedupNumber` (`task_types.go:175`), and its only readers are `TaskMatchesItem`/`TaskMatchesItemAsSource` (`workitem_types.go:48,91`), i.e. exactly the functions item 4 defers to Task 21, plus `webhook/server.go:525`. Removing the field now breaks Task 21's own surface. Also: **Task 20's verification greps cannot pass at step 5 and were never going to.** `grep issueLifecycle` cannot be zero while the old REST surface (`restapi/handlers.go`), the webhook's issue-intake bridge, `obs/lifecycle_metrics.go`, `agent/pod.go`'s kind map and the `api/v1alpha1` CEL rules still exist - all of them Task 21's. `grep "Status.Phase"` is naive besides: it matches `pod.Status.Phase` (podwatch) and `repo.Status.Phase` (the Repository CR), which are unrelated and live. Within `internal/controller`, every surviving `issueLifecycle` hit is now a kind-string in a list (turn-cap, reaper batching, the project gauge) or a comment, and the only Task `Status.Phase` writer left is `turncallback.go` - all of it Task 21's to remove with the field.

2026-07-13 (ACCEPTED RISK - USER DECISION D-A, contract C.9 - NOT A DEFECT, DO NOT RE-RAISE) **The merge gate is OPERATOR LOGIC, not a forge-enforced control.** The platform runs on ONE bot identity, so the operator cannot post `event=APPROVE` on a PR that same token opened - GitHub 422s a self-approve - which means **branch protection can never require an approving review**: enabling it would deadlock EVERY merge the platform makes. The review is therefore posted as `event=COMMENT` (there is no `Event` field on `PendingReview` at all; the constant is `reviewEventComment`) and the "approved" verdict lives only in operator state. Consequence, stated plainly: **any pod holding `GIT_TOKEN` can bypass the entire review gate by curling the forge's merge endpoint.** The chosen control is DETECTION, not prevention: `operator_unexpected_merge_total{repo}` counts a MergeRequest observed merged with no `mergeCursor` advance, and the chart's `TataraUnexpectedMerge` alert is CRITICAL severity. A second bot identity (a dedicated reviewer app) is the only real fix and is out of scope. Do not "fix" this by arming branch protection.

2026-07-13 (Task 22, cutover trap) **The `Subtask` CRD SURVIVES `helm upgrade`.** `templates/crds.yaml` injects `helm.sh/resource-policy: keep` into every CRD it renders, which is what stops a chart rollback or a failed upgrade from cascade-deleting every Task in the cluster - but it also means a CRD *removed* from `crd-bases/` is simply left behind, not deleted. Chart 1.0.0 renders exactly SIX CRDs (issues, mergerequests, projects, queuedevents, repositories, tasks) and `subtasks.tatara.dev` is not among them, so **the cutover MUST run `kubectl delete crd subtasks.tatara.dev` as an explicit step** (that also reaps any orphaned Subtask CRs). `make chart-lint` asserts the count is 6; if it ever says 7 again, a CRD came back. Do not "fix" the assertion back to 7.

2026-07-13 (Task 22, why the A.7 byte guard is HALF the etcd ceiling) The guard refuses a write at ~half the 1.5 MiB etcd object limit, not at 90% of it, because **the size WE compute is not the size etcd stores.** `metadata.managedFields` grows with every server-side-apply field-manager that ever touched the object (the operator, each controller, kubectl, any admission webhook), it is counted against the same limit, and we do not control it or even see it in the body we marshal. Half the ceiling is the headroom for the part of the object we cannot measure. A guard tuned to 90% would pass locally and 413 in the cluster, and the write it drops is a comment, a note or an event - silent data loss.

2026-07-13 (Task 22, why `QueuedEvent.spec.priority` is a `*int` and not an `int`) A `+kubebuilder:default` only fires when the field is **ABSENT from the request body**. A non-pointer `int` with `omitempty` serializes 0 as absent (so the default fires and a deliberate priority 0 silently becomes the default), and without `omitempty` it serializes 0 as present (so the default NEVER fires for a client that omits it, because client-go sends the zero value). A `*int` is the only shape where "the client did not set it" and "the client set it to 0" are distinguishable on the wire, which is what the defaulting webhook needs. Same reasoning applies to every scalar whose zero value is a legal, meaningful setting.

2026-07-13 (Task 22, THE STALE-COMMENT TRAP - the comment was FALSE, do not trust it again) `task_types.go:327-330` carried a comment asserting that no code path creates the retired Task kinds (`issueLifecycle` in particular) and that the enum members were vestigial. **It was false and it was live.** `issueLifecycle` Tasks were being created every hour: `createScanTask` takes the kind as an ARGUMENT, so a grep for the literal string `"issueLifecycle"` at the creation sites finds NOTHING while five producers (`projectscan.go:1791`, `:1315`, `:2960`, `backstop.go:404`, `:456`) happily mint them. The trap generalizes: **in this codebase a grep for a kind/stage/reason literal does not prove a code path is dead - the value is routinely threaded as a parameter.** The reap was driven by `golangci-lint run --tests=false -E unused` as the dead-code oracle and by call-graph reads, never by grep, and that is why it was correct. Every one of those five producers is now unreachable (they lived inside `issueScan`/`recoverOrphans`/`backstopSweep`, all dropped from `runScans` and then deleted).

2026-07-13 (Task 22, the SIX unplanned gaps this run found and closed - each was "the new machine does not actually work", and the plan had no step for any of them) **G1 - the dispatcher could not admit an EXISTING Task.** `queue_controller.go` only ever called `BuildTaskFromQueuedEvent`, which CREATES a Task from the payload and ignored `Payload.TaskRef`/`AgentKind`/`NewTask` entirely, so F.3's `approved -> implementing` edge ("a QueuedEvent for the implement pod is ADMITTED") was unimplementable. `admitTicket` now owns that edge. **G2 - `StageDriver` had ZERO production callers.** `ReconcileMerging`, `CloseIssuesOnDelivery`, `DrainPendingReview`, `DrainPendingComments`, `advanceAfterReview` were wired to nothing: `wire.go` never constructed one. Task 13's entire output was dead code, `reviewing` never advanced, and no review was ever posted. Now constructed in `wire.go` and driven by `stage_controller.go` (merging/deploying) + the Issue/MergeRequest reconcilers (the drains). **G3 - NOTHING stamped `MergeRequest.status.deployedAt`.** `deploying -> delivered` gates on it and there was exactly one reader and no writer anywhere; every Task would have wedged at `deploying` until its budget parked it. The CONTRACT never says who stamps it either - this is a contract gap, not a plan gap. `deploy_stage.go` is the writer; the MergeRequest CR is the deploy ledger now. **G4 - there were TWO merge drivers.** `superviseApprovedPRs` merged review-approved bot PRs via `mergePRSquash` alongside `StageDriver.ReconcileMerging`: a double-merge. The plan's "KEEP the discrete/umbrella branch" was WRONG - that branch IS the double-merge. It is deleted; `mergePRSquash` is the single `writer.Merge` egress and `TestSingleMergeEgress` walks the package AST to keep it single. **G5 - the F.4 clocks had no driver.** `stage.ArmedClock`, `Budget`, `OnElapse`, `BudgetExit` had zero production callers: every "the 2h budget parks it" / "merging reaches merge-timeout at 4h" claim in the contract was FICTION, and the merging/deploying loops requeued at 60s forever against a deadline that never fired. `task_stage.go` now arms the clock every pass. **G6 - NOTHING applied the `semver:<level>` PR label.** The only appliers hung off `writeBackOpenChange`, which the new machine replaced with a PR-open path that never labels. Per H.4 CI cuts the release tag FROM THAT LABEL: no label -> no tag -> no publish -> no pin -> `deploying` never resolves -> every Task wedges. `semver_label.go` projects it from `MergeRequest.status.significance`, applied at `submit_outcome` AND again inside `ReconcileMerging` immediately BEFORE `mergePRSquash` (CI cuts the tag from the label at the merge commit, so a merge that lands before the label is a release that never gets tagged).

2026-07-13 (Task 22, the webhook-originated ACTIVE-mint regression) Task 21 correctly deleted the webhook's Task-minting surface (the B.4 sweep is the sole intake) but ORPHANED the liveness signal with it: `MintStage`'s only caller passed a hardcoded `false` for `webhookOriginated`, and `humanHasLastWord` is false on an EMPTY thread, so **a freshly-opened human issue minted `parked(backlog-sweep)` - zero pods - and sat there until the human commented a second time on their own issue.** The platform's front door was dead. Liveness cannot be recovered from thread shape (a brand-new issue and a three-year-old backlog issue are both open, human-authored and zero-comment); it only comes from the forge saying something JUST happened. Fixed with a durable `tatara.dev/webhook-originated` annotation on the mirror Issue CR, stamped by the webhook and consumed+cleared by the sweep's mint. **The `MintStage` ordering FLIPPED and that is the design decision: `tatara-parked` is now checked BEFORE the marker.** As an in-process bool the signal could never disagree with a label; as a durable annotation it can outlive its delivery and meet a `tatara-parked` label stamped afterwards (by the reaper on a park, or by a human). If the marker won, a human parking a just-opened issue would be overruled, and an uncleared marker would re-open the M25 loop from the other side: mint ACTIVE -> pod re-triages -> parks -> reaper stamps `tatara-parked` -> sweep reads the marker again -> ACTIVE, forever.

2026-07-13 (Task 22, plan + contract ERRATA found while implementing - the code is right, the documents are wrong) **F.5's closed reason set omits `declined` and `false-positive`, but F.3's own transition table emits both** (`clarifying -> rejected` on `decision=close`; `investigating -> rejected` on `submit_outcome(false_positive)`). `stage.Enter` validates the reason against the set, so honouring F.5 literally would make "decline an implement" and "false-positive an incident" fail at runtime. **The set has 26 members, not 24**, and M.2's sweep ("every reason used in F.3 appears in F.5") is simply wrong. **K.1's emit table omits `operator_task_terminal_total` entirely** though 4 chart alerts and 29 tatara-observability rules select on it; the ALERTS win, and the emitted labels are `{kind, stage, stageReason}`. **Contract A.5 says delete `Task.Spec.Source`; it is KEPT** - the machine Task 20 landed depends on it and there is no replacement (`mintTaskForIssue`/`mintReviewTaskForPR`/`mintClarifyTask` seed it, `mintIssueCRs` reads it to mint the Issue CR at `triaging`, and `TaskBranch` derives the deterministic work branch from `Source.Number`+`Source.Title`). Only `TaskSource.DedupNumber` was deleted, which is the part the plan actually justified. **Contract A.4 makes `Task.Spec.Kind` required; it keeps `+optional`/`omitempty`** - required would 422 every Task minted without an explicit kind. **H.4 is SILENT on WHEN the semver label is applied**; it should say: projected from `MergeRequest.status.significance`, set at `submit_outcome` and re-asserted before the merge. **Task 20 Step 5's dedup item 4 collides with Task 21 Step 6** (both own `internal/controller/ledger.go`).

2026-07-13 (first live incident post-cutover, the mint-vs-own-pod-ticket admission deadlock) An incident Task deadlocked FOREVER at `investigating` with no pod, and every subsequent incident queued behind it. Root cause: `ticketSpent` treated ANY mint payload (`agentKind==""`) as never spent - "the TASK is the ticket, only terminality frees it" - which was correct for a Task that stays in one class's pool for its whole life but wrong once a Task's OWN later pod stage reuses the SAME class. An incident's CREATE QueuedEvent (class=alert, `agentKind=""`) is Admitted and mints the Task; `poolInflight(alert)` counted it as holding the single `AlertCapacity=1` slot (`queueTaskHoldsSlot`=true, `ticketSpent`=false forever). The Task's OWN `investigating` pod-ticket (class=alert, `agentKind=incident`, `payload.taskRef=<task>`) then needed an alert slot - the only one existed, held by the CREATE event of the SAME Task. Fixed: `ticketSpent` now spends a mint event once its Task leaves the create/triaging bootstrap (`stage != "" && != triaging`), matching the per-stage-ticket accounting every other stage already uses. **Test-coverage gap that let this ship**: `ensureTicket` (`task_stage.go` ~660) short-circuits `if r.Seq == nil { return true }`, and unit tests run with `Seq==nil`, so no test exercised real create-event-then-pod-ticket admission accounting against `AlertCapacity=1`. Closed with `TestTicketSpent_MintPayload` (table-driven over the stage buckets) and `TestAdmit_IncidentMintReleasesAlertSlot_RegressionForDeadlock` (envtest end-to-end: mint admits, Task driven to `investigating`, asserts `poolInflight(alert)` drops to 0 and the pod-ticket then admits) in `queue_controller_test.go`. Fixing this also surfaced that `TestPoolInflight_CountsAdmittedNonTerminal` was itself asserting the buggy "mint held forever regardless of stage" behavior on tasks parked at `reviewing`/`delivered`; updated to model a realistic per-stage ticket (`payload.agentKind` matching the stage) instead of a bare mint shape.

2026-07-13 (Task 22, the chart + the alerts that were about to go green forever) Chart 1.0.0 (MAJOR). SIX CRDs; RBAC gains `issues`, `mergerequests`, their `/status` subresources and **`tasks/finalizers` `update`** (a custom controller does NOT get `blockOwnerDeletion` for free - the API server checks `update` on the OWNER's finalizers subresource before admitting a dependent that asks for it, so without that rule every Issue/MR write is a 403). `ingress.className` un-baked from `nginx` to `""` (rule 14). **The reap left five alerts selecting metrics nothing emits any more**, which is the exact failure class this release train exists to kill - an alert on a dead metric is not a quiet alert, it is a GREEN one. `TataraTaskFailures` selected `operator_task_terminal_total{phase="Failed"}` and the label is now `{kind,stage,stageReason}` (repointed to `stage="failed"`). `TataraAgentBootCrashLoop` selected `operator_agent_boot_crash_total`, whose only emitter died with `bootcrash.go` (repointed to `failed(pod-recreation-exhausted)`, the terminal reason the stage machine actually writes). `TataraLifecycleGiveups` selected the deleted `tatara_lifecycle_giveup_total` (replaced by `TataraTasksParked` on `stage="parked"`, which is what "the loop gave up" means now). `TataraWritebackGaveUp4xx` selected the deleted `operator_writeback_outcome_total` (deleted: the agent opens its own PR through the REST API, so there is no operator-side writeback retry loop left to give up). **`TataraSCMWriteErrors` and `TataraSCMWriteFailureRatioHigh` were the worst of the five:** `operator_scm_writes_total` and `operator_scm_request_errors_by_status_total` still EXISTED but every one of their emitters died with `writeback.go`/`backstop.go`/`comment_gate.go`/`deploy_supervision.go`/`handlers.go`, so a platform whose whole job is writing to forges had NO forge-write-failure alerting at all. Emission restored at all 22 surviving forge call sites (20 writes + the merge gate's 2 live reads) through one nil-safe `RecordSCM` choke point (`labels.go`), with `get_pr_head`/`get_merge_state` added to `scmReadVerbs` so those two hot LIVE reads do not land in the write-failure ratio's denominator. One of the 20 - `DeleteBranch` in the reaper's `closeOwnMRs` - was never instrumented even by the OLD machine; `delete_branch` is a new verb. Six alerts added for the new machine's own failure modes: `TataraUnexpectedMerge` (CRITICAL, the D-A detection control), `TataraIllegalStageTransition`, `TataraSemverLabelMissing`, `TataraSweepStalled` (the sweep is the ONLY intake now - a sweep erroring every pass means the platform silently takes in NO work while looking perfectly healthy, and the heartbeat gauge is only stamped on a zero-error pass), `TataraSweepErrors`, `TataraObjectTooLarge`.

2026-07-16 (O1-O6, incident dedup + tracker-linking Fix A, #320/#328) Replaced `alertGroupHash(groupKey)` with `incidentDedupKey(alert, project, denylist)` = sha256(project + alertname + sortedKV(stable labels))[:16] (`internal/webhook/grafana.go`); pinned regression asserts #320/#328's real label sets collapse. `dedupExists` (`internal/queue/enqueue.go`) now also matches an OPEN incident Issue CR via a new `tatara.dev/alert-rule-key` label (`FindOpenIncidentIssue`), stamped at issue-creation time (`mintIssueCR` gained a `crLabels` param; `outcome.go incident()` stamps both the CR label and a `tatara-alert-rule=<key>` forge label from `Task.Spec.DedupKey`). Suppressed refires against an open tracker enqueue a coalesced comment via the EXISTING `Issue.status.PendingComments` drain (no new drain code) - `IssueStatus` gained `RefireCount`/`LastRefireCommentAt`, CRD regenerated. Added `webhook.Server.now func() time.Time` (defaults `time.Now`, overridable via `Config.Now`) since none existed - needed for a deterministic cooldown test. New config knobs `INCIDENT_DEDUP_VOLATILE_LABELS` (CSV, default {pod,reason,instance,container,endpoint,uid,id,replica,ordinal}) and `INCIDENT_REFIRE_COMMENT_COOLDOWN_MINUTES` (default 30), UPPER_SNAKE envFrom per rule 6. Metrics: `operator_incident_dedup_suppressed_total{reason}`, `operator_incident_refire_comment_total{result}`. O7-O9 (AddSubIssue SCM primitive, operator-side link execution, goal.go prompt rewrite) are NOT done - next subagent's scope, per plan docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-16-incident-dedup-and-linking-plan.md.

2026-07-16 (production incident: two bugs found live) **Superseded-stage pod reap.** `orphanReason` had no rule for "pod belongs to a stage the Task already left" - only terminal/gone/UID-stale/idle. An incident's investigating pod stayed Running after the Task advanced to clarifying, because the pod carried no agent-kind label to compare against. Fixed by stamping `tatara.dev/agent-kind` (= `stage.AgentKindFor(task.Status.Stage)`) on every wrapper Pod/Service at build time (`agent.LabelAgentKind`, `podLabels`), and adding a reaper rule between the terminal check and the idle backstop: both kinds non-empty and disagreeing = reaped (`"superseded: pod kind X, stage wants Y"`). Deliberately conservative on a pod-less current stage (`AgentKindFor==""`) - left to the idle backstop instead of an unconditional reap, to avoid a false positive on the between-stages blip. **Incident downstream stages starved on AlertCapacity=1.** `ensureTicket` classed EVERY stage of an incident Task as `QueueClassAlert` off `task.Spec.Kind`, so a `clarifying`/`implementing` ticket queued behind `AlertCapacity=1` alongside `investigating` itself. Fixed: class off the STAGE's `agentKind` parameter instead - only `investigating` (`AgentKindFor==incident`) is alert-class.

2026-07-17 (Task 9, remove the vestigial mrScan API surface) `runScans`/`activityScheduleAndLast`/`stampScan` had zero live "mrScan" dispatch since the 2026-07-13 redesign, but `ScmCron.MRScan` and `ProjectStatus.LastMRScan` still round-tripped on the CRD, so both live Projects carried a `spec.scm.cron.mrScan` block that silently did nothing. Deleted both fields + the two unreachable switch arms, regenerated CRD/deepcopy, added `TestProjectCR_StaleMRScanBlockIsPrunedNotRejected` (envtest, proves structural-schema pruning drops the stale field with no error - no coordinated cutover needed with tatara-helmfile's matching values removal). Two adjacent findings while auditing comments naming mrScan: **`PRReactionScope` (project_types.go) has a live consumer** (`sweep.go:1173` `prInReactionScope`, gates the B.4 sweep's PR review path) - comment fixed to name it, field kept. **`ProjectStatus.ScanMarks`/`ScanMark` have ZERO consumers anywhere** (only the type declarations + generated deepcopy reference them) - the whole per-item high-water-mark mechanism from issue #285 appears to have been dropped in the same 2026-07-13 redesign without the field being removed. Left alone (out of this task's scope) and flagged in ROADMAP.md; the two now-stale #285 roadmap items that referenced mrScan directly were marked abandoned.

2026-07-17 (fix/review-outcome-claim-lease-and-handoff-guard) **All six `kind=review` Tasks of 2026-07-16 died despite their agents finishing** (3 `failed[pod-recreation-exhausted]` at podRuns=5, 2 `parked[no-outcome]` at podRuns=4 after re-reviewing the SAME already-merged PR four times, 1 `parked[review-post-refused]` correctly) and `mr-tatara-agent-skills-20` was stamped approved+reviewedSHA while its Task `cgthv` ended failed - two defects, neither touched by v1.0.1..v1.3.0. **DEFECT A - the claim outlived a failed commit.** `claimOutcomeFingerprint` stamps the fingerprint BEFORE kind-specific validation; every `review()` early-return responded 4xx without committing but LEFT the claim, so identical retries matched on fingerprint alone and replayed 200 OK forever. **The claim-first ordering is NOT the bug and was NOT moved** - it is the C7 fix (2026-07-13 entry above): the `/outcome` handler runs on all 3 replicas, so a stamped-only-at-commit fingerprint admits two concurrent identical POSTs to the same forge write / child-mint / ReviewRounds increment. Research initially argued "claim after validation"; reading the code proved that wrong - Stripe does not validate-then-claim either, it claims WITH A LOCK and unlocks on failure. `outcome_concurrency_test.go`'s C7 tripwire test MUST FAIL if anyone ever moves the claim after validation; that is deliberate, do not "fix" it. Fix: the claim is now a three-state lease keyed on the condition's `Reason`, which already distinguished claimed (`"Outcome"`) from committed (the kind's own reason, e.g. `"Review"`) - nothing read it before. committed -> 200 replay; bare claim younger than `OutcomeClaimTTL` -> 409; older -> re-claim; plus an ownership-checked release on class-B (pre-execution) rejections. **TRAP - the lease-steal window:** a handler that outlives its own lease gets it stolen and double-files; `OutcomeHandlerBudget` (3m) < `OutcomeClaimTTL` (5m) is the load-bearing invariant that makes this impossible, and it is test-pinned. 3m was chosen because the brainstorm validator permits 5 proposals x ~30s per CreateIssue = 150s worst case - **do not raise the budget past the TTL to fix slow brainstorms**, parallelize the calls or tighten the per-call scm timeout instead. **TRAP:** `r = r.WithContext(ctx)` is load-bearing - every kind handler and commit pull `o.r.Context()` for themselves, so bounding only the local `ctx` bounds NOTHING. **TRAP - class B vs class A:** Stripe caches post-execution business 4xx under the idempotency key but NOT pre-execution rejections (param validation, auth, rate limiting), because those never reach the committed path; every `review()` rejection here is class B, and caching them under the fingerprint (the pre-fix behaviour) is the Stripe ANTI-pattern. **TRAP - `refine`'s `foldMembers` is the point of no return** (STEP 4 DELETES member Tasks): its links-shape check was rejecting AFTER the deletes, so once a rejection released the claim, the retry re-validated immediately, could not find the deleted members, and 500'd forever - `refine` could never complete. The check is hoisted into the read-only block; every shape check must stay above `foldMembers`. **ArgoCD is the anti-pattern twin**: `Application.status.operationState` is an in-CR lock not atomically paired with a guaranteed terminal write - a crash wedges it in `Running` forever, needing `argocd app terminate-op`. That is exactly the shape avoided here. **DEFECT B - the pod caps were blind to an in-flight advance.** `kind=review` is the ONLY outcome kind whose commit does not call `stage.Enter`; the advance is deferred to `MergeRequestReconciler` -> `DrainPendingReview` -> `advanceAfterReview`. **That split is DELIBERATE and was NOT removed**: phase 1 is pure etcd with no forge write, so a forge outage cannot lose an accepted outcome. But `BudgetExit`/`ArmedClock`/`reconcileCaps` read only pod liveness + `Stats.PodRecreations`, so a completed Task kept getting respawned until a cap killed it. Fix: `handoffCondition()` is the ONE predicate all three sites route through (`reconcileClocks`' deadline + the two B2 guards). **TRAP - it MUST be occupancy-scoped**, and this nearly shipped as a much worse bug: (1) it must key on `OutcomeCommittedFor(t, agentKind)` - the CURRENT stage's own kind - never bare `OutcomeCommitted(t)`, because `OutcomeAccepted` is a per-Task condition that survives across stages, so an `implement` Task's commit (`Reason="Implement"`) is already committed the instant it reaches `reviewing`; a bare predicate would suppress its not-yet-spawned review pod and WEDGE EVERY IMPLEMENT TASK. (2) it must also reject a commit from a PREVIOUS occupancy of the same stage: `stage.Enter` NEVER clears `Status.Conditions` and `release` only removes bare claims, so a committed `Reason="Review"` is PERMANENT for the Task's life - `merging->reviewing` (HeadMoved, cycle 4) and the `kind=review` awaiting-human unpark both re-enter `reviewing` carrying it, and without a `cond.LastTransitionTime >= StageEnteredAt` check the first reconcile would silently park them at `handoff-stalled` before any pod spawned (legal edge, no F.6 re-entry, both cycles die permanently). The full green test suite did not catch this - nothing exercised a reconcile after a re-entry. **BOUND:** the guard suppresses ONLY the pod-liveness caps (no-outcome, pod-recreation-exhausted); clock 3 stays armed and `HandoffDeadline` (5m) parks at `parked[handoff-stalled]` - a suppressed Task holds its admitted concurrency ticket for the drain window, so at `maxConcurrentAgents=5` five stalled drains would block ALL admission; 5m is what makes that survivable rather than 4h. **ACCEPTED:** the turn budget stays armed even on a committed outcome (only reachable if turns >= max AT commit time - same shape as the bug being fixed, far lower probability). **NOT A BUG, do not "fix":** `podRuns` is a lifetime counter never reset; `podRecreations` resets on every `stage.Enter`. podRuns=5 => 4 recreations => 4>3 => failed; podRuns=4 => 3>=3 => parked[no-outcome]. **ADJACENT:** `illegal stage transition triaging -> triaging` (`refine-qe-lh79w` 06:00:04Z, `brainstorm-qe-5snrr` 06:24:30Z) was a stale-cache mint - `task_controller.go` decided on a CACHED `status.stage == ""` while `FitTask` re-read live and ran `stage.Enter` there. Fixed with an `APIReader` live read at the mint (`MaxConcurrentReconciles=1` + leader election means one extra GET per Task closes it completely). A self-edge in the `Transitions` table was REJECTED: it weakens the choke point for every caller, and `stage.Enter`'s side effects are not idempotent even when the stage is unchanged (re-stamps `StageEnteredAt`, nils `PodStartedAt`/`StageWorkStartedAt`, zeroes `PodRecreations`).

2026-07-17 (fix/review-outcome-claim-lease-and-handoff-guard, final fix pass) **Three of this branch's own new tests proved nothing; a full-green suite lied.** Each was found by MUTATION TESTING (stub the fix, re-run, see it still pass) and each is now pinned by a test proven to discriminate. (1) `TestReconcileStage_MintIsIdempotentAgainstAStaleCache` was SELF-FULFILLING: it built a stale `cached` client and a live `apiReader` and set `Client: cached`, but the illegal-transition counter fires from the in-write `stage.Enter` inside `objbudget.FitTask`, which re-Gets through `r.Client` - so the stale client made the in-write Enter see `stage==""`, take the LEGAL Create edge, and `triaging -> triaging` could never happen in its own fixture. The `apiReader` was read by nothing but the code under test. Fixed to production's real shape: ONE client holding the LIVE minted Task as both `Client` and `APIReader`, with a SEPARATE stale in-memory `*Task` passed as the `task` arg (that IS a stale informer cache handing the reconciler a stale object). (2) The caps guard's `edge.Reason` scoping was unpinned - widening it to a bare `handoffCondition(task) != nil` kept the whole controller suite green, silently handing a runaway agent an unbounded turn budget. `TestTurnBudgetExhausted` uses an *implementing* Task with no outcome condition, so it never enters the guard. Now pinned by `TestReconcile_CapsSuppressionDoesNotCoverTheTurnBudget` (kind=review, committed Review outcome at stageEnteredAt, live Ready pod so no-outcome cannot fire, turns >= max -> must still fail turn-budget-exhausted). (3) `handoffCondition`'s fail-closed on nil `StageEnteredAt` was unpinned - inverting it to fail OPEN kept the suite green; no test built a committed-outcome Task with no stage stamp. Now pinned by `TestHandoffCondition_FailsClosedWithNoStageStamp`. **TRAP - the re-claim's `LastTransitionTime` refresh rests on an accident:** the orphan re-claim refreshes the lease clock ONLY because `setCondition` is a WHOLE-STRUCT overwrite. `meta.SetStatusCondition` would NOT refresh it (Status goes True->True, and it only re-stamps on a Status CHANGE), minting a lease born already expired - the next retry 1s later reads it as orphaned, re-claims, and duplicates every side effect, **reachable on a single-version single-pod cluster with no race at all**. The existing "past the TTL" test asserted only 200 + stage + `Reason=="Clarify"`, all of which `commit()` overwrites, so the claim's own timestamp went unobserved. Pinned by `TestOutcome_ReclaimOfAnOrphanedStubRefreshesTheLeaseClock`, which parks a handler inside `CreateIssue` (the existing `blockingCreateIssueForge`) to read the condition in the window between re-claim and commit; `setCondition` now carries a DO-NOT-tidy-into-`meta.SetStatusCondition` warning. Also pinned `release()` on the unknown-kind `default:` arm (reachable: `status.agentKind` is an unvalidated plain string and the gate only checks `env.Kind == task.Status.AgentKind`, so a bogus agentKind sails through on a matching bogus kind). Deleted three VACUOUS tests that asserted constants against themselves (`TestOutcomeClaimTTLAndHandoffDeadline`, `TestOutcomeReasonFor`'s `"" -> OutcomeReasonClaimed` entry, `TestHandoffStalledIsInTheF5ClosedSet`'s literal restatement); KEPT `TestOutcomeHandlerBudgetIsUnderTheClaimTTL`, which pins a real invariant. **Rationale inconsistency resolved:** this branch deleted `mrScan` on the grounds that pruning makes removal safe, while `healthCheck` was kept "inert for stored-CR back-compat" - one had to be wrong. The mrScan rationale is the correct one (`TestProjectCR_StaleMRScanBlockIsPrunedNotRejected` proves pruning drops a stale block silently), so healthCheck's back-compat claim is false; it survives only as scope. Comments corrected at all four sites, deletion queued in ROADMAP.md. `deploy-samples`' stale `mrScan` blocks removed; `issueScan.maxPerCycle` (not a `CronActivity` field at all) is PRE-EXISTING rot, left alone and noted in ROADMAP.md.

2026-07-18 (fix-stream H, the `operator_unpark_declined_total` burst, #368) 29,756 declines over ~4h, peak 3.14/s, wildly disproportionate to the handful of active tasks. Root cause was NOT one stuck task: `project.Status.Memory.Phase` was pinned at `Provisioning` for the whole window, which forces `reconcileMemory` to return `RequeueAfter=10s` EVERY pass (`project_memory.go:480-483`) - and that floor drives `Reconcile()`'s ENTIRE `ctrl.Result`, not just the memory subsystem. Loki shows Project reconciling even faster than that 10s timer within some windows (three `reconciled project` lines in 0.6s) - filed separately as #367 (suspect: `applyMemoryStack` re-patching `.Owns()`-watched objects every Provisioning pass, re-triggering through the watch on top of the timer; not fixed here, deliberately out of scope). `driveUnparks` had NO pacing of its own: it re-swept the FULL parked-Task backlog (58 system-wide at burst time, most days old - "in-flight" active-task counts are a different, much smaller number) on every single pass, whatever cadence that happened to be, and `kind="rule"` (normal steady-state non-eligible re-entry, per the metric's own doc comment) accounted for ~100% of the volume. **Confirmed NOT a gap: `operator_unpark_declined_total` already carries both `stageReason` and `kind` labels** (added #352/3d35a17, predates this investigation) - the original hypothesis that the metric lacked a reason label was wrong; dropped from scope once verified live against Prometheus. Fix: `driveUnparksPaced` (`unpark.go`) floors `driveUnparks` to `UnparkDriveInterval` (30s constant, `defaultUnparkDriveInterval`), **keyed per-project via `lastDriveUnparks map[string]time.Time`** - deliberately NOT a single scalar clock like `lastGaugeRecompute`, because gauge recompute really is cluster-wide by design (see its own doc comment) while `driveUnparks` is per-Project; a scalar here would have made two live Projects throttle each other. The residual wait folds into `soonestRequeue` so a genuinely-eligible F.6 re-entry is never starved past the floor once nothing else forces frequent reconciles. `driveCommentUnpark` (webhook comment-driven F.6 promptness path) is untouched - different call site, no pacing needed there by design.

2026-07-17 (issue #324, the residue after #347's mint fix - `refining -> refining`) The #347 mint fix closed the CACHED `status.stage == ""` race one edge too early: `reconcileTriaging` fires on a CACHED `status.stage == triaging`, computes `next` from `triageTarget(spec.kind)` (deterministic on Spec, so every reconcile of a stale-cached Task recomputes the SAME target), and calls `r.enter(next)`. `objbudget.FitTask`'s in-write `Get` re-reads through the SAME cached `r.Client` but later in the SAME reconcile - `mintIssueCRs`'s own I/O is enough wall-clock time for the informer to have caught up on our OWN prior reconcile's `triaging -> refining` write - so it sees the Task already at `refining` and refuses `refining -> refining`. Audited every `r.enter` caller for the same shape (cached-derived target, no live check): `reconcileClocks` (both the handoff-stalled Parked exit and the budget-elapsed exit) and `reconcileCaps` (turn/pod-recreation/no-outcome exits) share it identically - each does its own I/O (`ownedMergeRequests`, `podGone`) before `enter`, and each recomputes its edge from a `task` struct that is never re-Get'd, so a stale cached copy yields the SAME edge.To on repeat, genuinely reachable the same way, just rarer than triaging (which fires on every single new Task). Fixed ONCE, generally: new `refreshTaskFromAPI` (task_controller.go, APIReader live Get, nil-safe for unit tests) called in `reconcileStage` right after the terminal check and before `reconcileClocks`/`reconcileCaps`/the stage switch, so every one of those branches is covered by a single choke point instead of three bespoke ones. Rejected AGAIN (twice now): a self-edge in the `Transitions` table - `stage.Enter` re-stamps `StageEnteredAt` and zeroes `PodStartedAt`/`StageWorkStartedAt`/`PodRecreations` even when from==to, so a self-edge would silently reset a running Task's clocks and crash budget. TDD caught its own mint precedent's known failure mode: the new `TestReconcileStage_TriagingIsIdempotentAgainstAStaleCache` was written to production's real shape (ONE client backing both `Client`/`APIReader` holding the LIVE `refining` Task, a SEPARATE stale in-memory `triaging` struct as the `task` arg) FIRST, proven to fail with the exact production error string when the guard is stubbed out, then proven to pass once restored.

2026-07-18 (issue #355, memory-provisioning stream D - bounded Degraded timeout + rollout convergence + pre-SubmitTurn gate) Live incident: `mem-tatara-lightrag` sat Running-but-never-Ready ~7h+, `status.memory.phase` stuck `Provisioning` indefinitely (no bound existed at all - `memoryPhase` only ever returns "Ready"/"Provisioning"), old+new API pods coexisted (no rollout-convergence check in `memoryStackHealth` - `AvailableReplicas` alone can't distinguish a converged rollout from a stale-generation pod still Available), LightRAG call error ratio hit 72-84%. Consistent with issue #327 (closed, different root cause - node-isolation SPOF, no anti-affinity; tracked separately as #365, out of this stream's scope). Three fixes, all operator-repo-only: **(a) bounded timeout -> Degraded.** New `Project.Status.Memory.ProvisioningSince` (mirrors `ReadySince`'s edge-set/clear shape but in the opposite direction: set on any Ready/Failed/""->Provisioning edge, PRESERVED across a Provisioning<->Degraded episode so the clock does not reset every 10s poll, cleared on reaching Ready). New chart-configurable `memoryProvisioningTimeoutMinutes` (default 45m, `MEMORY_PROVISIONING_TIMEOUT_MINUTES` env, same clamp-floor/zero-disables shape as `idlePodReapMinutes`/`IDLE_POD_REAP_MINUTES`). `reconcileMemory` flips phase to `"Degraded"` (NOT `"Failed"` - Failed stays reserved for hard apply/password errors) once `now - ProvisioningSince >= timeout`, with `MemoryReady=False/reason=ProvisioningTimeout`.
