New `TataraMemoryStackDegraded` alert (charts/tatara-operator/templates/prometheusrule.yaml, sibling of the existing `TataraMemoryStackFailed`, `for: 5m`) - deliberately NOT in internal/memory/monitoring.go's per-project rule, because `operator_memory_stacks` is the OPERATOR's own cluster-wide gauge (scraped via the operator's chart ServiceMonitor), not a per-project tatara-memory-scraped series; a per-project PrometheusRule would emit one identical duplicate alert per project. **(b) rollout convergence.** `deploymentRolloutConverged` (project_memory.go) gates `lightragAvail`/`memoryAvail` on `ObservedGeneration==Generation && UpdatedReplicas==Replicas==AvailableReplicas`, not `AvailableReplicas` alone - closes the exact old+new-pod-coexisting gap the incident showed. **(c) pre-SubmitTurn memory gate.** The existing admission gate (task_controller.go, `task.Status.PodStartedAt == nil && !memoryStablyReady`) only fires ONCE per pod-lifecycle, before ensureStagePod; it does NOT re-check between a pod becoming Ready (PodWatchReconciler stamps `PodStartedAt`/arms CLOCK 3) and the actual `SubmitTurn` call in `reconcilePodStage`, a gap spanning scheduling+image-pull+the G.10 handshake during which memory can flip unhealthy. New re-check immediately before `SubmitTurn` (same `memoryStablyReady`/`InfraIncidentExempt` semantics, `memGateRequeue` cadence) closes it for every turn0 path uniformly (first pod, `respawnLostPod`, `ttlStop` rotation - all funnel through the one `SubmitTurn` call site). Held-turn surfacing mirrors the existing WS3-I5 `enqueueDeployTimeoutComment` pattern exactly: ONE operator comment per owned open issue on first hold, deduped via new `Issue.Status.LastMemoryGateCommentAt` (DISTINCT marker from `LastDeployTimeoutCommentAt`/`LastRefireCommentAt`, same one-shot shape). New `operator_memory_gate_hold_total{project}` counter (sibling of the existing `operator_memory_gate_bypass_total`). **TRAP found while fixing:** `tsProject` (task_stage_test.go, ~40 callers) deliberately carries `Phase=Ready` with NO `ReadySince`, so `memoryStablyReady` reads false and the OLD admission gate accidentally protects every `PodStartedAt==nil` fixture from ever reaching `ensureStagePod`'s `ValidatePodSecretRefs` (none of these fixtures wire `AnthropicSecretName`). Backdating `ReadySince` in `tsProject` itself (the first attempt) broke `TestSteadyStateQueuedTaskDoesNotTerminate`/`TestReconcilerAppliesTheThreeClocks` by removing that incidental protection. Fixed with a SEPARATE `tsStablyReadyProject` opt-in used only by the two tests that actually need `SubmitTurn` to fire. Also: `deploymentRolloutConverged`'s stricter gate broke `fakeStackUnhealthy` (memory_debounce_test.go's `TestReadySince_TransitionEdges`) because it zeroed `Replicas` but left a stale `UpdatedReplicas=1` from a prior `fakeStackHealthy` call - envtest's k8s 1.33 API server validates `status.updatedReplicas <= status.replicas` on Deployment status subresource writes; fixed by also zeroing `UpdatedReplicas` in the test helper. Anti-affinity/topologySpreadConstraints (issue #327's other recommendation) tracked separately as #365, filed but not implemented here.

2026-07-17 (issue #324, fix pass on the above) The guard ADOPTS the live object (`*task = live`) instead of bailing, and the four decisions behind that are the ones worth keeping. (1) **ADOPTION, not a requeue.** The first cut paid for a live GET, DISCARDED it, and returned `RequeueAfter: 1s` so the NEXT reconcile could redo the work from a cache it merely hoped had caught up. Adoption is strictly better: the live object is FRESHER than the cache the requeue was waiting for, so there is nothing left to wait for. It also removes a real LIVELOCK - a wedged watch or a dropped event drifts EVERY reconcile, and the bail turned that into a 1s requeue reporting `ReconcileResult("Task","success")` forever with zero progress and nothing firing (the default 10h `SyncPeriod` is nowhere near close enough to rescue it). What makes adoption safe is that nothing downstream needs the cached object: `EnterStage`/`FitTask` re-Get and re-mutate under `RetryOnConflict` anyway. **`StageTerminal` is re-checked on the FRESH object** - a Task that went terminal between the cached and live reads must take the reaper's early return, not fall through into clocks/caps. `mintedAlready` still BAILS and that asymmetry is deliberate: there is no live object to adopt AS at the mint, the whole question there is whether our own Create edge landed. NotFound is deliberately NOT a bail either (proceed; the reaper owns it, or the enter surfaces a real NotFound). (2) **COST, accepted knowingly:** one live GET - an etcd QUORUM read via `mgr.GetAPIReader()` - on EVERY non-terminal reconcile. `delivered`/`approved`/`merging`/`deploying` pay it while entering nothing from this reconciler; `delivered` alone requeues at 30s for 48h, ~5760 quorum reads per Task. Narrowing the guard to just the entering stages was CONSIDERED AND REJECTED for now: a single choke point that is obviously right beats three call-site checks that drift apart, and the whole reason this branch exists is that the last narrow fix (#347, mint-only) left a residue one edge later. Only ever narrow it with the pod-stage test below in place. (3) **The window is NARROWED, not CLOSED** - the pre-fix comment claiming a live read "closes the window completely" was FALSE generalized and is corrected. It is true only for the MINT, whose sole writer is this reconciler. `status.stage` has other writers, none serialised against this one: the `/outcome` REST handler (runs on ALL 3 replicas, not just the leader), `queue_controller`'s `admitTicket` (a DIFFERENT controller - `MaxConcurrentReconciles: 1` is PER-CONTROLLER, so it runs concurrently), and `StageDriver`. A write from any of them between the live GET and `objbudget`'s in-write Get reopens it; that residue is what transition.go's post-write `IllegalStageTransition` emit catches. (4) **New `operator_stage_drift_total{stage}`** (obs/stage_metrics.go, labelled by the CACHED/stale stage, next to `IllegalStageTransitionTotal` as its early-warning sibling) plus an INFO log with `cached_stage`/`live_stage`: adoption is self-healing, and self-healing silently is how a wedged watch stays invisible. A trickle is normal informer lag; a sustained rate on one stage is a wedge. **THE TEST THAT MATTERS is the POD-STAGE one**, and the widening was entirely unpinned without it: both triaging tests use a Task with no `StageEnteredAt`, so `ArmedClock` returns `ClockNone` (stage.go:572) and `BudgetExit` returns nothing for a podless stage - between them they execute ZERO lines of clocks/caps edge derivation, and anyone narrowing the guard back into `reconcileTriaging` keeps the suite green while clocks/caps drift reopens, surfacing only as `{from="failed",to="failed"}` in prod. `TestReconcileStage_PodStageCapsAreIdempotentAgainstAStaleCache` (implementing, all three stamps set, `PodRecreations` over budget, no Pod so `podGone`, live copy already `failed`) is mutation-proven: stubbing the guard fails it with `illegal stage transition failed -> failed`.

2026-07-18 (fix/mr-mirror-selfheal, issues #380/#381) **Review Task permanently orphaned from its MergeRequest mirror when a mint is interrupted.** Live: review Task for PR #373 finished but submit_outcome 400'd `this task owns no open MR` on every retry; scm_read(kind=mr) listed #361-378 but not #373/374/376. The MR CR EXISTED but as an unbound STUB - spec present, status carried only `headSHA` (a webhook stampMRHead from a later push) + a misleading MirrorSynced condition (hourly cadence thread-sync), NO state/body/headBranch/author, NO controller owner; the Task carried no mrRefs. Root cause: `MintReviewTask` (intake.go) mints in three non-atomic etcd steps - createTaskRaceSafe (Task create), bindMRToTask (SyncMergeRequest full-populate + ownMergeRequest), stampMintStatus (mrRefs). A restart between step 1 and completing step 2 (the v1.8.1->v1.8.2 rollout this afternoon) left the Task created but the MR a bare stub. Every later attempt (hourly sweep PRReview path AND webhook re-mint) hit `createTaskRaceSafe` returning created=false and returned early WITHOUT re-binding; the MergeRequestReconciler cadence only re-syncs the comment thread (syncMergeRequestThread), never re-runs full SyncMergeRequest, so the stub's state/ownership were never repaired - permanent. The 400's proximate cause is `ownedMRs` (handlers_v2.go) filtering by controller-owner==task.Name (empty -> no-open-mr); scm_read hiding #373 is handlers_v2.go filtering `state != open` (stub state empty). Fix: made the created=false backstop SELF-HEALING - createTaskRaceSafe now returns the live twin, and MintReviewTask/MintIssueTask run `repairMRBinding`/`repairIssueBinding` against it when the artifact is an unbound stub (or absent). Repair NEVER steals: a CR already controller-owned (by the twin - idempotent - or, defensively, anyone) is left untouched, so it is safe on every hourly pass and race-safe (ownMergeRequest's RetryOnConflict + never-steal is the real arbiter; the Get is a cheap skip). ClassifyPR already routes an UNOWNED stub to PRReview, so live stubs #373/374/376 self-repair within one sweep cycle (<=1h) after deploy, no manual mutation. **Adjacent, filed NOT fixed (#381):** `report_internal_issue` is a stdout-only no-op (turncallback.go re-logs and returns 204, no CR) - agents believe they file platform reports that reach no durable sink; the #373 review agent's tool_error report left no trace but its own handoff Task notes. semver: patch (bugfix, no API/CRD change).
2026-07-18 (fix/metric-wiring-audit, issue #370: post-redesign dead-metric audit) Live Prometheus (Grafana MCP, 7-day history across pod generations) proved several I1/K.1 metrics were NOT dead-code residue despite reading zero in the raw 48h evidence that opened this stream - they were correctly wired and had fired in PRIOR pod generations (`operator_review_outcome_total`, `operator_review_post_total`, `operator_open_proposals`); the flat-zero window was pod-restart-recency + genuinely low event frequency, not a bug. Do not "fix" a live-zero metric without checking longer history first. Real findings: (1) **`operator_task_parked_total` undercounted, root cause found:** `internal/restapi/outcome.go`'s own `stage.Enter(...StageParked...)` sites (awaiting-human, identity-unverified, ...) bypass `transition.go`'s `EnterStage` - the only other caller of `TaskParked()` - the same choke-point gap D1 already closed for `operator_task_terminal_total` via `commit()`'s `TaskTerminalEntry` call, never extended to `TaskParked`. Fixed by adding the identical `if to == StageParked && from != ""` check to `commit()`. (2) **`operator_sweep_errors_total` and `operator_stage_drift_total`** were CounterVecs with zero pre-warm (no `seedLabels`, unlike every other closed-set CounterVec in this codebase) - a healthy zero-error steady state produced literally no series, not a zero baseline. Pre-seeded both. (3) **`tatara_scan_items_total`/`tatara_scan_tasks_created_total`/`tatara_scan_duration_seconds` pruned** (dead-per-redesign, tatara-observability already treats them as such) - but the operator's OWN chart (`templates/prometheusrule.yaml`'s `TataraLoopStalled` deadman + `dashboards/tatara-loop.json`) still queried two of them; pruning them without fixing the chart would have made `TataraLoopStalled`'s PromQL `and` against a nonexistent metric evaluate to an empty vector FOREVER (the alert would never fire again, silently). Repointed the alert onto its own already-documented primary term (`operator_tasks_minted_per_sweep_count`) and the dashboard panel onto `operator_tasks_minted_per_sweep_sum`/`operator_sweep_mint_cap_hit_total`; added `obs.SweepLastSuccessTimestamp{activity=brainstorm|documentation|issueScan}` (new label values on the EXISTING sweep heartbeat gauge, set from `stampScan` on success) as the successor signal for a stalled scan cron, but deliberately did NOT fold it into `TataraLoopStalled`'s expression - opt-in-disabled activities (brainstorm/documentation) would need `absent_over_time`-aware gating to avoid false-firing on a project that never enabled them, which is real alerting design, not a mechanical repoint; a dedicated per-activity alert is a ROADMAP follow-up. `Makefile`'s `chart-lint` metric-presence allowlist updated to match (had the OLD dead names hardcoded, which would have masked exactly this class of break). (4) **Real unreported hygiene bug found while auditing item 6 (stage-age gauge staleness):** the stage/stage-age gauges self-heal fine (Reset+recompute every 60s, verified sound, not a bug) - but `DeleteTaskSeries` (`operator_task_tokens_total`/`operator_task_turns_total` per-issue counters) had ZERO production callers, only a unit test. Wired into `deleteReapedTask` (reaper.go); switched its matching from exact `DeleteLabelValues(...,model,type)` to `DeletePartialMatch(project,repo,kind,issue)` so a Task whose `Status.ResolvedModel` changed mid-life (respawn/stage change) gets ALL its model-labelled series cleared, not just the final model's. (5) `operator_orphan_adopted_total` confirmed a legitimate zero (both webhook- and sweep-driven mint counts were 0 in the same 7-day window - the backlog is fully covered by webhook-primary reactivity, not silently dropped). Companion tatara-observability PR (allowlist entries for `operator_review_post_total`/`operator_stage_drift_total`) tracked separately per stream E's concurrent allowlist rewrite there.

  the illegal-transition infinite-requeue crash-loop the un-gated version hit.
- 2026-07-19 (#398): `incidentDedupKey` dropped its CommonLabels hashing
  entirely - key is now sha256(project + rule name) only, no denylist. Root
  cause: Grafana's CommonLabels is the intersection of whatever instances
  co-fire in one evaluation, so the member set (and therefore the label
  intersection) churns run to run even though the rule itself hasn't
  changed; the #320/#328 "stable labels" denylist still let that churn
  change the key and bypass the open tracker, re-spawning full
  investigations 4x ~35min apart on one rule. Trade-off accepted: same rule
  + different co-firing workload now collapses onto ONE tracker (a coarser
  key than #320/#328's), so workload distinction is no longer in the dedup
  key - it now rests on the refire comment (`labelSummary`, full
  CommonLabels, replaces the old volatile-stripped `stableLabelSummary`),
  the escalation valve (refire threshold 10 / stale age 48h re-admits a
  fresh investigation), and cross-rule group linking (`incidentGroupKey`,
  untouched, still project+correlation-labels). Removed as dead:
  `defaultVolatileDenylist`/`denylistSet` (grafana.go),
  `Server.dedupDenylist` (server.go), `Config.IncidentDedupVolatileLabels` +
  `INCIDENT_DEDUP_VOLATILE_LABELS` (config.go + webhook.Config +
  cmd/manager/wire.go wiring). `correlationSet`/`incidentGroupKey` (the
  separate GROUP key) are untouched.
